Salah — Prayer
beginner
6 min
Cutting Sunnah Prayer When Obligatory Congregation Begins
Ruling on cutting sunnah prayer when khatib appears or iqamah is called

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended action when the khatib appears during the sunnah of Jumu'ah or when iqamah is called during the sunnah of Zuhr, and apply the principle of shaf' to similar situations.

Core Idea
When the obligatory congregation begins, complete the current pair (shaf') and make up the rest after fard.

This lesson addresses a common situation: you are in the middle of a four-rak'ah sunnah prayer, and the fard congregation is about to start. The Hanafi school provides a clear guideline to balance completing your sunnah and not missing the fard. Understanding the concept of shaf' helps you act appropriately.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Determine whether you are praying the four-rak'ah sunnah before Jumu'ah and the khatib emerges, or the four-rak'ah sunnah before Zuhr and the iqamah is called.
These are the two specific cases covered in this ruling.
2
Recognize the shaf' structure
Understand that the four-rak'ah sunnah is composed of two independent pairs (shaf') of two rak'ahs each. Each shaf' is a complete unit that can be terminated with salam.
The text states 'har do rakat ek shaf' hai' (every two rak'ahs is a pair).
3
Apply the ruling
Upon the occurrence of the trigger (khatib appears or iqamah called), say salam after completing the current pair of rak'ahs. If you are in the middle of a rak'ah, complete it to finish the pair.
Do not break in the middle of a rak'ah; always complete the pair.
4
Plan the make-up
After performing the fard prayer, pray the remaining two rak'ahs of the sunnah that you had intended. This ensures the sunnah is not abandoned entirely.
The text says 'farz ke baad sunnat ki qaza kar le' (make up the sunnah after the fard).
5
Understand the wisdom
This ruling avoids two harms: breaking the prayer prematurely (which is disliked) and missing the fard congregation. It preserves the sunnah without conflict.
The commentary emphasizes 'ta ke namaz ko torna bhi lazim na aae aur jamaat mein bhi shirkat ho jae'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۷۱۸) اور اگر جمعہ کی سنت پڑھتا ہو اور خطیب نکلے یا ظہر کی سنت میں اقامت کہی جاوے تو دو رکعت پر سلام پھیر دے، پھر فرض کے بعد سنت کی قضا کر لے۔ اچھی بات یہی ہے۔ تشریح : جمعہ کی سنت چار رکعت ہے، اور ظہر کی سنت بھی چار رکعت ہے اور ان دونوں سنتوں کی ایک اہمیت ہے، البتہ ان میں ہر دورکعت ایک شفع ہے، اس لئے جمعہ کی سنت پڑھ رہا ہو اور خطیب خطبہ کے لئے نکل گیا تو اس وقت سنت پڑھنا اچھا نہیں ہے اس لئے ایک شفع یعنی دو رکعت پر سلام پھیر دے اور یہ سنت بعد میں پڑھے، یہی حال ظہر کی سنت کا ہے کہ سنت پڑھ رہا تھا اور فرض کی اقامت ہوگئی تو دو رکعت پر سلام پھیر دے اور جماعت کے ساتھ شریک ہو جائے ۔ تا کہ نماز کو توڑنا بھی لازم نہ آئے اور جماعت میں بھی شرکت ہو جائے۔
Translation: (718) And if he is praying the sunnah of Jumu'ah and the khatib comes out, or the iqamah is called while he is in the sunnah of Zuhr, then he should say salam at the end of two rak'ahs, and then make up the sunnah after the fard. This is the best view. Explanation: The sunnah of Jumu'ah is four rak'ahs, and the sunnah of Zuhr is also four rak'ahs, and both have importance. However, every two rak'ahs form a shaf' (pair). So if he is praying the sunnah of Jumu'ah and the khatib comes out for the sermon, it is not good to continue the sunnah at that time. Therefore, he should say salam after one shaf' (i.e., two rak'ahs) and pray this sunnah later. The same applies to the sunnah of Zuhr: if he is praying it and the iqamah for the fard is called, he should say salam after two rak'ahs and join the congregation, so that neither does he have to break the prayer nor does he miss the congregation.
Source pages p. 28

Commentary
This lesson covers the rulings for two specific situations: (1) When a person is performing the four-rak'ah sunnah before Jumu'ah and the khatib emerges to deliver the khutbah, and (2) When performing the four-rak'ah sunnah before Zuhr and the iqamah is called for the fard. In both cases, the recommended course of action (al-awjah) is to terminate the sunnah after completing two rak'ahs, because each two rak'ahs constitute a complete unit (shaf'). This allows the person to attend the fard congregation without completely abandoning the sunnah. The remaining two rak'ahs of the sunnah should be performed after the fard prayer. The reasoning is to avoid an interruption that would require breaking the prayer mid-rak'ah, and to ensure participation in the obligatory congregation which has a higher priority.

Key Terms
سنّة (sunnah): Recommended supererogatory prayer (as distinct from fard).
شفع (shaf'): A pair; in prayer, a set of two rak'ahs.
اوجه (awjah): The most appropriate or preferred opinion.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person is praying the four-rak'ah sunnah before Jumu'ah and the khatib comes out, what should he do?
A) Complete all four rak'ahs before joining.
B) Say salam after two rak'ahs and make up the rest after Jumu'ah.
C) Break the prayer immediately without salam.
D) Continue praying until the fard starts.

Key Takeaway
When the fard congregation begins during a four-rak'ah sunnah, complete the current pair (shaf') and say salam, then make up the rest after fard.

Joining Imam in Fard and Avoiding Sunnah During Iqamah
Ruling on joining congregational fard and not starting sunnah when iqamah is called

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a person enters the mosque during iqamah or when the imam is already in fard prayer, and explain the three proofs (two hadiths and one rational proof) supporting that ruling.

Core Idea
When iqamah is called, join the imam immediately; no supererogatory prayer is permitted except the obligatory one.

This lesson addresses a common scenario in congregational prayer: what should a person do if he enters the mosque when the iqamah is being called or finds the imam already leading the fard? The Hanafi school rules that he must join the congregation immediately and not occupy himself with any sunnah prayer, even the regular sunnah associated with that fard. The text provides two hadiths and a rational proof to support this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is entering the mosque when iqamah is called or imam is in fard. Ruling: wajib to join congregation, prohibited to start sunnah.
Prohibition here means makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked) according to Hanafi fiqh.
2
Locate the primary hadith
The hadith 'When iqamah is said, there is no prayer except the obligatory one' (Muslim, Tirmidhi) is the main textual proof.
This is a general prohibition (amm) covering all supererogatory prayers.
3
Analyze the second hadith
The Prophet (peace be upon him) rebuked a man praying during iqamah for Fajr, asking if he was praying four rak'ahs, which indicates the prohibition of sunnah at that time.
This hadith specifically targets the Fajr sunnah, showing even the emphasized sunnah is not permitted.
4
Understand the rational proof
Joining the congregation is wajib (obligatory), while performing sunnah is sunnah (recommended). The wajib takes precedence over the sunnah.
This is a qiyas based on the hierarchy of legal categories.
5
Apply the ruling
In practice, one must immediately enter the prayer line and make the intention to follow the imam, leaving any sunnah for later (if possible) or omitting it entirely.
The Fajr sunnah has a special exception (to be covered in a later lesson) but generally this ruling applies to all fard prayers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمہ: (۷۱۹) اور جو ایسے وقت میں آئے کہ امام فرض نماز میں ہو تو امام کے ساتھ اقتدا کرے اور سنت پڑھنے میں مشغول نہ ہو وجه : (۱) جماعت کھڑی ہوگئی ہو تو کوئی نماز نہیں ہے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن ابي هريرة عن النبى الله الله قال : (( اذا أقيمت الصلوة فلا صلوة الا المكتوبة ( مسلم شریف ، باب کراھیة الشروع في نافلة بعد شروع المؤذن في اقامة الصلوۃ ، الخ، ص ۲۸۸، نمبر ۱۶۴۴/۷۱۰ / ترمذی شریف ، باب ماجاء اذا اقیمت الصلوۃ فلا صلوۃ الا المكتوبة ،ص۱۱۳،نمبر ۴۲) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ فرض نماز کی اقامت کہی جارہی ہو تو کوئی نماز نہ پڑھے ، بلکہ فرض ہی پڑھے۔ (۲) عن ابن بحينة قال : صلى الله أقيمت صلوة الصبح ، فرأى رسول الله الله رجلا يصلى و المؤذن يقيم فقال : (( أتصلى الصبح أربعا ))؟ مسلم شریف ، باب کراھیۃ الشروع في نافلة بعد شروع المؤذن في اقامة الصلوۃ ، الخ ص ۲۸۸، نمبرا ا۱۶۵۰/۷) اس حدیث میں اقامت کے وقت سنت پڑھنے سے منع فرمایا ہے۔ (۳) ایک وجہ یہ بھی ہے کہ جماعت میں شامل ہونا واجب ہے اور سنت پڑھنا سنت ہے اس لئے واجب کو تر جیح دی جائے گی۔
Translation: (719) And whoever comes at a time when the imam is in the fard prayer, he should follow the imam and not occupy himself with the sunnah. Evidence: (1) When the congregation has begun, there is no other prayer. For this there is the hadith: Abu Hurairah narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'When the iqamah is said, there is no prayer except the obligatory one.' (Muslim, Tirmidhi) (2) Ibn Muhayriz reported that the iqamah for Fajr was said, and the Prophet (peace be upon him) saw a man praying while the mu'adhdhin was saying the iqamah, and said: 'Do you pray Fajr with four (rak'ahs)?' (Muslim) (3) Another reason: joining the congregation is wajib, while praying sunnah is sunnah, so the wajib should be given precedence.
Source pages p. 28

Commentary
This lesson establishes a general principle in the Hanafi school: when a person enters the mosque and finds the imam already leading the fard prayer (or the iqamah is being called), he must join the congregation immediately and not engage in any sunnah prayer, including the regular sunnah prayers associated with that fard. The text provides three proofs: First, the famous hadith 'When the iqamah is said, there is no prayer except the obligatory one' (reported by Muslim and Tirmidhi). Second, the hadith where the Prophet rebuked a man for praying two rak'ahs during the iqamah for Fajr, asking if he was praying four rak'ahs (implying the two sunnah plus the two fard). Third, a rational proof: joining the congregation is a wajib (obligatory) act, while performing sunnah is only recommended; the wajib must take precedence over the sunnah. This ruling applies generally, with the exception of Fajr sunnah as seen in the next lesson.

Key Terms
اقتدى (iqtadā): To follow the imam in congregational prayer.
واجب (wājib): A legal obligation; joining the congregation is considered wājib in this context.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When the iqamah is called, what prayer is permitted according to the hadith quoted in the text?
A) Only the obligatory prayer (al-Maktubah).
B) Any supererogatory prayer.
C) Only the sunnah of Fajr.
D) No prayer at all.

Key Takeaway
When the iqamah is called for a fard prayer, the only valid prayer is the fard itself; one must join the congregation immediately and abandon all supererogatory prayers.

Exception for Fajr Sunnah When Safe from Missing Congregation
Ruling allowing Fajr sunnah during iqamah if congregation can still be caught

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on praying the Fajr sunnah during iqamah and apply the condition that one must hope to catch at least one rak'ah of the congregation.

Core Idea
Fajr sunnah is so emphasized that it may be prayed even during iqamah—provided you can still catch the congregation.

The general Hanafi rule states that once the iqamah is called, one should not begin any nafl prayer. However, the Fajr sunnah is given exceptional status due to its high emphasis (sunnah mu'akkadah). This lesson details the condition under which this exception applies and provides the textual evidence from the Prophet's practice and that of the Companions.

Guided Path
1
1. Recognize the general prohibition and the exception
Recall that normally no sunnah should be started after iqamah. Understand that Fajr sunnah is an exception.
2
2. Identify the condition for the exception
The exception applies only if the person hopes to catch at least one rak'ah of the fard congregation. If missing the congregation is feared, the sunnah is abandoned.
The condition is based on the greater importance of the congregational prayer.
3
3. Locate the proofs
The text provides three categories of evidence: (a) a hadith from Ali that the Prophet prayed the two rak'ahs at iqamah, (b) athar from Sa'id ibn Jubayr and Ibn Mas'ud showing the practice of praying at the door or even after iqamah, and (c) a general hadith emphasizing the importance of the two rak'ahs.
4
4. Analyze the legal implication
The Fajr sunnah is classified as sunnah mu'akkadah. This justifies an exception to the general rule. The Hanafi school prioritizes this sunnah over the general prohibition of nafl during iqamah, but only when the congregation is not endangered.
5
5. Apply the ruling
In practice: if confident of catching the congregation, pray the sunnah quickly in a corner and then join. If uncertain or likely to miss the fard completely, skip the sunnah and join directly.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۷۲۰) ہاں فجر کی سنت پڑھنے سے جماعت فوت ہونے کا اندیشہ نہ ہو تو سنت پڑھ کر شریک ہو جائے۔ اور اگر جماعت فوت ہو جانے کا خوف ہو تو اس کو چھوڑ دے۔ تشریح : فجر کی سنت کی اہمیت ہے اس لئے اگر اس بات کی امید ہو کہ فرض کی آخری رکعت مل جائے گی تو ایک کونے پر سنت پڑھ کر اس میں شامل ہو جائے ، اور آخری رکعت بھی ملنے کی امید نہ ہو تو سنت چھوڑ کر جماعت میں شامل ہو جائے کیونکہ جماعت اہم ہے وجه : فجر کی سنت پڑھے اسکی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے (۱) ۔ عن على قال كان النبى الله يصلى الركعتين عند الاقامة .( ابن ماجہ شریف ، باب ما جاء فی الرکعتین قبل الفجر، ص۱۶۰، نمبر ۱۱۴۷) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ فجر کی سنت اتنی اہم ہے کہ فرض کی اقامت کے وقت بھی اسکو پڑھ سکتا ہے۔ (۲) اور دروازے کے پاس سنت پڑھے اسکی دلیل یہ اثر ہے . عن سعيد بن جبير أ و أنه جاء الى المسجد و الامام في صلاة الفجر فصلى الركعتين قبل أن يلج المسجد عند باب المسجد . (مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ، باب الرجل يدخل المسجد فی الفجر ، ج ثانی، ص ۵۶، نمبر ۶۴۱۲) اس اثر میں ہے کہ فجر کی جماعت کھڑی ہوگئی ہو تو مسجد کے دروازے کے پاس سنت پڑھ لینی چاہئے ۔ (۳) عن حارثة بن مضرب أن ابن مسعود و أبا موسى خرجا مـن عـنـد سعيد بن العاص فأقيمت الصلوة فركع ابن مسعود ركعتين ثم دخل مع القوم في الصلوة و أما أبو موسى فدخل فى الصف (مصنف ابن ابي شيبة ، باب الرجل يدخل المسجد فى الفجر ، ج ثانی جص ۵۶ نمبر ۶۴۱۴) اس اثر میں ہے کہ فجر کی سنت اتنی اہم ہے کہ فرض نماز کھڑی ہوگئی ہو تب بھی فجر کی سنت پڑھے تب فرض میں شریک ہو۔ (۴) فجر کی سنت بہت اہم ہے اسلئے جماعت کے وقت بھی پڑھنے کی تاکید ہے ۔ اسکے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن ابي هريرة قال قال رسول الله الله لاتدعوهما و ان طردتكم الخيل ) ( ( ابوداود شریف، باب فی تخفیفهما رای سيته الفجر اص ۱۸۹، نمبر ۱۲۵۸) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ گھوڑا بھی روند دے تب بھی فجر کی سنت پڑھنی چاہئے۔
Translation: (720) However, regarding the sunnah of Fajr, if there is no fear of missing the congregation, then he should pray the sunnah and then join. And if he fears missing the congregation, he should leave it. Explanation: The sunnah of Fajr has great importance. Therefore, if there is hope that he will catch the last rak'ah of the fard, he should pray the sunnah in a corner and then join. If there is no hope of catching even the last rak'ah, he should leave the sunnah and join the congregation because the congregation is more important. Evidence for praying Fajr sunnah: (1) Hadith from Ali: The Prophet (peace be upon him) used to pray the two rak'ahs at the time of iqamah. (Ibn Majah) (2) Athar from Sa'id ibn Jubayr: He came to the mosque while the imam was in Fajr prayer, so he prayed the two rak'ahs at the door of the mosque before entering. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah) (3) Athar from Harithah ibn Mudrib that Ibn Mas'ud and Abu Musa came, the iqamah was said, so Ibn Mas'ud prayed two rak'ahs then entered, while Abu Musa entered the row directly. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah) (4) Hadith from Abu Hurairah: The Prophet said: 'Do not leave them (the two rak'ahs), even if horses trample you.' (Abu Dawud)
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This lesson provides an exception to the general rule established in lesson (719). While normally no sunnah should be prayed when the iqamah is called, the sunnah of Fajr (two rak'ahs before the fard) is given special importance in the Hanafi school. The ruling is conditional: if the person is confident that he will catch at least one rak'ah of the Fajr congregation (e.g., by quickly praying in a corner of the mosque), then he should pray the sunnah and join. If he is unsure or will miss the congregation entirely, he should abandon the sunnah and join directly. The text provides multiple proofs: (1) A hadith from Ali indicating the Prophet himself prayed the two rak'ahs at iqamah. (2) The practice of the Companion Sa'id ibn Jubayr. (3) The practice of Ibn Mas'ud, who prayed the two rak'ahs even when the congregation had started. (4) A strong hadith emphasizing the importance of these two rak'ahs even in extreme circumstances. This reflects the Hanafi view that Fajr sunnah is the most emphasized of the sunnah prayers (sunnah mu'akkadah).

Key Terms
سنّة الفجر (sunnat al-fajr): The two-rak'ah supererogatory prayer prescribed before the Fajr fard.
اقامة (iqāmah): The second call to prayer, indicating the immediate start of the fard prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when may a person pray the Fajr sunnah even if the iqamah has been called?
A) Always, regardless of whether he will miss the congregation.
B) Only if he is sure to catch at least one rak'ah of the fard.
C) Only if he prays it in the mosque before the imam starts.
D) Never; sunnah is not allowed when iqamah is called.

Key Takeaway
The Fajr sunnah is uniquely emphasized in the Hanafi school, allowing it to be prayed during iqamah as long as the congregation is not missed.

Salah — Prayer
beginner
6 min
Qada of Fajr Sunnah Only with Fard
Ruling on qada of Fajr sunnah with fard

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on making up the Fajr sunnah and identify the condition under which qada is permitted.

Core Idea
The Fajr sunnah is not made up alone; it is only made up together with the fard.

This lesson clarifies the Hanafi position on qada of the Fajr sunnah. Many assume all missed sunnah prayers can be performed later, but the Hanafi school restricts qada of sunnah to specific cases. The key is that the Fajr sunnah is attached to its fard; it cannot be performed independently as qada.

Guided Path
1
Identify the default ruling
Determine what act is being ruled on: making up the Fajr sunnah alone (without the fard). The Hanafi ruling is that this is not prescribed; it is makruh tanzih (disliked) to do so.
The ruling applies to any missed sunnah of Fajr, not just once.
2
Note the exception
The sunnah can be made up only if the Fajr fard is also being made up at the same time. The exception is conditional: the sunnah must accompany the fard in the same prayer time.
The exception does not apply to other sunnah prayers.
3
Understand the underlying principle
Sunnah prayers are generally not made up because they are tied to their respective fard prayers. The Fajr sunnah has a special connection to its fard, allowing qada together.
This is based on the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him).
4
Apply to practice
If a person missed both Fajr fard and sunnah, they should pray both when making up the fard. If only the sunnah was missed, it is not made up separately.
If one mistakenly prays the sunnah alone as qada, it is not considered valid qada.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۷۲۱) اور فجر کی اکیلی سنت کی قضا نہیں ہے، ہاں اگر فرض کے ساتھ قضا کی جائے۔
Translation: (721) And the solitary sunnah of Fajr is not made up (qada'), except if it is made up together with the fard.
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This is a brief ruling regarding the making up (qada') of the Fajr sunnah prayer. According to the Hanafi school, if a person misses the Fajr sunnah (the two rak'ahs before the fard), he does not make it up alone at another time. However, if he also missed the Fajr fard and is making it up later as qada, then he may also make up the sunnah along with it. The implication is that the Fajr sunnah is attached to the Fajr fard in terms of qada; it is not an independent act of worship that can be performed alone when the time has passed. This reflects the principle that the sunnah prayers are tied to their respective fard prayers and do not have independent qada, except in specific cases like the Fajr sunnah when the fard is also being made up.

Key Terms
قضاء (qaḍā'): The compensatory performance of a missed prayer after its prescribed time.
اكيلى سنت (akīlī sunnat): The solitary sunnah (i.e., the Fajr sunnah performed alone without the fard).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when is it permissible to make up the Fajr sunnah?
A) At any time after sunrise.
B) Only together with the Fajr fard prayer.
C) Alone, but only before midday.
D) It is never made up.

Key Takeaway
The Fajr sunnah is not made up alone; it is only made up together with the Fajr fard.

Fajr Sunnah and the Congregation: Conditional Exception
Explains the ruling on praying Fajr sunnah when congregation is established

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on praying the Fajr sunnah after iqamah by correctly identifying whether there is fear of missing the congregation.

Core Idea
Pray Fajr sunnah even after iqamah, but only if you will catch at least one rak'ah.

The Fajr sunnah is highly emphasized in the Hanafi school, but what happens when the congregation is about to start? This lesson explores the rule: normally, one should not begin a voluntary prayer after iqamah, but Fajr is an exception—with a condition. The source presents the ruling, its proof, and practical guidance from the Companions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general principle
The default rule: when the iqamah is called, one should join the congregation, not start a supererogatory prayer.
This is to avoid missing the wajib (congregation) for a sunnah.
2
Spot the exception for Fajr
The text says 'except in Fajr' – the Fajr sunnah is treated differently due to its special emphasis.
The Arabic phrase 'illa fi al-fajr' signals the exception.
3
Analyze the condition
If you are safe from missing the congregation (i.e., you can catch at least one rak'ah), pray the sunnah; if you fear missing it entirely, leave the sunnah.
The condition is about hope of catching some part of the fard.
4
Examine the proofs
The text cites four proofs: a hadith of Ali (praying at iqamah), athar of Sa'id ibn Jubayr (praying at the door), athar of Ibn Mas'ud (praying two rak'ahs then joining), and a hadith of Abu Hurairah (do not leave even if horses trample).
These establish the permissibility and virtue of the Fajr sunnah after iqamah.
5
Formulate the mufta bihi
The operative ruling: if you can catch at least one rak'ah of the congregation, pray the sunnah in a corner or outside, then join; otherwise, skip the sunnah and join immediately.
This balances the importance of both the sunnah and the congregational prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

ترجمه : (۷۲۰) ہاں فجر کی سنت پڑھنے سے جماعت فوت ہونے کا اندیشہ نہ ہو تو سنت پڑھ کر شریک ہو جائے۔ اور اگر جماعت فوت ہو جانے کا خوف ہو تو اس کو چھوڑ دے۔
تشریح : فجر کی سنت کی اہمیت ہے اس لئے اگر اس بات کی امید ہو کہ فرض کی آخری رکعت مل جائے گی تو ایک کونے پر سنت پڑھ کر اس میں شامل ہو جائے ، اور آخری رکعت بھی ملنے کی امید نہ ہو تو سنت چھوڑ کر جماعت میں شامل ہو جائے کیونکہ جماعت اہم ہے وجه : فجر کی سنت پڑھے اسکی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے (۱) ۔ عن على قال كان النبى الله يصلى الركعتين عند الاقامة .( ابن ماجہ شریف ، باب ما جاء فی الرکعتین قبل الفجر، ص۱۶۰، نمبر ۱۱۴۷) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ فجر کی سنت اتنی اہم ہے کہ فرض کی اقامت کے وقت بھی اسکو پڑھ سکتا ہے۔ (۲) اور دروازے کے پاس سنت پڑھے اسکی دلیل یہ اثر ہے . عن سعيد بن جبير أ و أنه جاء الى المسجد و الامام في صلاة الفجر فصلى الركعتين قبل أن يلج المسجد عند باب المسجد . (مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ، باب الرجل يدخل المسجد فی الفجر ، ج ثانی، ص ۵۶، نمبر ۶۴۱۲) اس اثر میں ہے کہ فجر کی جماعت کھڑی ہوگئی ہو تو مسجد کے دروازے کے پاس سنت پڑھ لینی چاہئے ۔ (۳) عن حارثة بن مضرب أن ابن مسعود و أبا موسى خرجا مـن عـنـد سعيد بن العاص فأقيمت الصلوة فركع ابن مسعود ركعتين ثم دخل مع القوم في الصلوة و أما أبو موسى فدخل فى الصف (مصنف ابن ابي شيبة ، باب الرجل يدخل المسجد فى الفجر ، ج ثانی جص ۵۶ نمبر ۶۴۱۴) اس اثر میں ہے کہ فجر کی سنت اتنی اہم ہے کہ فرض نماز کھڑی ہوگئی ہو تب بھی فجر کی سنت پڑھے تب فرض میں شریک ہو۔ (۴) فجر کی سنت بہت اہم ہے اسلئے جماعت کے وقت بھی پڑھنے کی تاکید ہے ۔ اسکے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن ابي هريرة قال قال رسول الله الله لاتدعوهما و ان طردتكم الخيل ) ( ( ابوداود شریف، باب فی تخفیفهما رای سیته الفجر اص ۱۸۹، نمبر ۱۲۵۸) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ گھوڑا بھی روند دے تب بھی فجر کی سنت پڑھنی چاہئے۔
(720) Except in Fajr: if he is safe from missing it (the congregation) and if he is not safe, he leaves it. Translation: (720) Yes, if there is no fear of missing the congregation by praying the Fajr sunnah, then pray the sunnah and join. And if there is fear of missing the congregation, then leave it. Commentary: The Fajr sunnah has importance. Therefore, if there is hope that the last rak'ah of the obligatory prayer will be caught, then pray the sunnah in a corner and join it. And if there is no hope of catching even the last rak'ah, then leave the sunnah and join the congregation because the congregation is important. Proof: Hadith (1) from Ali: The Prophet used to pray the two rak'ahs at the time of iqamah. (2) The athar from Sa'id ibn Jubayr: He came to the mosque and the imam was in Fajr prayer, so he prayed the two rak'ahs before entering the mosque at its door. (3) From Harithah ibn Mudarrib: Ibn Mas'ud and Abu Musa left from Sa'id ibn al-'As, and the prayer was established. Ibn Mas'ud bowed two rak'ahs then entered with the people in prayer, while Abu Musa entered the row. (4) Hadith from Abu Hurairah: The Prophet said: Do not leave them (the two rak'ahs) even if horses trample you.
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof (hukm ma'a al-dalil) from the section on catching the obligatory prayer. The author states the general principle that when the congregation is established, one should not begin a supererogatory prayer. However, Fajr sunnah is an exception due to its great emphasis. The ruling is conditional: if one fears missing the congregation (i.e., even the last rak'ah), then the sunnah is abandoned; otherwise, it is prayed even after the iqamah. The commentary elaborates that the Fajr sunnah may be prayed in a corner of the mosque or outside the door, as reported from the Companions. Four proofs are cited: (1) A hadith from Ali showing the Prophet prayed the two rak'ahs at iqamah, (2) an athar from Sa'id ibn Jubayr praying at the door, (3) an athar from Ibn Mas'ud praying the two rak'ahs before joining the congregation, and (4) a hadith from Abu Hurairah emphasizing the importance of the Fajr sunnah even in difficult circumstances. The Hanafi position is clear: the Fajr sunnah is highly recommended (sunnah mu'akkadah) and in normal circumstances should not be abandoned; however, the obligation of congregational prayer (wajib) takes precedence if there is a real fear of missing it. This balance is reflected in the conditional phrasing.

Key Terms
فجر (fajr): The dawn prayer, consisting of two rak'ahs fard and two rak'ahs sunnah.
سنت (sunnah): Supererogatory prayer that the Prophet regularly performed; in this context, the two rak'ahs before Fajr fard.
جماعت (jama'ah): Congregational prayer with an imam; considered wajib for men in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if the iqamah for Fajr has started and you are confident you can catch at least one rak'ah of the congregation after praying the sunnah, what is the ruling?
A) Pray the sunnah and then join the congregation.
B) Skip the sunnah and join immediately.
C) Wait for the congregation to finish and pray sunnah alone.
D) Pray the sunnah after the congregation.

Key Takeaway
The Fajr sunnah is prayed after iqamah only if you are confident of catching at least one rak'ah; otherwise, the wajib congregation takes priority.

When to Make Up the Fajr Sunnah
Explains when and how to make up the missed Fajr sunnah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on qada of the Fajr sunnah and identify the proof from the Prophet's action.

Core Idea
The Fajr sunnah is made up only if missed together with the fard, not alone.

This lesson addresses a common question: what if you miss the Fajr sunnah? The Hanafi school has a specific ruling based on the Prophet's practice and the principle that qada is for obligatory prayers. You will learn the exact conditions for making it up and the evidence behind the ruling.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Understand the core ruling: the Fajr sunnah is not made up if missed alone, but it is made up if missed together with the fard.
2
Identify the two scenarios
Distinguish between missing only the sunnah (no qada) versus missing both sunnah and fard (qada of sunnah before fard).
3
Analyze the hadith proof
Examine the hadith of Abu Qatadah: when the Prophet made up Fajr, he prayed two rak'ahs (sunnah) first, then the fard.
The hadith is in Sahih Muslim.
4
Understand the legal basis
Recognize that qada is for wajib acts; the sunnah is not wajib, so no independent qada. The sunnah is only made up as a continuation of the fard qada.
Also consider the prohibition of voluntary prayer after Fajr fard.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
... ترجمه : (۷۲۱) اور فجر کی اکیلی سنت کی قضا نہیں ہے، ہاں اگر فرض کے ساتھ قضا کی جائے۔  ثمرة النجاح جلد ٢ ۲۹ باب ادراك الفريضة (۷۲۱) ولم تقض سنة الفجر الا بفوتها مع الفرض ... تشریح : فجر کی سنت اور فرض دونوں قضا ہوئے ہوں تو جس وقت فرض قضا کرے اس کے ساتھ سنت کی بھی قضا کر لے لیکن صرف سنت چھوٹی ہو تو اس کی قضا نہ کرے۔ وجه : (1) عن ابي قتادة ..... فصلى رسول الله الا الله ركعتين ثم صلى الغداة فصنع كما كان يصنع كل يوم - ) مسلم شریف، باب قضاء الصلاة الفائمة واستحباب تقبيل قضائها، ص ۲۷۶، نمبر ۶۸ ۱۵۶۲) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ فجر کی قضا کی تو اس کے ساتھ سنت کی بھی قضا کی ۔ (۲) قضا واجب کی ہوتی ہے، یہ سنت ہے اس لئے اس کی مستقل قضا نہیں ہے ، البتہ سنت کے طور پر قضا کرنا چاہے تو کرسکتا ہے۔ (۳) اور فجر کے فرض کے بعد کوئی سنت پڑھنا اچھا نہیں ہے اس لئے فجر کے فرض کے بعد نہ پڑھے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے ۔ عن ابن عباس .... أن النبي نهى عن الصلوة بعد الصبح حتى تشرق الشمس ، و بعد العصر حتى تغرب . ( بخاری شریف، باب الصلوة بعد الفجر حتى ترتفع الشمس، ص ۱۸۲، نمبر ۱۵۸۱ مسلم شریف ، باب الاوقات التي نھي عن الصلوة فيها ،ص ۱۳۳۳، نمبر ۱۹۲۰/۸۲۵) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ فجر اور عصر کے فرض کے بعد کوئی نفل نہیں ہے ، اسلئے فرض پڑھنے کے بعد فجر اور عصر کی جماعت میں شریک نہ ہو۔
(721) And the sunnah of Fajr is not made up except if it is missed together with the obligatory prayer. Translation: And the Fajr sunnah alone is not made up; yes, if it is made up with the obligatory prayer. Commentary: If both the Fajr sunnah and fard are missed, then when making up the fard, also make up the sunnah with it. But if only the sunnah is missed, do not make it up. Proof: (1) Hadith from Abu Qatadah: The Prophet prayed two rak'ahs then prayed Fajr, doing as he used to do every day. (2) Qada is for obligatory acts; this is sunnah, so there is no independent qada, although one may pray it as supererogatory. (3) And after the Fajr fard, it is not good to pray any sunnah, so do not pray after Fajr. For this, there is a hadith from Ibn Abbas: The Prophet forbade prayer after Fajr until sunrise, and after Asr until sunset.
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof concerning the qada (make-up) of the Fajr sunnah. The matn states that the Fajr sunnah is only made up if it was missed together with the fard prayer. The commentary explains that if both the sunnah and fard of Fajr are missed (e.g., because one slept through the entire prayer time), then when making up the fard, one should also pray the sunnah. However, if only the sunnah was missed but the fard was performed on time, then the sunnah is not made up independently. The reason given is that qada is for obligatory prayers, and the sunnah is not obligatory. However, one may pray it voluntarily (as nafl) if desired. Additionally, after the Fajr fard, it is disliked to pray any voluntary prayer until sunrise, as per the prohibition in the hadith of Ibn Abbas. Therefore, the Fajr sunnah cannot be made up after the fard if only the sunnah was missed. The proofs include the action of the Prophet (peace be upon him) when he made up Fajr, he prayed the two rak'ahs (sunnah) first, and the general principle that qada applies to wajib acts.

Key Terms
قضا (qada): Making up a missed prayer after its time has passed.
سنة الفجر (sunnat al-fajr): The two rak'ahs of sunnah before the Fajr fard prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person wakes up after sunrise and missed both the Fajr sunnah and fard, what should he do according to the Hanafi school?
A) Pray the fard only, but not the sunnah.
B) Pray the sunnah first, then the fard.
C) Pray the fard first, then the sunnah.
D) Pray neither, as the time has passed.

Key Takeaway
The Fajr sunnah is only made up if both the sunnah and fard were missed; it is not a separate obligation.

Making Up the Missed Sunnah Before Zuhr
Explains when to make up the missed sunnah before Zuhr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on qada of the sunnah before Zuhr, identify the two recommended timings, and explain the evidence from hadith.

Core Idea
A missed sunnah mu'akkadah can be made up within the same prayer time; the Hanafi school recommends doing so after the fard before the ba'diyyah or after it.

This lesson examines the Hanafi position on making up the four rak'ahs of sunnah before Zuhr if they are missed. The primary text states that they should be made up within Zuhr time before the two rak'ahs after Zuhr. The commentary elaborates with two hadith from Aisha, showing that the Prophet himself would pray them after the Zuhr fard, either immediately or after the ba'diyyah. Understanding this ruling is essential because it demonstrates the Hanafi flexibility in handling sunnah prayers and the importance of intention in fulfilling recommended acts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
The passage concerns the four rak'ahs of sunnah before Zuhr. Determine that it is a sunnah mu'akkadah (emphasized sunnah). The act in question is making them up (qada) if missed.
Sunnah mu'akkadah is highly recommended; omitting it is makruh tanzih, but no sin.
2
Recognize the Recommended Time for Qada
The matn states to make them up in the time of Zuhr, before its pair (the two rak'ahs after Zuhr). The commentary clarifies that they should be prayed after the Zuhr fard but before the ba'diyyah. A second hadith permits praying them after the ba'diyyah as well. Both are recommended (mustahabb).
The timing is within Zuhr time; after Zuhr time ends, qada is not recommended.
3
Understand the Dalil from Hadith
Two ahadith from Aisha are cited. The first shows the Prophet would pray the missed four after the Zuhr fard. The second shows he would pray them after the two rakat after Zuhr. These establish the practice and provide flexibility.
Though the Prophet's actions are from ahad hadith, they are sufficient for recommended practices in Hanafi usul.
4
Note the Optional Nature
The commentary states that these are recommended forms; one may also do otherwise. Thus, if someone chooses not to make up the sunnah, it is permissible, though it is better to do so.
The Hanafi view is that qada of sunnah mu'akkadah is mustahabb, not wajib.
5
Apply the Ruling
In practice, if you miss the four before Zuhr, you have two valid options: (a) pray them after the fard but before the ba'diyyah, or (b) pray them after the ba'diyyah. Both are acceptable, and the latter is also supported by a hadith.
One may also combine them by praying the missed four and then the two ba'diyyah, maintaining the usual order.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۷۲۲) اور قبل الظہر کی سنت ظہر کے وقت میں دو رکعت بعد الظہر سے پہلے قضا کی جائے ۔ 6** تشریح : ظہر سے پہلے کی سنت چھوٹ گئی ہے تو ظہر کے بعد جو دو رکعت ہیں اس کے پہلے پڑھے، اور ظہر کے وقت میں پڑھے۔ وجه : (۱) ظہر کے بعد پڑھے اس کی حدیث یہ ہے ۔ عن عائشة أن النبي الله كان اذا لم يصل أربعا قبل الظهر صلا من بعدها . ( ترمذی شریف، باب منه [ای من الرکعتین بعد الظهر ] آخر ص ۱۱۵ نمبر ۴۲۶ ) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ پہلے کی چار رکعت سنت ظہر کے فرض کے بعد پڑھے، یعنی فورا بعد پڑھے۔ (۲) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ ظہر کے بعد جو دورکعت سنت ہے اس کے بعد پڑھے۔ عن عائشة قالت : كان رسول الله الا الله اذا فاتته الاربع قبل الظهر ، صلاها بعد الركعتين بعد الظهر - (ابن ماجہ شریف ، باب من فاته الا ربع قبل الظهر ، ص ۱۶۲ نمبر ۱۱۵۸) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ ظہر کی چھوٹی ہوئی سنت فرض کے بعد اداء کرے۔۔ یہ سب استحبابی شکلیں ہیں اس کے خلاف بھی کر سکتا ہے۔
(722) And he makes up the sunnah which is before Zuhr in its time, before its pair (the two rak'ahs after Zuhr). Translation: And the sunnah before Zuhr is made up in the time of Zuhr, two rak'ahs before the after-Zuhr (sunnah). Commentary: If the sunnah before Zuhr is missed, then pray it after the Zuhr fard, before the two rak'ahs (sunnah after Zuhr), and pray it within the time of Zuhr. Proof: (1) Hadith from Aisha: When the Prophet did not pray four rak'ahs before Zuhr, he prayed them after it. (2) Hadith from Aisha: When he missed the four before Zuhr, he prayed them after the two rak'ahs after Zuhr. All these are recommended forms; one may also do otherwise.
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof concerning the make-up (qada) of the sunnah before Zuhr (i.e., the four rak'ahs of sunnah before the Zuhr fard). The matn states that it is made up in the Zuhr time, before the two rak'ahs of sunnah after Zuhr (i.e., before the ba'diyyah). The commentary explains that if one misses the sunnah before Zuhr, he should pray it after the Zuhr fard but before the two rak'ahs of sunnah that are normally prayed after the fard. The proofs are two hadith from Aisha showing that the Prophet would pray the missed four rak'ahs after the Zuhr fard, either immediately or after the ba'diyyah. The commentary notes that these are recommended (mustahabb) forms; one may also choose other orders. The Hanafi position is that the qada of the Zuhr sunnah is not obligatory but recommended, and it should be done within the Zuhr time.

Key Terms
قبل الظهر (qabl al-zuhr): The four rak'ahs of sunnah prayed before the Zuhr fard prayer.
شفع (shaf'): The pair; in this context, it refers to the two rak'ahs of sunnah prayed after Zuhr (the ba'diyyah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) After the Zuhr fard, before the two rak'ahs of sunnah after Zuhr.

C) The next day at the same time.
D) He should not make them up at all.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school recommends making up the missed sunnah before Zuhr within Zuhr time, either before or after the ba'diyyah, based on prophetic practice.

Catching One Rak'ah of Congregation: Virtue vs. Full Status
Explains the ruling on catching one rak'ah of Zuhr congregation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on catching one rak'ah of a four-rak'ah prayer in congregation and apply it to determine fulfillment of an oath.

Core Idea
Catching one rak'ah gives the virtue but not the full legal status of congregation.

In this lesson, we examine a specific ruling from the Hanafi school regarding catching a portion of the congregational prayer. The matn states that for Zuhr (four rak'ahs), catching only one rak'ah with the imam does not count as having prayed in congregation for all legal purposes, though the reward is obtained. This distinction has practical consequences, for example in fulfilling an oath to pray in congregation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is catching one rak'ah of Zuhr with the congregation. Ruling: the person is not considered to have prayed in congregation, but he obtains its virtue.
The text explicitly states this: 'he is not considered to have prayed Zuhr in congregation by catching one rak'ah, but rather he catches its virtue.'
2
Locate the evidence
The text does not cite a specific dalil, but the ruling is based on the Hanafi understanding that full congregational status requires catching the entire prayer. The example of an oath shows the practical application.
The proof is implicit in the distinction made; the school relies on hadith about catching a rak'ah but restricts its application.
3
Trace the legal reasoning
For a four-rak'ah prayer, one rak'ah is less than half, so it does not constitute joining the congregation fully. The reward (fadilat) is given because some participation occurred.
The commentary explains that Zuhr has four rak'ahs; one rak'ah gives virtue but not full status.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The text mentions there is a difference of opinion regarding catching three rak'ahs. This ikhtilaf is not elaborated, but it indicates that the cutoff might be somewhere between one and four rak'ahs.
The passage is incomplete here; the full discussion is not available.
5
Apply the ruling to an oath scenario
If someone swears to pray in congregation, catching one rak'ah does not fulfill that oath because the prayer is not considered congregational.
This is directly from the commentary example.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۷۲۳) اور ظہر کی ایک رکعت ملنے سے جماعت سے پڑھنا نہیں کہا جاتا ، ہاں جماعت کی فضیلت ملے گی ۔ اور تین رکعت ملنے میں اختلاف ہے۔
تشریح : ظہر کی چار رکعت ہیں اس لئے ایک رکعت جماعت کے ساتھ پڑھی تو یہ کہی جائے گی کہ جماعت کی فضیلت مل گئی ، لیکن یہ نہیں کہی جائے گی کہ جماعت ملی، چنانچہ کسی نے قسم کھائی کہ جماعت کے ساتھ نماز پڑھوں گا تو ایک رکعت جماعت کے ساتھ
(723) And he is not considered to have prayed Zuhr in congregation by catching one rak'ah, but rather he catches its virtue. And there is difference of opinion regarding one who catches (three rak'ahs?). Translation: And from catching one rak'ah of Zuhr, it is not said that he prayed with the congregation; yes, he will get the virtue of congregation. And there is difference of opinion regarding catching three rak'ahs. Commentary: Zuhr has four rak'ahs, so if he prayed one rak'ah with the congregation, it will be said that he got the virtue of congregation, but it will not be said that he got the congregation. Thus, if someone swore that he would pray in congregation, then one rak'ah with the congregation...
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This is a ruling with an incomplete commentary from the section on catching the obligatory prayer. The matn states that catching only one rak'ah of the Zuhr congregation does not count as having prayed in congregation; rather, one obtains the virtue of congregational prayer. There is a difference of opinion regarding catching three rak'ahs (the text does not specify for which prayer). The commentary begins to explain that Zuhr has four rak'ahs, so catching one rak'ah gives the reward but not the full status of being with the congregation. An example is given: if someone swore to pray in congregation, catching only one rak'ah would not fulfill that oath. The passage is cut off before completing the discussion on the ikhtilaf regarding three rak'ahs. The Hanafi position is that for a four-rak'ah prayer, one must catch at least one rak'ah with the imam to receive the virtue of congregation, but the prayer is not considered fully congregational for certain legal consequences (like an oath).

Key Terms
مدرک (mudrik): A latecomer who joins the congregation after the imam has started; in this context, one who catches part of the prayer.
فضیلت (fadilat): The reward or virtue of congregation, as distinct from the legal status of being considered in congregation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Yes, because he caught the congregation.
B) No, because catching one rak'ah does not count as full congregation.
C) Yes, if he catches at least one rak'ah.
D) It depends on his intention.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, catching one rak'ah of a four-rak'ah prayer gives the reward but not the full legal status of congregational prayer.

Making Up the Sunnah of Fajr
Ruling on when the sunnah of Fajr is made up

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on making up the sunnah of Fajr, explain the dalil, and distinguish between qada' for wajib versus sunnah.

Core Idea
The sunnah of Fajr is only made up with the fard; it is not independently obligatory to make up.

This lesson examines the Hanafi position on when the sunnah (voluntary) prayer of Fajr is made up (qada'). Unlike obligatory prayers, sunnah prayers are not typically subject to qada'. However, the Hanafi school provides a nuanced ruling based on the Prophet's practice when he made up a missed Fajr prayer. Understanding this distinction clarifies the relationship between obligation (wajib) and confirmed sunnah (sunnah muakkadah) in matters of making up missed prayers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being ruled upon (the sunnah of Fajr) and what the ruling is regarding its qada'.
The passage states the sunnah is not made up except when missed with the fard.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the proof cited: the hadith of Abu Qatada where the Prophet prayed two rak'ahs then the fard when making up a missed Fajr.
The hadith is from Muslim.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the hadith prove the ruling? The Prophet's action shows the sunnah is performed alongside the fard, implying it is not made up independently.
The context of making up a missed prayer is key.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Identify that the Shafi'i school differs, allowing independent qada' of the sunnah.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
Understand why the Hanafi position is mufta bihi: qada' is for wajib, and this is a sunnah.
The ruling is based on the principle that sunnah is not wajib to make up.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَمْ تُقْضَ سُنَّةُ الْفَجْرِ إِلَّا بِفَوْتِهَا مَعَ الْفَرْضِ. عَنْ أَبِي قَتَادَةَ ... فَصَلَّى رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ رَكْعَتَيْنِ ثُمَّ صَلَّى الْغَدَاةَ فَصَنَعَ كَمَا كَانَ يَصْنَعُ كُلَّ يَوْمٍ. (مُسْلِمٌ) قَضَاءُ وَاجِبٍ تَكُونُ، وَهَذِهِ سُنَّةٌ فَلَا تُقْضَى مُسْتَقِلَّةً، إِلَّا إِنْ شَاءَ فَعَلَهَا عَلَى سَبِيلِ السُّنَّةِ. وَالْفَجْرُ بَعْدَ الْفَرْضِ لَا يُصَلَّى نَفْلٌ، كَمَا فِي حَدِيثِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ: نَهَى عَنِ الصَّلَاةِ بَعْدَ الصُّبْحِ حَتَّى تَشْرُقَ الشَّمْسُ.
The sunnah of Fajr is not made up except when it is missed along with the fard. On the authority of Abu Qatada ... the Messenger of Allah ﷺ prayed two rak'ahs then prayed the morning prayer, doing as he used to do every day. (Muslim) Qada' is for obligations, and this is a sunnah, so it is not made up independently; however, if one wishes, one may do it as a sunnah. And after the fard of Fajr, no voluntary prayer is offered, as in the hadith of Ibn Abbas: He forbade prayer after the dawn prayer until the sun rises.
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This is a ruling statement from the text explaining the legal position on making up the sunnah of Fajr. The passage establishes that the sunnah of Fajr is only to be made up (qada') if it was missed together with the obligatory prayer (fard). The proof is a hadith where the Prophet ﷺ first performed two rak'ahs (the sunnah) and then the fard when making up a missed Fajr prayer. The commentary clarifies that qada' is only for obligatory acts; this is a sunnah, so it is not made up independently. However, if one wishes, they may perform it as a sunnah (nafl) but not as a dedicated qada'. Additionally, after the fard of Fajr, no voluntary prayers are allowed until sunrise, as per another hadith. This ruling is specific to the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
سنة الفجر (sunnat al-fajr): The two rak'ahs of sunnah (voluntary) prayer performed before the obligatory Fajr prayer.
قضاء (qada'): Making up a missed obligatory or recommended prayer after its prescribed time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When is the sunnah of Fajr made up according to the Hanafi school?
A) Whenever it is missed, regardless of the fard
B) Only if the fard of Fajr is also missed
C) It is never made up
D) Only on Fridays

Key Takeaway
The sunnah of Fajr is only made up together with the fard, not independently, because qada' is reserved for obligatory acts.

Making Up the Sunnah Before Zuhr: Ruling and Proof
Ruling on making up the sunnah before Zuhr with proof from hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on making up the missed sunnah before Zuhr and explain the evidence from the Sunnah.

Core Idea
Making up the pre-Zuhr sunnah is recommended; the Prophet's practice shows flexibility within Zuhr time.

The Hanafi school holds that the four rak'ahs of sunnah before Zuhr are sunnah muakkadah. If one misses them, it is mustahabb to make them up within the Zuhr time, preferably before the two rak'ahs after Zuhr. The proof comes from two hadiths of Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) showing the Prophet's ﷺ practice. This lesson examines the ruling and the evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What act is being ruled upon? The act is making up the four rak'ahs of sunnah before Zuhr that were missed. What is the ruling? It is mustahabb (recommended).
The text explicitly says 'all of these are recommended' (istihbabiyyah).
2
Locate the dalil
What proof is cited? Two hadiths from Aisha. The first is from Tirmidhi, the second from Ibn Majah.
Both hadiths are ahad, so they are zanni al-thubut.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How do these hadiths prove the ruling? The Prophet's action of making up the missed sunnah shows that it is permissible and recommended. The two hadiths together show two possible timings: after the fard or after the after-sunnah.
The Hanafi position takes both hadiths as valid, hence flexibility.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Is there disagreement? Some schools (e.g., Shafi'i) may restrict the make-up to immediately after the fard, while the Hanafi school allows both timings.
See the al-mukhtalaf fih block for details.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
What is the operative ruling for fatwa? In the Hanafi school, it is mustahabb to make up the missed sunnah before the after-sunnah, but doing it after is also permissible.
This is derived from the second hadith's specification.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَقَضَى السُّنَّةَ الَّتِي قَبْلَ الظُّهْرِ فِي وَقْتِهِ قَبْلَ شَفْعِهِ. عَنْ عَائِشَةَ أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ ﷺ كَانَ إِذَا لَمْ يُصَلِّ أَرْبَعًا قَبْلَ الظُّهْرِ صَلَّى مِنْ بَعْدِهَا. (التِّرْمِذِيُّ). وَعَنْهَا قَالَتْ: كَانَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ إِذَا فَاتَتْهُ الْأَرْبَعُ قَبْلَ الظُّهْرِ صَلَّاهَا بَعْدَ الرَّكْعَتَيْنِ بَعْدَ الظُّهْرِ. (ابْنُ مَاجَهْ). هَذِهِ كُلُّهَا اسْتِحْبَابِيَّةٌ، وَيَجُوزُ خِلَافُهَا.
And he makes up the sunnah that is before Zuhr in its time before its pair (the two rak'ahs after Zuhr). On the authority of Aisha that the Prophet ﷺ, when he did not pray four rak'ahs before Zuhr, prayed them after it. (Tirmidhi). And on her authority, she said: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ, when the four before Zuhr were missed, he prayed them after the two rak'ahs after Zuhr. (Ibn Majah). All of these are recommended, and the opposite is permissible.
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This passage gives the ruling on making up the missed sunnah before Zuhr. The primary ruling is that if one misses the four rak'ahs of sunnah before Zuhr, they should be made up in the time of Zuhr, before the two rak'ahs of sunnah after Zuhr (i.e., between the fard and the after-sunnah). The proof includes two hadiths from Aisha showing the Prophet's practice. The first hadith indicates that he prayed the missed four after the Zuhr prayer (i.e., after the fard). The second specifies that he prayed them after the two rak'ahs that are after Zuhr (i.e., after the regular after-sunnah). The commentary notes that these are recommended forms, and one may act contrary to them (e.g., pray the make-up at a different time). The Hanafi position is that the sunnah before Zuhr is sunnah muakkadah, and it is mustahabb to make it up in this manner.

Key Terms
السنة التي قبل الظهر (al-sunnah allati qabl al-zuhr): The four rak'ahs of sunnah (two sets of two) that are performed before the Zuhr fard prayer.
شفعه (shaf'uhu): Literally 'its pair', referring to the two rak'ahs of sunnah after Zuhr.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in this passage, what is the status of making up the missed sunnah before Zuhr?
A) Wajib
B) Mustahabb
C) Sunnah muakkadah
D) Haram

Key Takeaway
Making up the missed pre-Zuhr sunnah is mustahabb, and the Prophet's practice shows it can be done after the fard or after the after-sunnah within Zuhr time.

Catching One Rak'ah: Virtue vs. Full Congregation
Ruling on whether catching one rak'ah counts as praying in congregation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between attaining the virtue of congregation and being considered as having prayed the entire prayer in congregation, and apply the Hanafi ruling on catching one rak'ah.

Core Idea
Catching one rak'ah gives virtue, not full congregational status; catching majority counts as whole.

In this passage, we examine a common scenario: a latecomer catches only part of the congregational prayer. The text clarifies that while one gains the virtue (fadl) of congregation, the entire prayer is not considered congregational for legal purposes such as oaths. A hadith is cited, and the principle of 'majority counts as whole' is introduced.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What situation is being discussed? The text specifically addresses a person who catches one rak'ah of Zuhr with the imam. Determine the ruling stated.
2
Distinguish between virtue and full status
The text explicitly says 'he does not pray Zuhr in congregation by catching one rak'ah, rather he attains its virtue.' Understand the two levels: fadl al-jama'ah (virtue) and full congregational reward.
3
Analyze the dalil
The hadith 'Whoever catches one rak'ah has caught the prayer' is the proof. How does the Hanafi school interpret it? They see it as meaning he caught the prayer as a latecomer, not that the whole prayer is congregational.
The hadith is zanni al-thubut and zanni al-dalalah.
4
Recognize the ikhtilaf on three rak'ahs and the principle
The text mentions disagreement about the one who catches three rak'ahs. It introduces the principle: 'The majority of a thing is considered as the whole.' Explain how this principle leads to the view that three rak'ahs count as full congregation for oaths.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَمْ يُصَلِّ الظُّهْرَ جَمَاعَةً بِإِدْرَاكِ رَكْعَةٍ بَلْ أَدْرَكَ فَضْلَهَا. وَاخْتُلِفَ فِي مُدْرِكِ الثَّلَاثِ. إِنْ أَدْرَكَ رَكْعَةً مَعَ الإِمَامِ، فَقَدْ أَدْرَكَ فَضْلَ الْجَمَاعَةِ وَلَيْسَ كَمَنْ صَلَّى الْكُلَّ مَعَهُ. عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ: «مَنْ أَدْرَكَ رَكْعَةً مِنَ الصَّلَاةِ فَقَدْ أَدْرَكَ الصَّلَاةَ.» (أَبُو دَاوُدَ، التِّرْمِذِيُّ). الْأَصْلُ: أَكْثَرُ الشَّيْءِ يُعْتَبَرُ كَالْكُلِّ.
And he does not pray Zuhr in congregation by catching one rak'ah, rather he attains its virtue. And there is disagreement regarding the one who catches three (rak'ahs). If he catches one rak'ah with the imam, then he attains the virtue of congregation, but not like the one who prays the entire (prayer) with him. On the authority of Abu Huraira: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: 'Whoever catches one rak'ah of the prayer has caught the prayer.' (Abu Dawud, Tirmidhi). The principle: The majority of a thing is considered as the whole.
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This passage addresses the issue of joining the congregation late. The ruling is that if a person catches only one rak'ah of the Zuhr prayer with the imam, he does not get the reward of having prayed the entire prayer in congregation; rather, he attains the virtue (fadl) of congregation. The text notes an ikhtilaf (disagreement) regarding if he catches three rak'ahs. The proof is the hadith: 'Whoever catches one rak'ah of the prayer has caught the prayer,' meaning he has caught the congregation in the sense of being considered a latecomer, but not that the entire prayer is counted as congregational. The commentary explains that if someone swears an oath to pray in congregation, catching one rak'ah does not fulfill that oath because the entire prayer was not with the congregation. However, catching the majority (i.e., three out of four) is treated as the whole according to the principle (al-asl: akthar al-shay' yu'tabaru ka al-kull). This disagreement among scholars (some say three rak'ahs count as full congregation, others do not) is reflected in the text.

Key Terms
مدرك (mudrik): A latecomer who joins the congregation after the imam has begun; one who catches part of the prayer.
فضل الجماعة (fadl al-jama'ah): The virtue or reward of praying in congregation, which is attained even if one catches only part of the prayer.
أكثر الشيء يعتبر كالكل (akthar al-shay' yu'tabaru ka al-kull): The legal principle that the majority of a thing is considered as the whole.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, if a person catches one rak'ah of Zuhr with the imam, what is the ruling?
A) He has prayed the entire Zuhr in congregation
B) He attains the virtue of congregation but not the full congregational status
C) He must repeat the prayer
D) He is considered absent

Key Takeaway
Catching one rak'ah gives the virtue of congregation but not the legal status of having prayed the entire prayer in congregation.

Voluntary Prayers Before the Fard if Time Is Short
Ruling on performing sunnah prayers before fard when time is limited

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on performing sunnah prayers before the fard when time is short and apply the condition of safety from loss of time.

Core Idea
Prioritize the fard over sunnah when time is tight; the sunnah is postponed, not abandoned.

Sometimes we wonder whether to pray the sunnah before the obligatory prayer if the congregation is about to start or time is running out. This passage provides a clear ruling: the sunnah is recommended only if you are safe from losing the fard time or congregation. Otherwise, skip the sunnah and join the fard directly. The Prophet's practice and a hadith on the virtue of the twelve rak'ahs support this guidance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is performing voluntary (sunnah) prayers before the obligatory prayer. The ruling: do so if safe from loss of time, otherwise omit.
The ruling is mustahabb (recommended) under the condition.
2
Locate the dalil
Two hadiths from Aisha: (1) describes the Prophet's regular sunnah prayers before Zuhr and Fajr. (2) mentions the great reward for persevering in the twelve rak'ahs.
The first shows his practice when time allowed; the second encourages consistency.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadiths establish the virtue of sunnah prayers but do not require them. The condition 'if safe from loss of time' is derived from the principle that wajib (fard) takes precedence over recommended acts.
The Prophet's practice is model, but the fiqh rule prioritizes fard when conflict appears.
4
Note the condition
The key condition is 'amn fawt al-waqt' (safety from loss of time). This includes fear of missing the congregation, which is similarly important.
If congregation (jama'ah) is about to start, one should join it and postpone the sunnah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيَتَطَوَّعُ قَبْلَ الْفَرْضِ إِنْ أَمِنَ فَوْتَ الْوَقْتِ وَإِلَّا فَلَا. عَنْ عَائِشَةَ قَالَتْ: كَانَ يُصَلِّي فِي بَيْتِي قَبْلَ الظُّهْرِ أَرْبَعًا ثُمَّ يَخْرُجُ فَيُصَلِّي بِالنَّاسِ، ثُمَّ يَدْخُلُ فَيُصَلِّي رَكْعَتَيْنِ... وَكَانَ إِذَا طَلَعَ الْفَجْرُ صَلَّى رَكْعَتَيْنِ. (مُسْلِمٌ). وَعَنْهَا قَالَتْ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ: «مَنْ ثَابَرَ عَلَى ثِنْتَيْ عَشْرَةَ رَكْعَةً مِنَ السُّنَّةِ بَنَى اللَّهُ لَهُ بَيْتًا فِي الْجَنَّةِ: أَرْبَعَ رَكَعَاتٍ قَبْلَ الظُّهْرِ، وَرَكْعَتَيْنِ بَعْدَهَا، وَرَكْعَتَيْنِ بَعْدَ الْمَغْرِبِ، وَرَكْعَتَيْنِ بَعْدَ الْعِشَاءِ، وَرَكْعَتَيْنِ قَبْلَ الْفَجْرِ.» (التِّرْمِذِيُّ)
And he performs voluntary prayers before the fard if he feels safe from loss of time, otherwise not. On the authority of Aisha, she said: He used to pray in my house before Zuhr four, then go out and lead the people, then enter and pray two... And when dawn broke, he prayed two. (Muslim). And on her authority, she said: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: 'Whoever perseveres in twelve rak'ahs of sunnah, Allah will build for him a house in Paradise: four rak'ahs before Zuhr, two after it, two after Maghrib, two after Isha, and two before Fajr.' (Tirmidhi)
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling on whether to perform the sunnah (voluntary) prayers before the obligatory prayer when time is short. The ruling is that if there is no fear of missing the time (or the congregation), one should perform them; otherwise, they should be omitted. The commentary explains that congregation is wajib and sunnah is nafl, so the wajib takes precedence. The first hadith from Aisha describes the Prophet's practice of regularly performing the twelve rak'ahs of sunnah. The second hadith emphasizes the virtue of these twelve rak'ahs. The evidence supports the recommendation of performing sunnah prayers before the fard when possible, but if time is tight, the fard is prioritized.

Key Terms
تطوع (tatawwu'): Voluntary prayers that are not obligatory, including sunnah muakkadah and nafl.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What should a person do if the congregation for Zuhr is about to start and they have not yet prayed the four rak'ahs of sunnah before Zuhr?
A) Pray the sunnah quickly and then join the congregation
B) Join the congregation and omit the sunnah
C) Pray the sunnah after the fard in all cases
D) Wait for the next prayer

Key Takeaway
When time or congregation is at risk, skip the sunnah and perform the fard first; the sunnah can be made up later.

Voluntary Prayers Before Obligatory: When to Prioritize Fard
Ruling on prioritizing fard over sunnah when time or congregation is at risk.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on offering voluntary prayers before the obligatory when there is fear of missing the congregation or time, and explain the basis for prioritizing fard.

Core Idea
If congregation or time may be lost, leave the Sunnah and join the fard – wajib precedes sunnah.

A common question is whether one should pray the Sunnah before the fard prayer when the congregation has already started or time is short. Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani provides a clear answer in this passage: the ruling depends on whether there is a real fear of missing the wajib obligation of congregation or the prayer time. This lesson examines that ruling and the proofs that support it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is offering voluntary prayers (sunnah or nafl) before the obligatory prayer. The ruling is: if it is safe from missing the time or congregation, then do it; otherwise, do not.
The text uses the word 'يتطوع' meaning to supererogate.
2
Understand the condition (fear of loss)
The condition is 'if one feels safe from missing the time/congregation' (ان امن فوت الوقت والا فلا). This implies that if there is any risk of losing the fard time or the congregation, one should skip the voluntary prayers.
Fear can be justified (e.g., imam has already started salah or time is about to exit).
3
Explain the basis: wajib over sunnah
Congregation (wajib) takes precedence over sunnah. The author states: 'جماعت واجب ہے اور سنن سنت ہیں' – congregation is wajib, sunnah is sunnah, so one should observe the wajib. Similarly, praying within the time is mandatory.
This is a general principle in Hanafi fiqh: when a wajib and a sunnah conflict, the wajib prevails.
4
Examine the proofs
The passage cites two proofs: (1) The hadith of A'ishah describing the Prophet's regular practice of praying four rak'ahs before Zuhr, two after, etc., showing that sunnah are performed when time permits. (2) The hadith of perseverance on twelve rak'ahs establishing their virtue, but that does not override the priority of fard.
The hadith texts are quoted to confirm the sunnah, but the ruling on precedence is derived from the principle.

صلى الله
عشرة ركعة من السنة بنى الله له بيتا فى الجنة : أربع ركعات قبل الظهر ، و ركعتين بعدها ، و ركعتين بعد المغرب ، و ركعتين بعد العشاء ، و ركعتين قبل الفجر )) ( ترندی شریف ، باب ما جاء فیمن صلى في يوم وليلة مثنتى عشرة رکعته من السنة، ص ۱۲، نمبر ۴۱۴ رابن ماجه، باب ما جاء فی ثنتى عشرة ركعة من السنته، ص ۱۲۰ نمبر ۱۱۴۰ر مسلم شریف ، باب فضل السنن
Chapter: Catching the Obligatory Prayer. Three [724]: He may supererogate before the obligatory if he feels safe from missing the time, otherwise not. [725]: And whoever catches his imam in ruku' (bowing) will break his oath by praying (only that much), because he did not pray the entire prayer with the congregation, only the virtue of congregation was attained. And if he prayed three rak'ahs with the congregation, there is disagreement about that: those who said that praying the majority is like praying the whole said he does not break his oath, because it is as if he prayed the whole prayer with the congregation. And those who said he has not yet prayed the whole prayer with the congregation said he breaks his oath. Basis: (1) There is proof in the hadith from Abu Hurairah that the Prophet said: 'Whoever catches a rak'ah of the prayer has caught the prayer.' (Abu Dawood, etc.) This hadith indicates that if he caught even one rak'ah, he attained the virtue of congregation. Principle: Catching the majority of a thing is considered as catching that thing. Translation of [724]: And if there is no fear of missing it, he should perform voluntary prayers before the obligatory, otherwise not. Explanation: If there is no fear of missing congregation or time, he should pray the Sunnahs before the obligatory, and if possible, many supererogatory acts. And if he fears that praying the Sunnahs will cause him to miss the congregation or the time, he should leave the Sunnahs and pray the fard. Basis: (1) Congregation is wajib and Sunnahs are sunnah, so he should observe the wajib. (2) If there is time, he should pray the Sunnahs, and the proof is the hadith: I asked A'ishah about the voluntary prayer of the Prophet; she said: He used to pray four in my house before Zuhr, then go out and lead the people, then enter and pray two, etc. This hadith shows that before and after the fard prayers throughout the day and night there are confirmed Sunnahs, which are twelve rak'ahs. (3) A'ishah narrated that the Prophet said: 'Whoever perseveres with twelve rak'ahs of the Sunnah, Allah will build for him a house in Paradise: four before Zuhr, two after it, two after Maghrib, two after 'Isha, and two before Fajr.'
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage covers two rulings from the chapter on catching the obligatory prayer. First (724): It is recommended to perform voluntary prayers (Sunnah and nafl) before the obligatory prayer only if there is no fear that doing so will cause the loss of the congregation or the prayer time. The reasoning is that congregation (wajib) takes precedence over sunnah. Second (725): The ruling about an oath to pray with congregation. If someone swears to pray with congregation and only catches the imam in ruku' (i.e., one rak'ah), he breaks his oath according to some. However, if he catches three rak'ahs, there is a difference of opinion: some consider that the majority (three) is treated as the whole, so the oath is not broken. The key hadith from Abu Hurairah is cited: 'Whoever catches a rak'ah of the prayer has caught the prayer.' This is used to argue that catching one rak'ah gives the virtue of congregation, but not necessarily that the whole prayer was performed. The principle 'أكثر الشيء كله' (the majority of a thing is like the whole) is applied by some scholars. The passage also confirms the twelve confirmed Sunnah rak'ahs from the hadith of A'ishah and the hadith of perseverance.

Key Terms
سنن مؤکدہ (sunan muʾakkadah): Confirmed Sunnah prayers that the Prophet regularly performed.
تطوع (tatawwuʿ): Voluntary, supererogatory acts of worship; here specifically voluntary prayers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in this lesson, what should a person do if he fears missing the congregation while praying the sunnah before the fard?
A) Continue the sunnah and then join the congregation.
B) Break the sunnah and join the congregation immediately.
C) Pray the sunnah after the fard instead.
D) Both B and C are correct depending on the situation.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that when performing sunnah prayers conflicts with a wajib (congregation or time), the wajib takes precedence and the sunnah should be postponed.

Catching a Rak'ah in Congregation: Effect on an Oath
Ruling on oath to pray with congregation when only part of the prayer is caught.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on an oath to pray with the congregation when only one or three rak'ahs are caught, and explain the disagreement among scholars on whether the majority of the prayer fulfills the oath.

Core Idea
Catching a single rak'ah gives the virtue of congregation but may not fulfill an oath; catching three rak'ahs leads to scholarly disagreement.

A person swears an oath to pray the entire prayer with the congregation. Later, he arrives late and catches only part of the prayer. Does his oath become broken? Imam Muhammad addresses this by distinguishing between catching a single rak'ah and catching the majority. This lesson examines the ruling and the underlying evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the oath
A person swears an oath that he will pray a particular prayer with the congregation. He later catches the imam in ruku' of the last rak'ah, or catches three rak'ahs. The question is whether he fulfilled his oath.
The oath is about praying 'with the congregation' – the entire prayer from beginning to end?
2
State the ruling for one rak'ah
If he catches only one rak'ah (e.g., joins in the last ruku'), then according to the text, the oath is broken. Reason: He did not pray the whole prayer with the congregation; he only attained the virtue of congregation.
The hadith says 'whoever catches a rak'ah has caught the prayer', but that refers to virtue not fulfillment of vow.
3
State the ruling for three rak'ahs (majority)
If he catches three rak'ahs (the majority of a four-rak'ah prayer), there is a difference of opinion. Some scholars say the oath is not broken because the majority is treated as the whole. Others say it is broken because the entire prayer was not performed with the congregation.
The text mentions both views without preferring one.
4
Explain the basis: the principle of 'majority is like the whole'
Those who say the oath is not broken apply the principle that 'الغالب ملحق بالكل' or the majority of a thing is considered as the whole. Those who disagree require actual complete performance.
This is a legal maxim used in various fiqh contexts.
5
Analyze the hadith proof
The hadith 'من أدرك ركعة من الصلوة فقد أدرك الصلوة' is cited. It is used to show that catching a rak'ah gives the virtue of congregation. But the text says this is not enough for the oath; the oath requires the actual prayer with congregation.
The hadith itself is about virtue, not about oaths. The application to oaths is by analogy.

And if he prayed three rak'ahs with the congregation, there is disagreement about that: those who said that praying the majority is like praying the whole said he does not break his oath, because it is as if he prayed the whole prayer with the congregation. And those who said he has not yet prayed the whole prayer with the congregation said he breaks his oath. Basis: (1) There is proof in the hadith from Abu Hurairah that the Prophet said: 'Whoever catches a rak'ah of the prayer has caught the prayer.' (Abu Dawood, etc.) This hadith indicates that if he caught even one rak'ah, he attained the virtue of congregation. Principle: Catching the majority of a thing is considered as catching that thing. Translation of [724]: And if there is no fear of missing it, he should perform voluntary prayers before the obligatory, otherwise not. Explanation: If there is no fear of missing congregation or time, he should pray the Sunnahs before the obligatory, and if possible, many supererogatory acts. And if he fears that praying the Sunnahs will cause him to miss the congregation or the time, he should leave the Sunnahs and pray the fard. Basis: (1) Congregation is wajib and Sunnahs are sunnah, so he should observe the wajib. (2) If there is time, he should pray the Sunnahs, and the proof is the hadith: I asked A'ishah about the voluntary prayer of the Prophet; she said: He used to pray four in my house before Zuhr, then go out and lead the people, then enter and pray two, etc. This hadith shows that before and after the fard prayers throughout the day and night there are confirmed Sunnahs, which are twelve rak'ahs. (3) A'ishah narrated that the Prophet said: 'Whoever perseveres with twelve rak'ahs of the Sunnah, Allah will build for him a house in Paradise: four before Zuhr, two after it, two after Maghrib, two after 'Isha, and two before Fajr.'
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage covers two rulings from the chapter on catching the obligatory prayer. First (724): It is recommended to perform voluntary prayers (Sunnah and nafl) before the obligatory prayer only if there is no fear that doing so will cause the loss of the congregation or the prayer time. The reasoning is that congregation (wajib) takes precedence over sunnah. Second (725): The ruling about an oath to pray with congregation. If someone swears to pray with congregation and only catches the imam in ruku' (i.e., one rak'ah), he breaks his oath according to some. However, if he catches three rak'ahs, there is a difference of opinion: some consider that the majority (three) is treated as the whole, so the oath is not broken. The key hadith from Abu Hurairah is cited: 'Whoever catches a rak'ah of the prayer has caught the prayer.' This is used to argue that catching one rak'ah gives the virtue of congregation, but not necessarily that the whole prayer was performed. The principle 'أكثر الشيء كله' (the majority of a thing is like the whole) is applied by some scholars. The passage also confirms the twelve confirmed Sunnah rak'ahs from the hadith of A'ishah and the hadith of perseverance.

Key Terms
رکعة (rakʿah): A unit of prayer consisting of standing, bowing, and prostrations.
حانث (hānith): One who breaks an oath; the legal consequence is that expiation (kaffarah) becomes due.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling if a person swears to pray with the congregation but catches only one rak'ah?
A) The oath is not broken because he caught the prayer according to the hadith.
B) The oath is broken.
C) There is a disagreement; some say broken, others not.
D) He must repeat the prayer.

Key Takeaway
Catching a single rak'ah gives the virtue of congregation but does not fulfill an oath to pray the entire prayer with the congregation; catching the majority (three rak'ahs) leads to scholarly disagreement.
