Three Exceptions Where Sujud al-Sahw Suffices Even if Intentional
List and proof of three intentional omissions compensated by sujud al-sahw

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three exceptions where sujud al-sahw suffices even if the omission was intentional, and explain the dalil for each.

Core Idea
Three intentional omissions are remedied by sujud al-sahw, not i'adah.

In the Hanafi school, the default rule is that intentional omission of a wajib or rukn requires repeating the prayer (i'adah). However, there are three well-known exceptions where even intentional action is compensated by sujud al-sahw. This lesson examines these exceptions and the proofs that support them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule and the exceptions
Start by stating the general Hanafi rule: intentional omission of a wajib or rukn invalidates the prayer and requires i'adah. Then note that there are three cases where this rule is relaxed and sujud al-sahw suffices.
The exceptions are limited; not all intentional acts are covered.
2
List the three exceptions
From the source, extract the three cases: (1) intentionally leaving the first sitting (qa'dah ula) in a 3- or 4-rak'ah prayer; (2) intentionally delaying one prostration from its original rak'ah to a later rak'ah; (3) intentionally engaging in prolonged reflection that delays a pillar (rukn) until it is performed later.
These are mentioned with 'قيل' indicating an accepted view within the school.
3
Examine the dalil for the first exception
The source provides a hadith from Mughira ibn Shu'ba: when the imam stands after two rak'ahs, if he remembers before standing straight, he should sit; if he stands straight, he should not sit and should perform sujud al-sahw. This indicates that even intentional standing (by not sitting) is remedied by sujud.
This hadith is used as the basis and then qiyas is applied to the other two exceptions.
4
Understand the qiyas for the other two exceptions
The author states that on this hadith (delay of first sitting) all other delays are analogized. Thus delaying a prostration or reflecting excessively are treated similarly because they involve delaying a wajib or rukn without completely invalidating the prayer's structure.
The analogy rests on the common illa of 'delay of an obligatory element'.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute and the mufta bihi
Some Hanafi scholars initially held that these exceptions are not valid, but the majority and later fatwa collections accept them. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that these three intentional acts are compensated by sujud al-sahw.
This illustrates how later scholars can confirm exceptions within the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقيل الا في ثلاث ترک القعود الاول او تاخيــر سـجـدة من الركعة الاولى الى آخر الصلوة وتفكره عمدا حتى شغله عن . ترجمه : (۷۳۲) مگر بعضوں کے نزدیک تین مسئلوں میں سجدہ سہو ہے۔ اول : پہلا قعدہ چھوڑ نا، دوم: پہلی رکعت کا ایک سجدہ اخیر نماز تک مؤخر کرنا سوم: ایک رکن کے برابر قصداً متفکر رہنا کہ ایک رکن چھوٹ جائے۔ تشریح : تین مسئلے ایسے ہیں کہ جان کر بھی کرے گا تو سجدہ سہو سے نقصان پورا ہو جائے گا[1] چار رکعت کی نماز تھی اور قعدہ اولی جان کر چھوڑ دیا ، جو واجب ہے اس لئے اس کے لئے سجدہ کرے گا تو نماز ہو جائے گا [۲] دوسرا مسئلہ یہ ہے دوسرا سجدہ پہلے سجدے کے ساتھ کرنا واجب ہے، اس نے دوسرا سجدہ پہلے سجدے کے ساتھ نہیں کیا بلکہ دوسری رکعت میں یا تیسری رکعت میں کیا تو اس تاخیر رکن. (۷۳۳) ويُسنّ الاتيان بسجود رد السهو بعد السلام ويكتفى بتسليمة واحدة عن يمينه في کے نقصان کو سجدہ سہو کرنے سے پورا کیا جاسکتا ہے۔ [۳] بھول کر ایک رکن ادا کرنے تک سوچتا رہا تو سجدہ سہو واجب نہیں ہے، کیونکہ اس میں انسان مجبور ہے، لیکن جان کر ایک رکن ادا کرنے تک سوچتا رہا جس کی وجہ سے اس رکن کی تاخیر ہوئی اس لئے سجدہ سہو سے نقصان پورا کیا جاسکتا ہے۔ وجه (۱) قعدہ اولی کی تاخیر سے سجدہ سہو واجب ہوتا ہے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے، اس پر سب کی تاخیر کو قیاس کریں ۔ عن مغيرة بن شعبة قال قال رسول الله الله اذا قام الامام في الركعتين فان ذكر قبل ان يستوى قائما فليجلس فان استوى قائما فلا يجلس ويسجد سجدتي السهو . (ابو داؤد شریف ، باب من نسی ان بیتشهد وهو جالس ،ص ۲۵۵، نمبر ۱۰۳۶ار دار قطنی ، باب الرجوع الى القعود قبل استتمام القیام ج اول ص ۳۶۷ نمبر ۱۴۰۳) اس حدیث میں قعدہ اولی کے چھوڑنے سے سجدہ سہو لازم ہوا۔ (۲) اس قول تابعی میں بھی ہے۔ عن الزهري في الرجل يسهو في الصلوة ان استوى قائما فعليه السـجـدتـان ، و ان ذكر قبل أن يعتدل قائما فلا سهو عليه - ( مصنف ابن ابی شبیۃ ، ۲۴۹ ، من کان یقول: اذالم يستقم قائما فلیس علیه سھو ، ج اول ص ۱۳۹۰، نمبر ۴۴۹۱ ) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ بیٹھنے کے قریب ہو تو سجدہ سہو نہ کرے اور کھڑا ہو گیا ہو تو سجدہ سہو کرے۔
And it is said except in three: leaving the first sitting, or delaying a prostration from the first rak'ah to the end of the prayer, and deliberately reflecting until it keeps him from... Translation: (732) But according to some, in three cases there is sujud al-sahw. First: leaving the first sitting. Second: delaying one prostration of the first rak'ah to the end of the prayer. Third: deliberately reflecting to the extent of a pillar that a pillar is missed. Explanation: There are three matters such that even if one does them intentionally, the deficiency can be compensated by sujud al-sahw. [1] It was a four-rak'ah prayer and he intentionally left the first sitting, which is wajib; so he will perform sujud and the prayer will be valid. [2] The second matter: performing the second prostration together with the first is wajib; he did not perform the second with the first but in the second or third rak'ah; then this delay... [3] If he forgetfully kept reflecting until performing a pillar, then sujud al-sahw is not wajib because the person is compelled; but if he deliberately kept reflecting until performing a pillar, causing delay of that pillar, then the deficiency can be compensated by sujud al-sahw. Proof (1): Delay of the first sitting makes sujud al-sahw wajib; for this there is this hadith, and on this analogize all delays. From Mughirah ibn Shu'bah: he said the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'When the imam stands up after two rak'ahs, if he remembers before standing straight, let him sit; if he stands straight, he should not sit and perform two prostrations of forgetfulness.' (Abu Dawud, bab man nasi an yatashahhad, p.255, no.1036; al-Daraqutni, bab al-ruju' ila al-qu'ud, vol.1, p.367, no.1403). This hadith makes sujud al-sahw necessary for leaving the first sitting. (2) This saying of a tabi'i also: from al-Zuhri concerning a man who forgets in prayer: 'If he stands straight, then upon him are two prostrations; if he remembers before standing straight, then no forgetfulness upon him.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, 249, man kana yaqul: idha lam yastaqim qa'iman falaysa 'alayhi sahw, vol.1, p.1390, no.4491). This athar shows that if near sitting, do not do sujud al-sahw; if he has stood, do sujud al-sahw.
Source pages p. 36

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute (some say) about three exceptions where intentional action is still remedied by sujud al-sahw. These are: (1) intentionally leaving the first sitting (qa'dah ula) in a prayer with more than two rak'ahs; (2) intentionally delaying a prostration from its original rak'ah to a later one; (3) intentionally engaging in prolonged reflection (tafakkur) that delays a pillar (rukn) until it is performed later. In these cases, the deficiency is considered similar to forgetfulness because of the nature of the act. The proofs include a hadith from Mughirah about standing after two rak'ahs and a saying of al-Zuhri distinguishing between standing straight and not yet straight. The Hanafi response to potential objections is that these cases are exceptions to the general rule, and analogy (qiyas) is used to extend the same ruling to other delays.

Key Terms
القعدة الأولى (al-qa'dah al-ūlā): The first sitting after the second rak'ah in a prayer of three or four rak'ahs.
سجود السهو (sujud al-sahw): Two prostrations performed to compensate for certain errors in prayer.
الإعادة (i'adah): Repeating the prayer from the beginning due to an invalidating error.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In which of the following cases does the Hanafi school allow sujud al-sahw even if the action was intentional?
A) Reciting al-Fatihah loudly instead of silently.
B) Delaying one prostration from the first rak'ah to the third rak'ah.
C) Adding an extra ruk'u'.
D) Forgetting to recite tashahhud completely.

Key Takeaway
Intentional omission of the first sitting, delaying a prostration, or prolonged reflection that delays a pillar are three exceptions where sujud al-sahw suffices instead of i'adah.

Sunnah Timing of Sujud al-Sahw: After Salām with One Salām
Ruling that the sunnah is to perform sujud al-sahw after salām, with one salām to the right.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah method for sujud al-sahw and identify the ruling when performed before salām.

Core Idea
The sunnah is to give one salām, then prostrate, then give a second salām; doing otherwise is valid but disliked.

The timing of sujud al-sahw (prostration for forgetfulness) is a matter of sunnah. The Hanafi school emphasizes following the Prophet's practice as recorded in authentic hadith. This lesson clarifies the preferred sequence and the ruling if one deviates from it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? The timing of sujud al-sahw relative to the salām. The sunnah is to perform it after the first salām.
The ruling is sunnah muakkadah (emphasized sunnah).
2
Locate the dalil
What proof does the author cite? The hadith of Imran ibn Husayn where the Prophet forgot a rak'ah, completed it, then gave salām, performed sujud, then gave salām again.
The hadith is from Muslim, Bukhari, and others.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the hadith prove the ruling? The explicit sequence (salām, sujud, salām) is taken as the sunnah method.
The Prophet's action is the proof.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Do other schools differ? Some schools consider sujud before salām as sunnah; Hanafis hold after salām as sunnah, and doing before is makruh tanzihi.
The Hanafi position is based on the hadith sequence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويُسنّ الاتيان بسجود رد السهو بعد السلام ويكتفى بتسليمة واحدة عن يمينه . ترجمه : (۷۳۳) مسنون یہ ہے کہ جب سجدہ سہو کرے سلام کے بعد کرے، اور مسنون روایت یہ ہے کہ ایک ہی جانب دائیں جانب سلام پھیرے، پس اگر سلام سے پہلے ہی سجدہ کر لیا تو مکروہ تنزیہی ہے۔ تشریح : مسنون یہ ہے کہ پہلے دائیں جانب ایک سلام پھیرے پھر سجدہ سہو کرے، اس کے بعد دوسرا سلام پھیرے، لیکن اگر پہلے سلام سے پہلے ہی سجدہ کر لیا تب بھی جائز ہے، کیونکہ حدیث سے ثابت ہے، البتہ ہمارے نزدیک یہ مکروہ تنزیہی ہے۔ وجه : (۱) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ پہلے سلام کیا پھر سجدہ کیا پھر سلام کیا ۔ عن عمران بن حصين قال سلم رسول الله صلى الله عل في ثلاث ركعات من العصر ثم قام فدخل الحجرة فقام رجل بسيط اليدين فقال اقصرت الصلوة يا رسول الله فخرج مغضبا فصلى الركعة التي كان ترك ثم سلم ثم سجد سجدتي السهو ثم سلم (مسلم شريف ، باب فصل من ترک الرکعتین اونحوها فلیتم مابقی و یسجد سجدتین بعد التسلیم، ص۲۳۳، نمبر ۱۲۹۴/۵۷۴ر بخاری شریف ، باب هل یا خذ الامام اذا اشک بقول الناس ، ص ۹۹ نمبر ۷۱۴ ترمذی شریف ، باب ما جاء فی الامام نبض فی الرکعتین ناسیا ص ۸۳ نمبر ۳۶۴ را ابو داؤد شریف، باب السهو فی السجدتین ، ص ۱۵۳، نمبر (۱۰۱۸) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ کوئی واجب بھول جائے تو سلام کرے پھر سجدہ سہو کرے پھر سلام پھیرے۔
And it is sunnah to perform the prostration of forgetfulness after the salām, and to suffice with one salām to his right. Translation: (733) It is sunnah that when performing sujud al-sahw, do it after salām, and the sunnah narration is that he turns one salām to the right side only. So if he prostrates before salām, it is makruh tanzihi. Explanation: It is sunnah to first turn one salām to the right, then do sujud al-sahw, then turn another salām. But if he prostrated before the first salām, it is still permissible because it is proven by hadith; however in our school it is makruh tanzihi. Proof: (1) In this hadith, he first gave salām, then prostrated, then gave salām. From Imran ibn Husayn: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) gave salām after three rak'ahs of Asr, then entered his house; a man with outstretched hands said: Has the prayer been shortened? The Prophet came out angrily, prayed the missed rak'ah, gave salām, performed two prostrations of forgetfulness, then gave salām. (Muslim, bab fadl man tarak al-rak'atayn, p.233, no.1294; Bukhari, bab hal ya'khudh al-imam idha ishtabah, p.99, no.714; Tirmidhi, bab ma ja'a fi al-imam yandaf' fi al-rak'atayn, p.83, no.364; Abu Dawud, bab al-sahw fi al-sajdatayn, p.153, no.1018). This hadith shows that if one forgets a wajib, he should give salām, then prostrate, then give salām again.
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage gives the sunnah method for sujud al-sahw: it should be performed after the first salām (to the right only), then after sujud, a second salām is given. Doing sujud before any salām is makruh tanzihi (disliked but not forbidden). The proof is the well-known hadith of Imran ibn Husayn where the Prophet forgot a rak'ah, completed it, then gave salām, then prostrated, then gave salām again. This establishes the sequence as sunnah. The Hanafi position is clear: the sunnah method is preferred, but sujud before salām is still valid, though disliked.

Key Terms
مكروه تنزيهي (makrūh tanzīhī): Disliked but not prohibited; doing sujud before salām is makruh tanzihi, meaning it is valid but contrary to the preferred method.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hadith cited in this lesson, what sequence did the Prophet (peace be upon him) follow after he prayed the missed rak'ah?
A) He gave salām, then prostrated, then gave salām again.
B) He prostrated, then gave salām, then prostrated again.
C) He gave salām, then left.
D) He made two prostrations, then gave salām.

Key Takeaway
The sunnah sequence for sujud al-sahw is: salām (one side), sujud, salām (again); doing otherwise is valid but disliked.

Ruling on Performing Sujud al-Sahw After Salam
Ruling on timing of sujud al-sahw with prophetic evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the timing of sujud al-sahw, distinguish between performing it after and before salam, and cite the prophetic evidence for the preferred sequence.

Core Idea
The sunnah is to perform sujud al-sahw after salam; doing it before is makruh tanzihan.

Sujud al-sahw (prostration for forgetfulness) compensates for unintentional omissions or delays in prayer. A key question is when to perform it: before or after the final salam? The Hanafi school has a clear preference based on Prophetic practice, and this passage presents the ruling along with its evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage rules that sujud al-sahw after salam is sunnah; if done before, it is makruh tanzihan.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary evidence is the hadith of Imran ibn Husayn and the hadith of Mughirah ibn Shu'bah.
Both hadith are cited in the passage.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The explicit sequence (salam → sujud → salam) indicates the recommended order.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Other schools may have different views; the Hanafi position is the most sound (al-asahh).
The passage mentions 'al-asahh' indicating the preferred view.
5
Understand the nuance
One salam to the right suffices, and the ruling applies even if one forgets a wajib.

باب سجود السهو
رکن. (۷۳۳) ويُسنّ الاتيان بسجود رد السهو بعد السلام ويكتفى بتسليمة واحدة عن يمينه في
کے نقصان کو سجدہ سہو کرنے سے پورا کیا جاسکتا ہے۔ [۳] بھول کر ایک رکن ادا کرنے تک سوچتا رہا تو سجدہ سہو واجب نہیں ہے، کیونکہ اس میں انسان مجبور ہے، لیکن جان کر ایک رکن ادا کرنے تک سوچتا رہا جس کی وجہ سے اس رکن کی تاخیر ہوئی اس لئے سجدہ سہو سے نقصان پورا کیا جاسکتا ہے۔
وجه (۱) قعدہ اولی کی تاخیر سے سجدہ سہو واجب ہوتا ہے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے، اس پر سب کی تاخیر کو قیاس کریں ۔ عن مغيرة بن شعبة قال قال رسول الله الله اذا قام الامام في الركعتين فان ذكر قبل ان يستوى قائما فليجلس فان استوى قائما فلا يجلس ويسجد سجدتي السهو . (ابو داؤد شریف ، باب من نسی ان بیتشهد وهو جالس ،ص ۲۵۵، نمبر ۱۰۳۶ار دار قطنی ، باب الرجوع الى القعود قبل استتمام القیام ج اول ص ۳۶۷ نمبر ۱۴۰۳) اس حدیث میں قعدہ اولی کے چھوڑنے سے سجدہ سہو لازم ہوا۔ (۲) اس قول تابعی میں بھی ہے۔ عن الزهري في الرجل يسهو في الصلوة ان استوى قائما فعليه السـجـدتـان ، و ان ذكر قبل أن يعتدل قائما فلا سهو عليه - ( مصنف ابن ابی شبیۃ ، ۲۴۹ ، من کان یقول: اذالم يستقم قائما فلیس علیه سھو ، ج اول ص ۱۳۹۰، نمبر ۴۴۹۱ ) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ بیٹھنے کے قریب ہو تو سجدہ سہو نہ کرے اور کھڑا ہو گیا ہو تو
سجدہ سہو کرے۔
ترجمه : (۷۳۳) مسنون یہ ہے کہ جدہ ہو سلام کے بعد کرے، اور میچ روایت یہ ہے کہ ایک ہی جانب دائیں جانب سلام پھیرے، پس اگر سلام سے پہلے ہی سجدہ کر لیا تو مکروہ تنزیہی ہے۔
تشریح : مسنون یہ ہے کہ پہلے دائیں جانب ایک سلام پھیرے پھر سجدہ سہو کرے، اس کے بعد دوسلام پھیرے، لیکن اگر پہلے
سلام سے پہلے ہی سجدہ کر لیا تب بھی جائز ہے، کیونکہ حدیث سے ثابت ہے، البتہ ہمارے نزدیک یہ مکروہ تنزیہی ہے۔ وجه : (۱) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ پہلے سلام کیا پھر سجدہ کیا پھر سلام کیا ۔ عن عمران بن حصين قال سلم رسول الله صلى الله عل في ثلاث ركعات من العصر ثم قام فدخل الحجرة فقام رجل بسيط اليدين فقال اقصرت الصلوة يا رسول الله فخرج مغضبا فصلى الركعة التي كان ترك ثم سلم ثم سجد سجدتي السهو ثم سلم (مسلم شريف ، باب فصل من ترک الرکعتین اونحوها فلیتم مابقی و یسجد سجدتین بعد التسلیم، ص۲۳۳، نمبر ۱۲۹۴/۵۷۴ر بخاری شریف ، باب هل یا خذ الامام اذا اشک بقول الناس ، ص ۹۹ نمبر ۷۱۴ ترمذی شریف ، باب ما جاء فی الامام نبض فی الرکعتین ناسیا ص ۸۳ نمبر ۳۶۴ را ابو داؤد شریف، باب السهو فی السجدتین ، ص ۱۵۳، نمبر (۱۰۱۸) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ کوئی واجب بھول جائے تو سلام کرے پھر سجدہ سہو کرے پھر سلام پھیرے۔
الاصح . فان سجـد قبل السلام كره تنزيها
Chapter of Sujud al-Sahw (Prostration for Forgetfulness). Rule (733): It is recommended (sunnah) to perform sujud al-sahw after the salam, and one salam to the right is sufficient. ... The most correct (view): if he prostrates before the salam, it is disapproved (makruh tanzihan).
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the proper time for sujud al-sahw. The text begins by stating that it is sunnah to perform the two prostrations after the final salam, and it is sufficient to give one salam to the right. The Urdu commentary explains that if one forgets a rukn and thinks until completing it, sujud al-sahw is not obligatory because the person was compelled, but if he knowingly delayed the rukn, then the deficiency is made up by sujud al-sahw. The proof is given from the hadith of Mugheerah ibn Shu'bah, where the Prophet (saw) said: if the imam stands up after two rak'ahs, if he remembers before standing straight, he should sit; if he stands straight, he does not sit and performs sujud al-sahw. Also the statement of al-Zuhri: if one stands straight, he performs the two prostrations; if he remembers before being fully upright, no sujud. The translation clarifies: the sunnah is to perform sujud after salam, and the most reliable narration is that one salam to the right is sufficient. If one prostrates before salam, it is makruh tanzihan. The commentary further explains that the sunnah is to first give one salam to the right, then sujud, then another salam. However, if one prostrates before the first salam, it is still permissible due to a hadith, but according to our (Hanafi) view it is makruh tanzihan. The proof from the hadith of Imran ibn Husayn shows the Prophet (saw) did salam, then sujud, then salam. Thus when a wajib is forgotten, one should do salam, then sujud, then salam again. The final line states the most correct view: if he prostrates before salam, it is makruh tanzihan.

Key Terms
سجود السهو (sujud al-sahw): Two prostrations performed to compensate for forgetfulness in prayer.
مکروہ تنزیہی (makruh tanzihi): Disapproved but not sinful; doing it is disliked but the prayer is valid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling if one performs sujud al-sahw before the final salam?
A) It is haram and the prayer is invalid.
B) It is makruh tanzihan but the prayer is valid.
C) It is sunnah and more virtuous.
D) It is wajib to repeat the prayer.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi sunnah is to perform sujud al-sahw after the final salam, with one salam to the right, and doing it before is makruh tanzihan.

When Sujud al-Sahw Becomes Invalid: Three Situations
Lists three events after salam that remove the obligation of sujud al-sahw

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three events that invalidate sujud al-sahw and explain the hadith proof.

Core Idea
Sujud al-sahw is dropped if, after salam, the sun rises/reddens or an action breaks continuity.

In this lesson, we examine the conditions that can render sujud al-sahw invalid even before it is performed. Understanding these scenarios helps maintain the integrity of the prayer and ensures we do not perform acts of worship at prohibited times.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its default ruling
First, recall that sujud al-sahw is a sunnah muakkadah when a mistake occurs in prayer. This lesson deals with when this sunnah becomes invalid (saqit).
Sujud al-sahw is not obligatory; its dropping does not invalidate the prayer, but leaves a deficiency.
2
List the three invalidating events
From the text, identify the three specific situations after salam: sunrise in Fajr, sun reddening in Asr, and any action that prevents building (bina'), like speaking.
The first two are time-based prohibitions; the third is a general disruption.
3
Analyze the underlying principle
The common element is that these events sever the connection (bina') between the prayer and the sujud. Once severed, the sujud cannot be performed because the prayer is no longer continuous.
The Urdu commentary emphasizes: 'something that severs the sujud from the previous prayer'.
4
Examine the hadith proof
The text cites the hadith of Uqbah ibn Amir prohibiting prayer at sunrise, zenith, and sunset. Since sujud al-sahw is a form of prayer, it is also prohibited at those times, hence dropped.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut), but it is accepted in Hanafi fiqh.
5
Determine the practical outcome
In each case, the sujud is dropped. The worshiper then has two valid options: repeat the entire prayer, or consider it as performed with deficiency (i.e., accept the missing compensation).
This is the mufta bihi position.

الصلاة
الصلاة حتى
(734) Sujud al-sahw is dropped by the rising of the sun after salam in Fajr, and by its reddening in Asr, and by the occurrence of something that prevents building after salam. Translation: Sujud al-sahw becomes invalid by the sun rising after salam in Fajr, by the sun becoming red in Asr, or by the presence of an obstacle that prevents building after salam. Commentary: These three cases are based on the principle that if after salam something occurs that severs the sujud from the previous prayer and one cannot build upon it, then sujud al-sahw cannot be performed; rather, one must repeat the prayer or consider it performed with deficiency. [1] In Fajr, if the sun rises after salam before sujud, the prayer becomes invalid, so sujud cannot be joined; thus sujud is dropped, and one either repeats the prayer or considers it as performed with deficiency. [2] Similarly in Asr, if the sun becomes red, sujud cannot be joined. [3] Third, if after salam something like speaking occurs that ends the prayer, sujud cannot be joined. Proof: The hadith of Uqbah ibn Amir that the Prophet forbade prayer at three times: when the sun rises until it is high, when it is at its zenith until it declines, and when it becomes yellow until it sets. Also, sujud al-tilawah is of the rank of prayer, and to avoid resemblance to disbelievers it is disliked. The hadith of Amr ibn Abasah: pray Fajr, then refrain until sunrise, etc.
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding when sujud al-sahw becomes invalid. It states three situations: (1) after salam in Fajr prayer, if the sun rises before performing the sujud, the sujud is dropped because the prayer is no longer valid; (2) after salam in Asr prayer, if the sun becomes red (i.e., approaches sunset), similarly the sujud is dropped; (3) after salam, if something occurs that prevents 'building' (bina')—meaning an action that breaks the continuity of the prayer, such as speaking—then the sujud is also dropped. The Urdu commentary explains the underlying principle: if after salam something happens that cuts off the link between the sujud and the original prayer, one cannot perform the sujud because the prayer is already invalidated. In each case, one must either repeat the entire prayer or consider it completed with the deficiency (i.e., without wajib compensation). The proof is given from the hadith of Uqbah ibn Amir prohibiting prayer at sunrise, zenith, and sunset. Since sujud al-sahw is part of the prayer, it is also prohibited at those times. Additionally, the hadith of Amr ibn Abasah mentions refraining from prayer at sunrise because the sun rises between the horns of Shaytan and disbelievers prostrate to it. The text also notes that sujud al-tilawah (prostration of recitation) is of the same rank as prayer, so avoiding it at those times prevents resemblance to disbelievers.

Key Terms
ساقط (saqit): Dropped, invalid; the obligation or sunnah is no longer applicable.
مانع البناء (mani' al-bina): Something that prevents building upon the prayer, i.e., an action that breaks the continuity after salam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Sujud al-sahw should be performed immediately before the sun fully sets.
B) Sujud al-sahw is dropped and one must repeat the prayer or consider it deficient.
C) Sujud al-sahw is still valid because the prayer was before salam.
D) The prayer becomes invalid and must be repeated with sujud.

Key Takeaway
Sujud al-sahw becomes invalid if, after salam, the sun rises/reddens or an action severs continuity; one then either repeats the prayer or accepts it as deficient.

Sujud al-Sahw Dropped by Sunrise, Redness, or Obstacle After Salam
Ruling on conditions that drop sujud al-sahw after salam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three conditions that drop sujud al-sahw after salam and explain the principle of bina' that underlies them.

Core Idea
Sujud al-sahw after salam requires bina'; if an obstacle severs it, the sujud is dropped.

This ruling addresses a practical scenario: you finish your prayer, realize you need to perform sujud al-sahw, but before you do, something happens that breaks the connection to your prayer. When does this happen, and what should you do? The Hanafi school provides clear guidance based on the prohibition of prayer at sunrise and sunset, and the concept of bina' (building on the previous act). Let's explore the three obstacles and the evidence behind them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three obstacles
From the text, list the specific cases that drop sujud al-sahw: sunrise after salam in Fajr, redness after salam in Asr, and any obstacle that prevents bina' (e.g., speaking).
The obstacle must occur after salam but before performing sujud al-sahw.
2
Understand the principle of bina'
Bina' means building or connecting the sujud to the preceding prayer. If an obstacle severs this connection, the sujud cannot be performed.
If bina' is possible, sujud is performed after salam; if not, it is dropped.
3
Analyze the proof (hadith)
The hadith of 'Uqbah ibn 'Amir forbids prayer at sunrise and sunset. The hadith of 'Amr ibn 'Abasah explains that at these times disbelievers prostrate to the sun, so Muslims avoid sujud to prevent resemblance.
Sujud al-sahw is considered a form of prayer, so the prohibition applies.
4
Apply the ruling
In each case, determine the consequence: sujud is dropped, and the prayer must be repeated or considered complete with deficiency.
The prayer itself may become invalid (as with sunrise) or disconnected (as with speaking).

تین اوقات میں نماز پڑھنا مکروہ ہے۔ (۲) سجدہ تلاوت نماز کے درجے میں ہے اور کفار کے ساتھ تشابہ نہ ہو جائے اس لئے یہ مکروہ ہے اس کے لئے حدیث کا اشارہ یہ ہے۔ قال عمرو بن عبسة السلمى .... فقلت : يا نبي الله أخبرني عما علمك الله و أجهله ، أخبرني عن الصلاة ؟ قال : صل صلاة الصبح ، ثم اقصر عن ) حتى تطلع الشمس حتى ترتفع ، فانها تطلع . تطلع بين قرنی شیطان ، و حينئذ يسجد لها الكفار ، ثم صل ، فان الصلاة مشهودة محضورة ، حتى يستقل الظل بالرمح ، ثم أقصر عن الصلاة فان حيئنذ تسجر جهنم ، فاذا اقبل الفيء فصل ، فان الصلاة مشهودة محضورة حتى تصلى العصر ، ثم اقصر عن الصلاة حتى تغرب الشمس فانها تغرب بين قرني الشيطان و حينئذ يسجد لها الكفار۔ (مسلم شریف ، باب اسلام عمر و بن عبستہ ۔ ابواب صلاة المسافرین ،ص ۱۳۳۴، نمبر ۱۹۳۰/۸۳۲ سنن نسائی ، باب النھی عن الصلاة بعد العصر ص ۷۹، نمبر ۵۷۳) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ اس وقت کفار سورج کو سجدہ کرتے ہیں اسلئے مسلمانوں کو سجدہ نہیں کرنا چاہئے ۔
If he prostrates before salam, it is makruh tanzihi. (734) And sujud al-sahw is dropped by sunrise after salam in Fajr, and by its redness in Asr, and by the presence of something that prevents building (bina') after salam. Translation: (734) And sujud al-sahw is dropped in Fajr by sunrise after salam, and in Asr by sunset's redness, or after salam by the occurrence of such an obstacle that prevents building. Explanation: These three matters are based on the principle that if after making salam for sujud al-sahw something appears that is a hindrance, cutting off sujud al-sahw from the previous prayer and one cannot build upon it, then after that event one cannot perform sujud al-sahw. Rather, one should repeat the prayer or consider that the prayer was performed with deficiency. [1] First matter: In Fajr, after salam for sujud al-sahw and before performing sujud al-sahw, the sun rose, causing the prayer to become invalid. Now, since the prayer is invalid, he cannot join sujud al-sahw with what preceded, so sujud al-sahw must be omitted. He should either repeat the prayer or consider the prayer as performed with deficiency. [2] Similarly, in Asr prayer, after salam the sun became red, so he cannot join sujud al-sahw with what preceded, so sujud al-sahw is dropped. [3] Third matter: After salam, such an obstacle occurred, e.g., speaking, which ended the prayer, so sujud al-sahw cannot be joined with what preceded, so sujud al-sahw is dropped. Therefore, he should repeat the prayer later or consider it complete with deficiency. Proof: The prayer ends with sunrise. For this, there is a hadith: I heard 'Uqbah ibn 'Amir al-Juhani say: There are three times when the Messenger of Allah ﷺ forbade us to pray or bury our dead: when the sun rises until it is high; when the sun is at its zenith until it declines; and when the sun inclines towards setting until it sets. (Muslim, Book of Times Forbidden for Prayer, p. 1334, no. 1929/831; Abu Dawud, Book of Burial at Sunrise and Sunset, p. 466, no. 3192; Tirmidhi, Book of Dislike of Prayer over a Funeral, p. 249, no. 1030) This hadith states that prayer in three times is makruh. (2) Sujud al-tilawah is of the same rank as prayer, and to avoid resemblance to disbelievers, it is makruh. This is indicated by the hadith: 'Amr ibn 'Abasah al-Sulami said: I said: O Prophet of Allah, tell me about what Allah has taught you and I do not know. Tell me about prayer. He said: Pray the morning prayer, then refrain from prayer until the sun rises and is high, for it rises between the horns of the devil, and at that time the disbelievers prostrate to it. Then pray, for the prayer is witnessed and attended, until the shadow becomes equal to the spear. Then refrain from prayer, for at that time Hell is stoked. Then when the shadow leans, pray, for the prayer is witnessed and attended, until you pray 'Asr. Then refrain from prayer until the sun sets, for it sets between the horns of the devil, and at that time the disbelievers prostrate to it. (Muslim, Book of Islam of 'Amr ibn 'Abasah, Chapters on Prayer of Travelers, p. 1334, no. 1930/832; Nasa'i, Book of Prohibition of Prayer after 'Asr, p. 79, no. 573) This hadith says that at that time the disbelievers prostrate to the sun, so Muslims should not prostrate.
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the Hanafi school regarding sujud al-sahw (prostration of forgetfulness) being dropped after salam. The matn states that if one deliberately prostrates before salam, it is makruh tanzihi. Then it explains that sujud al-sahw is dropped by sunrise after salam in Fajr prayer, by redness of the sun after salam in Asr prayer, and by the occurrence of any obstacle after salam that prevents building upon the previous prayer. The commentator elaborates three scenarios: (1) sunrise after salam in Fajr invalidates the prayer, so sujud al-sahw cannot be performed and the prayer must be repeated or accepted as deficient; (2) redness after salam in Asr has the same effect; (3) any action like speaking after salam also severs the connection, dropping the sujud. The proof comes from hadiths prohibiting prayer at sunrise, sunset, and zenith, and the hadith of 'Amr ibn 'Abasah explaining that at these times disbelievers prostrate to the sun, so Muslims avoid sujud to prevent resemblance. This ruling is based on the principle that once an obstacle occurs after salam, the original prayer is disconnected, and sujud al-sahw cannot fix it.

Key Terms
سجود السهو (sujud al-sahw): A prostration performed to compensate for errors (sahw) in prayer
مانع (mani'): An obstacle that prevents building (bina') upon the previous prayer
بنا (bina'): Building or connecting the sujud of forgetfulness to the preceding prayer

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When is sujud al-sahw dropped after salam in Fajr prayer?
A) When the sun becomes red
B) When the sun rises
C) When a person speaks
D) When the time for Fajr ends

Key Takeaway
Sujud al-sahw after salam requires connection (bina') to the preceding prayer; if an obstacle like sunrise, redness, or speech severs that connection, the sujud is dropped and the prayer must be repeated or accepted as deficient.

The Follower is Bound by the Imam's Forgetfulness
Ruling with evidence from hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that the follower must perform sujud al-sahw when the imam forgets, and distinguish between the imam's and follower's forgetfulness.

Core Idea
The imam's forgetfulness binds the follower; the follower's forgetfulness does not affect the imam.

In congregational prayer, the imam acts as a guarantor (dhamin) for the prayer's validity. This lesson explains how forgetfulness (sahw) by the imam obligates the follower to perform prostration of forgetfulness (sujud al-sahw), while the follower's own forgetfulness is covered by the imam. The ruling is supported by two key hadiths.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
What is the hukm (legal ruling) for the follower when the imam forgets? The passage states that the follower is bound (lāzim) by the imam's forgetfulness.
The ruling is that the follower must perform sujud al-sahw if the imam does.
2
Understand the rationale
The imam is called a dhamin (guarantor). This means the imam's prayer actions guarantee the followers' prayer. Therefore, when the imam forgets, his forgetfulness is attributed to the entire congregation.
The principle of damān (guarantee) is central in Hanafi fiqh for congregational prayer.
3
Examine the first hadith
The hadith of Abdullah ibn Lujainah: The Prophet ﷺ forgot and stood after two rak'ahs without sitting. When he completed, he performed sujud al-sahw before taslim, and the companions followed him.
This hadith demonstrates that the followers must follow the imam even in compensatory actions.
4
Examine the second hadith
The hadith from Umar: 'There is no forgetfulness upon the one behind the imam. If the imam forgets, then upon him and those behind him is the forgetfulness.' This explicitly states the obligation on the follower due to the imam's forgetfulness.
The second hadith also clarifies that the follower's own forgetfulness does not obligate sujud on the imam.
5
Contrast with the opposite case
If the follower forgets alone, the imam is not obligated to perform sujud al-sahw. The imam's prayer is valid and the follower's forgetfulness is covered ('the imam suffices for him').
This asymmetry highlights the imam's role as dhamin.

Source Text

(735) And the follower is bound by the forgetfulness of his imam, not by his own forgetfulness. Translation: (735) The follower is bound by the imam's forgetfulness, not by his own. Explanation: If the imam forgets, the follower also must perform sujud al-sahw because the imam is the guarantor. But if the follower forgets, the imam is not obligated. Proof (1) The imam is the guarantor, so when the imam performs sujud al-sahw due to his forgetfulness, the follower must follow him even if he (the follower) did not forget. (2) The evidence is the hadith of 'Abdullah ibn Lujainah: He said: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ led us in prayer, then after two rak'ahs he stood without sitting, and the people stood with him. When he completed his prayer and we waited for the taslim, he said takbir and performed two prostrations while sitting before the taslim, then he said salam. (Abu Dawud, Book of One Who Stands After Two Rak'ahs and Did Not Recite Tashahhud, p. 155, no. 1034; Tirmidhi, Book of What is Related About the Imam Who Forgets Two Rak'ahs, p. 83, no. 365; Muslim, Book of When One Forgets to Sit in the Two Rak'ahs, Let Him Prostrate Two Prostrations Before Salam, p. 211, no. 570) In this hadith, the imam had forgetfulness, so the followers also had to follow him in sujud. This shows that the follower is bound by the imam's forgetfulness. (3) And from 'Umar from the Prophet ﷺ: 'There is no forgetfulness upon the one behind the imam. If the imam forgets, then upon him and those behind him is the forgetfulness. If the one behind the imam forgets, there is no forgetfulness upon him, and the imam suffices for him.' (Daraqutni, Book of No Sujud on the Follower, But Sujud is Required for Imam's Forgefulness, vol. 1, p. 365, no. 1398; Bayhaqi, Book of Those Behind the Imam Not Performing Sujud al-Sahw, vol. 2, p. 495, no. 3884) This proves that the follower's forgetfulness does not obligate sujud on the imam, but the imam's forgetfulness obligates sujud on the follower.
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This passage establishes a key principle in Hanafi congregational prayer: the follower (ma'mum) is bound by the imam's forgetfulness (sahw), but the imam is not bound by the follower's forgetfulness. The commentator explains that the imam is a guarantor (dhamin) for the prayer. Therefore, if the imam forgets and performs sujud al-sahw, the follower must follow him even if the follower did not forget personally. However, if the follower forgets, the imam's prayer is not affected, and the imam does not need to perform extra sujud. The proof includes the hadith of 'Abdullah ibn Lujainah, where the Prophet ﷺ forgot and performed sujud, and the companions followed him. Another hadith from 'Umar explicitly states that there is no forgetfulness upon the follower; the imam's forgetfulness is sufficient. This ruling emphasizes the imam's responsibility and the follower's dependency.

Key Terms
ضامن (dhamin): Guarantor; the imam guarantees the prayer's validity on behalf of the followers
مقتدی (muqtadi): The follower in congregational prayer
سهو (sahw): Forgetfulness in prayer requiring compensation

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Remain silent without sujud
C) Perform his own separate sujud
D) Leave the congregation

Key Takeaway
The follower must follow the imam's sujud al-sahw because the imam is a guarantor (dhamin).

Masbuq's Sujud al-Sahw: Following the Imam and Personal Forgetfulness
Rulings on masbuq performing sujud al-sahw with imam and for personal errors

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the order of sujud al-sahw for a masbuq and explain when he performs it for his own forgetfulness.

Core Idea
The masbuq follows the imam in sujud al-sahw, then completes his prayer; his own forgetfulness requires separate sujud.

This passage clarifies two distinct rulings for the masbuq (latecomer) regarding sujud al-sahw. First, during the imam's prayer, the masbuq must join the imam in sujud al-sahw before completing his own missed rak'ahs. Second, if the masbuq forgets during his own rak'ahs after the imam's salutation, he must perform sujud al-sahw for himself. The text also highlights that the lahiq (one who joined before the final sitting) does not perform sujud for his own forgetfulness, as he is still under the imam's prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
What is being ruled upon? The masbuq's performance of sujud al-sahw. Ruling: wajib to follow the imam, and wajib to do sujud for his own forgetfulness.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the general principle from practice of the companions: the masbuq is a follower (muqtadi) during the imam's prayer, so he must follow; after the imam finishes, he prays independently and his forgetfulness requires sujud.
The dalil is ahad, based on practice.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The masbuq's state as a follower obligates him to follow the imam in all actions, including sujud al-sahw. For his own forgetfulness, his independent prayer after the imam's salutation makes him responsible for his own errors.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some schools may require the masbuq to perform sujud after completing his prayer, but the Hanafi position (mufta bihi) is to do it with the imam first.
The distinction between masbuq and lahiq is also noted.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The relied-upon position is from Zahir al-Riwayah: the masbuq performs sujud with the imam, then stands to complete his missed rak'ahs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۷۳۶) ويسجد المسبوق مع امامه ثم يقوم بقضاء ما ترجمه : (۷۳۶) اور مسبوق امام کے ساتھ سجدہ کر کے پھر کھڑے ہو اور جو چھوٹ گئی ہو اس کو قضا کرے۔ تشريح : مثلا کوئی آدمی تیسری رکعت میں امام کے شریک ہوا، اور یہ مسبوق بن گیا، اور امام پر سجدہ سہو تھا تو مسبوق امام کے ساتھ سجدہ سہو کرے، اس کے بعد اپنی نماز کھڑا ہو کر پوری کرے۔ وجه : مسبوق امام کا مقتدی ہے اس لئے اس کے ساتھ سجدہ سہو کرے، اور اس کے بعد اس کی اپنی نماز پوری کرے۔ ترجمه : (۷۳۶) اور اگر مسبوق اپنی رکعت میں سہو کرے تو اس کے لئے سجدہ سہو کرے۔ ہاں لاحق نہ کرے۔ تشریح : مثلا مسبوق تیسری رکعت میں امام کے ساتھ ملا، اب پہلی پہلی اور دوسری رکعت جب پڑھ رہا تھا تو اس میں سہو ہو گیا ، تو
(736) And the masbuq performs sujud with his imam, then stands and completes what he missed. Translation: (736) The masbuq performs sujud with the imam, then stands and completes what he missed. Explanation: For example, a person joins the imam in the third rak'ah, becoming a masbuq. If the imam has forgetfulness (sahw), the masbuq performs sujud al-sahw with the imam, then stands and completes his own prayer. Proof: The masbuq is a follower of the imam, so he performs sujud with him, then completes his own prayer. Translation (second): (736) And if the masbuq forgets in his own rak'ahs, he performs sujud al-sahw for his own forgetfulness; but the lahiq does not. Explanation: For example, a masbuq joins the imam in the third rak'ah, and while he was performing his own first and second rak'ahs, he forgot. So he should perform sujud al-sahw for himself.
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This passage gives two rulings regarding the masbuq (latecomer) and sujud al-sahw. First, if the imam has forgetfulness, the masbuq must perform sujud al-sahw with the imam before completing his own missed rak'ahs. After the imam's salutation, the masbuq stands to complete the remainder of his prayer. This is because the masbuq is a follower during the imam's prayer, so he must follow the imam in sujud. Second, if the masbuq himself forgets during his own rak'ahs (the ones he prays after the imam has finished), he must perform sujud al-sahw for his own forgetfulness. The text notes a distinction: the 'lahiq' (a person who arrives late but joins before the imam's salutation) does not perform sujud al-sahw for his own forgetfulness in the presence of the imam? Actually the text says 'haan lahiq na kare' meaning 'the lahiq does not do'. This indicates that the lahiq is treated differently: his forgetfulness is covered by the imam's prayer. The ruling underscores the separation between the masbuq's role during the imam's prayer and after he becomes independent.

Key Terms
مسبوق (masbuq): A person who joins the congregation after the imam has started, missing some rak'ahs
لاحق (lahiq): A person who joined the imam before the final sitting but after some rak'ahs
قضاء (qada'): To make up missed parts of prayer after the imam's salutation

Key Takeaway
The masbuq must follow the imam in sujud al-sahw during the imam's prayer, then independently perform sujud for his own forgetfulness in his own rak'ahs.

Follower's Obligation Due to Imam's Forgetfulness
Ruling: follower bound by imam's sahw, not vice versa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling regarding the follower's obligation to perform sajdah sahw due to the imam's forgetfulness, and explain the evidence from the hadith.

Core Idea
The imam's sahw obligates him and his followers; the follower's individual sahw does not.

This lesson examines a key rule in congregational prayer: who is responsible when forgetfulness occurs. The Hanafi school holds that the imam is the guarantor (ḍāmin) of the prayer, so his sahw affects all followers, but a follower's sahw is absorbed by the imam's responsibility. We will explore the textual proof from the Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling and Its Subject
Read the matn: 'ويلزم الماموم بسهوا امامه لا بسهوه'. It states that the follower is bound by the imam's forgetfulness, not his own. Identify what act this applies to: the obligation of sajdah sahw.
The ruling is specific to congregational prayer.
2
Locate the Dalil (Evidence)
The commentator cites two hadith: (1) The hadith of Ibn Buḥayna where the Prophet ﷺ forgot and performed sajdah sahw, and the followers followed. (2) A hadith from Dāraqutnī stating that the follower is not liable for sahw, but the imam's sahw binds both. Identify these as the proofs.
The first hadith is in Abu Dawud, Tirmidhi, Muslim.
3
Trace the Wajh al-Dalalah (How the Proof Proves the Ruling)
In Ibn Buḥayna's hadith, the Prophet acted as imam and forgot. He performed sajdah sahw, and the people (followers) stood with him and presumably followed the sajdah. This indicates that the followers are obligated to follow the imam's sahw. The second hadith explicitly states that the imam's sahw is upon him and those behind him.
The Prophetic action is a Sunnah that establishes obligation (wujub) in Hanafi usul.
4
Note the Ikhtilaf (Scholarly Disagreement)
The Hanafi position is that both imam and followers must perform sajdah sahw due to the imam's forgetfulness. Some other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) may hold that only the imam is obligated. Understand that this is a legitimate ikhtilaf.
The cross-madhhab status is mukhtalaf fih.
5
Apply the Ruling to a Concrete Scenario
Consider a Hanafi imam who accidentally stands after two rak'ahs. He performs sajdah sahw before taslim. The followers must follow him. If a follower alone forgets a sunnah, no sajdah is required from either.
The imam's role as ḍāmin ensures unity of the congregation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويلزم الماموم بسهوا امامه لا بسهوه
It is binding upon the follower due to the forgetfulness of his imam, not due to his own forgetfulness.
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This passage states the ruling that if the imam forgets, the followers are required to perform sajdah sahw, but if a follower forgets, it does not affect the imam. The commentator explains that the imam is the guarantor (ḍāmin) of the prayer's validity. Two proofs are cited: (1) The hadith of Ibn Buḥayna where the Prophet ﷺ forgot and stood after two rakʿahs, and the people stood with him, then he performed sajdah sahw before taslim. This shows the followers follow the imam's sahw. (2) A hadith from Dāraqutnī: 'He who is behind the imam is not liable for sahw, but if the imam forgets, it is upon him and those behind him; if one behind forgets, it is not upon him, and the imam is sufficient.' Thus, the follower's sahw does not obligate the imam.

Key Terms
الماموم (al-ma'mūm): The person praying behind the imam, i.e., the follower.
سهوا (sahwan): Forgetfulness in prayer that requires sajdah sahw.
ضامن (ḍāmin): Guarantor; the imam is responsible for the prayer’s validity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Only the imam
B) Only the followers
C) Both imam and followers
D) Neither

Key Takeaway
The imam's forgetfulness in prayer obligates both him and his followers to perform sajdah sahw, based on the Prophetic practice and the imam's role as guarantor.

Masbuq's Sajdah Sahw with the Imam
Ruling: masbuq does sajdah sahw with imam, then completes missed rak'ahs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for a masbuq when the imam performs sajdah sahw and explain the proof.

Core Idea
The masbuq must follow the imam in sajdah sahw, then complete his own missed rak'ahs.

In congregational prayer, if the imam forgets and performs sajdah sahw, the latecomer (masbuq) is obliged to follow him. This lesson explains the ruling and its basis in the follower's duty.

Guided Path
1
Identify the masbuq
The masbuq is a latecomer who joined the imam after the first rak'ah. He is considered a muqtadi (follower) for the remainder of the prayer.
His status as follower is key.
2
State the ruling
When the imam performs sajdah sahw, the masbuq must perform it with him. He does not wait until after the imam's taslim.
This is wajib according to the Hanafi school.
3
Explain the proof
The masbuq is a muqtadi, and the imam is appointed to be followed. The hadith states, 'The imam is appointed to be followed, so do not differ from him.' This includes sajdah sahw.
The proof is general obedience to the imam.
4
Describe the subsequent action
After performing sajdah sahw with the imam, the masbuq stands up and completes the rak'ahs he missed. He does not sit for tashahhud with the imam.
His prayer is completed independently after the imam's taslim.

Masbuq and Lahiq: Sajdah Sahw in Missed Rak'ahs
Ruling: masbuq does sajdah for own sahw; lahiq does not

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for sajdah sahw for the masbuq and lahiq, and explain the underlying principle of the imam as guarantor.

Core Idea
The masbuq prays alone in his qada'; his forgetfulness requires sajdah. The lahiq is still with the imam; his forgetfulness is covered.

This passage clarifies a key distinction in congregational prayer: when a latecomer (masbuq) makes up missed rak'ahs, he prays independently and must perform sajdah sahw if he forgets. In contrast, one who was with the imam but missed some rak'ahs due to a valid excuse (lahiq) is treated as still following the imam, so he does not perform sajdah sahw for his own forgetfulness. The difference rests on whether the qada' is considered independent or attached to the imam's prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories: masbuq and lahiq
A masbuq enters the congregation late and misses one or more rak'ahs with the imam. A lahiq starts with the imam but misses some rak'ahs due to a reason (e.g., wudu breaking) and rejoins later. Understand how each makes up missed rak'ahs.
2
Determine the nature of qada' for each
For the masbuq, the qada' rak'ahs are performed independently after the imam's salam. For the lahiq, the qada' is performed after the imam's salam but while still considered in congregation; he does not recite Quran in those rak'ahs and is bound by the imam's rulings.
The lahiq’s connection to the imam remains intact.
3
Apply the rule of sajdah sahw
Since the masbuq prays independently, his own forgetfulness triggers the obligation of sajdah sahw. The lahiq, being still attached to the imam, is covered by the imam’s sajdah sahw (if any) and does not perform sajdah for his own forgetfulness.
The imam is the guarantor (damin) for the lahiq’s qada'.
4
Note the thamarah (practical consequence)
If a masbuq forgets in his qada', he must perform sajdah sahw. If a lahiq forgets, he does nothing; if the imam forgot and did sajdah, the lahiq follows.
This avoids confusion in application.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو سهـا الـمسبوق فيـمـا يقضيه سجد له ايضا لا اللاحق واذا... لا اللاحق
And if the masbuq forgets in what he makes up, he performs sajdah for it as well, not the lahiq.
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This passage distinguishes between the masbuq and the lahiq. The masbuq, when making up his missed rak'ahs, prays independently (not behind the imam for those rak'ahs). Therefore, if he forgets during those rak'ahs, he must perform sajdah sahw on his own. The lahiq, however, is one who was with the imam from the start but missed some rak'ahs due to a reason (e.g., wudu breaking), then rejoins. When making up his missed rak'ahs, he is still considered to be in the imam's followership, so he does not perform sajdah sahw for his own sahw, because the imam is his guarantor. This is similar to the rule that the lahiq does not recite Quran in those rak'ahs.

Key Terms
مسبوق (masbūq): A latecomer who joins the congregation after the imam has started and misses one or more rak'ahs. He completes his missed rak'ahs independently after the imam's salam.
لاحق (lāḥiq): One who started the prayer with the imam but missed some rak'ahs due to a legitimate excuse (e.g., wudu breaking) and later rejoins to complete them.
سجود السهو (sujūd al-sahw): Prostration performed to compensate for forgetfulness or error during prayer. It is wajib according to the Hanafi school when certain omissions or additions occur.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) He does not perform sajdah sahw
B) He performs sajdah sahw
C) He follows the imam's sajdah
D) He repeats the prayer

Key Takeaway
The masbuq must perform sajdah sahw for his own forgetfulness in qada' rak'ahs; the lahiq does not, because the imam is his guarantor.

No Sajdah Sahw for Imam in Jumu'ah and Eid Prayers
Ruling: imam omits sajdah sahw in Jumu'ah and Eid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that the imam omits sajdah sahw in Jumu'ah and Eid prayers and explain the rationale based on avoiding fitnah.

Core Idea
In Jumu'ah and Eid, the imam skips sajdah sahw to prevent disorder—public interest overrides the usual rule.

This passage from Thamaratun Najah presents a unique Hanafi ruling: the imam does not perform the prostration of forgetfulness (sajdah sahw) in the Friday and Eid congregational prayers. The rationale is practical: large crowds in these prayers would cause confusion if the imam performed extra prostrations. Thus, the ruling is an application of istihsan (juristic preference) to preserve order and avoid fitnah (disorder).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is sajdah sahw in Jumu'ah and Eid prayers. The ruling is that the imam does not perform it.
2
Understand the basis (dalil aqli)
The reasoning is that performing sajdah sahw would cause tanāfur (disorder/confusion) among the congregation, especially in the back rows, due to large crowds.
3
Recognize the legal principle
This is an application of istihsan, where the general rule that sajdah sahw is required when forgetfulness occurs is set aside for a specific public benefit.
4
Note the scope
The ruling applies only to the imam in these specific prayers; the followers also do not perform it, and the prayer remains valid even if forgetfulness occurred.
5
Contrast with other schools
Some other madhhabs (e.g., Shafi'i) require sajdah sahw in all prayers; this is a Hanafi specificity based on public interest.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يأتى الامام بسجود السهو في الجمعة والعيدين
And the imam does not perform the sajdah of forgetfulness in Jumu'ah and the two Eids.
Source pages p. 40

Commentary
This ruling is based on practical consideration: In Jumu'ah and Eid prayers, due to large crowds, performing sajdah sahw would cause confusion and disorder (fitnah) in the back rows. Therefore, the imam omits it, and if forgetfulness occurs, the prayer is valid without sajdah sahw. This is an application of istihsan (juristic preference) considering public interest.

Key Terms
التنافر (al-tanāfur): Disorder or confusion in the rows.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The imam does not perform sajdah sahw in Jumu'ah and Eid prayers to avoid disorder (fitnah), an application of istihsan.

Forgetting the First Tashahhud: When to Return
Ruling: return to tashahhud if not yet fully standing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on forgetting the first tashahhud and apply the boundary rule of being fully upright to determine whether to return or compensate with sajdah sahw.

Core Idea
Return to the first tashahhud only if you have not yet straightened your back; otherwise, complete the prayer and perform sajdah sahw.

The first tashahhud is wajib in the Hanafi school. Forgetting it triggers a choice: return if you are still near the sitting position, but once you are fully upright, the moment has passed and you must compensate with the prostration of forgetfulness. This lesson unpacks the precise boundary and the proof behind it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
Pinpoint the act: forgetting the first tashahhud in an obligatory prayer of three or four rak'ahs. The ruling: it is wajib to return to the sitting position as long as you have not become fully upright (istawā qā'iman).
The ruling applies only to the first sitting (qa'dah ūlā), not the final tashahhud.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith of Mughirah ibn Shu'bah (Abu Dawud, Daraqutni) which explicitly states: if the imam remembers before standing fully upright, let him sit; if he is already upright, do not sit but perform sajdah sahw.
This is a sunnah ahad, transmission is zanni but meaning is clear.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'falyajlis' (let him sit) indicates obligation (wujub) in Hanafi usul. The conditional 'if before fully upright' sets the boundary — after that, the command is 'lā yajlis' (do not sit).
Hanafi principle: al-amr yufīdu al-wujūb.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) consider the first tashahhud as sunnah, not wajib, so the ruling would be different. However, the Hanafi position is based on this explicit hadith and is mufta bihi.
The practical difference: Hanafi requires return (or sajdah sahw), while Shafi'i would not require either.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The commentary declares this ruling sahih (correct) and it is from the zahir riwayah. The hadith is explicit and not contradicted, so it is relied upon.
The Hanafi position is consistent with the literal text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن سها عن القعود الاول من الفرض عاد مالم يستو قائما
And whoever forgets the first sitting in the obligatory prayer returns as long as he has not become fully upright standing.
Source pages p. 40

Commentary
This ruling concerns forgetting the first tashahhud (al-qa'dah al-ūlā) which is wajib. The person should return to the sitting position as long as he has not fully stood up. Once he is upright, he should not return; instead, he continues and performs sajdah sahw at the end. The hadith of Mughirah ibn Shu'bah is cited: 'When the imam stands up after two rak'ahs, if he remembers before he is fully upright, let him sit; if he becomes fully upright, let him not sit, and let him perform two prostrations of forgetfulness.' This is the relied-upon (zahir riwayah) position.

Key Terms
القعود الاول (al-qu'ūd al-awwal): The first sitting after two rak'ahs in a prayer of three or more rak'ahs.
استوى قائما (istawā qā'iman): Became fully upright standing, i.e., after rising from bowing or from prostration.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Continue standing
B) Return to sitting
C) Perform sajdah sahw immediately
D) Repeat the prayer

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling: return to the first tashahhud is wajib only if remembered before fully standing straight; otherwise, sajdah sahw compensates.

Sajdah al-Sahw for Masbuq and Lahiq
Ruling on when a latecomer performs prostration of forgetfulness

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between a masbuq and a lahiq and state whether sajdah al-sahw is required for each.

Core Idea
A masbuq's makeup is independent; a lahiq's makeup is still behind the imam — only the masbuq prostrates for forgetfulness.

In congregational prayer, not all latecomers are the same. The Hanafi school distinguishes between a masbuq and a lahiq when it comes to sajdah al-sahw. This lesson explains why only the masbuq performs prostration of forgetfulness in his makeup prayer, while the lahiq does not, supported by a hadith of the Prophet (s).

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories
The text defines masbuq as one who joins late and completes his missed rak'ahs after the imam's salam. Lahiq is one who started with the imam but missed some rak'ahs due to a nullifier and then rejoins the imam before the imam's salam.
2
State the ruling for each
The matn states: if a masbuq forgets in his makeup, he performs sajdah al-sahw; a lahiq does not.
Sajdah al-sahw is wajib for the masbuq.
3
Understand the reasoning
The masbuq's makeup is considered his own prayer, separate from the imam, so forgetfulness requires prostration. The lahiq, even during makeup, is still in a state of following the imam (muqtadi), and since the imam has no forgetfulness, the lahiq does not prostrate.
4
Locate the dalil
The author cites the hadith of Mughirah, where the Prophet (s) caught one rak'ah with the congregation and then stood to complete his prayer after the imam's salam, indicating that a latecomer's completion is independent.
The dalil is a hadith from Sahih Muslim.
5
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith shows that the Prophet (s) completed his prayer after the imam's salam without the imam's involvement, proving the independence of the masbuq's makeup. By qiyas, if forgetfulness occurs in that independent portion, sajdah al-sahw is wajib.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب سجود السهو
ثمرة النجاح جلد ٢ سبق بــه (۷۳۷) ولو سهـا الـمسبوق فيـمـا يقضيه سجد له ايضا لا اللاحق
چونکہ یہ مسبوق کی اپنی نماز ہے اس میں امام اس کے آگے نہیں ہے اس لئے اس میں سہو ہو گیا ہومسبوق اس کا سجدہ کرے گا ۔۔اور لاحق اس کو کہتے ہیں کہ شروع سے امام کے ساتھ تھا اور درمیان میں اس کی رکعت چھوٹی ہے، مثلا پہلی رکعت میں امام کے ساتھ تھا پھر حدث پیش آیا اس لئے دوسری اور تیسری رکعت میں امام کے ساتھ نہیں رہا، پھر چوتھی رکعت میں امام کے ساتھ شریک ہو گیا ، اب دوسری اور تیسری رکعت پڑھنے لگا تو سہو ہو گیا، اس سہو کا سجدہ نہیں کرے گا، کیونکہ گویا کہ امام اس کے سامنے ہے، اور یہ امام کی اقتداء میں نماز پڑھ رہا ہے، اور امام پر سہو نہیں ہے اس لئے لاحق پر بھی سجدہ سہو نہیں ہو گا ، جس طرح ان رکعتوں کے ادا کرتے وقت لاحق پر قرآت نہیں ہے۔
وجه : مسبوق اپنی نماز پوری کرتے وقت وہ امام کے پیچھے نہیں ہے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ قال المغيرة فاقبلت معه حتـى نــجــد الـنـاس قد قدموا عبد الرحمن بن عوف فصلی لهم فادرک رسول الله علم احدى الركعتين فصلى مع الناس الركعة الآخرة فلما سلم عبد الرحمن بن عوف قام رسول الله الله يتم صلاته - (مسلم شریف ، باب تقديم الجماعة من يصلی بهم اذاتاً خرا الامام ولم یخافوا مفسدة بالتقديم، ص ۱۸۰ نمبر ۴۲۱ ۹۴۹)
اس حدیث میں ہے کہ مسبوق اپنی نماز پوری کرے گا۔
Chapter of Prostration of Forgetfulness. Thamaratun Najah Volume 2, preceded by (737): And if the masbuq forgets in what he completes, he prostrates for it as well, not the lahiq. Because this is the masbuq's own prayer, in which the imam is not ahead of him, so if forgetfulness occurs, the masbuq performs its prostration. The lahiq is the one who was with the imam from the beginning but missed some rak'ahs in between, e.g., he was with the imam in the first rak'ah, then a nullifier occurred, so he did not stay with the imam in the second and third rak'ahs, then he joined the imam in the fourth rak'ah. Now when he begins to pray the second and third rak'ahs, if forgetfulness occurs, he does not perform prostration for it, because it is as if the imam is in front of him and he is praying in the imam's following, and there is no forgetfulness upon the imam, so there is no prostration of forgetfulness upon the lahiq either, just as there is no recitation upon the lahiq when performing those rak'ahs. The point: When the masbuq completes his prayer, he is not behind the imam. For this is the hadith: Al-Mughirah said: I went with him until we found the people had put forward 'Abd al-Rahman ibn 'Awf to lead them. The Messenger of Allah (s) caught one of the two rak'ahs and prayed the final rak'ah with the people. When 'Abd al-Rahman ibn 'Awf said the salam, the Messenger of Allah (s) stood up to complete his prayer. (Muslim, Book of Precedence in Congregation, p. 180, no. 421, 949) This hadith indicates that the masbuq completes his prayer.
Source pages p. 40

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It distinguishes between two categories of latecomers in congregational prayer: the masbuq and the lahiq, regarding the obligation of sajdah al-sahw (prostration of forgetfulness). The ruling (matn) states: If a masbuq forgets in the part of prayer he makes up, he performs sajdah al-sahw for it; the lahiq does not. The commentary explains that a masbuq is one who joined the prayer late (after the first rak'ah) and completes his missed rak'ahs after the imam's salam—during this completion, he is not behind the imam, so if he forgets, he must prostrate. A lahiq, however, is one who started with the imam but missed some rak'ahs due to a nullifier (e.g., hadath), then rejoined later. When he makes up the missed rak'ahs, he is still considered to be following the imam, so if forgetfulness occurs, he does not prostrate because the imam has no forgetfulness. The proof is the hadith of Mughirah ibn Shu'bah, where the Prophet (s) caught one rak'ah and after the imam's salam stood to complete—showing that a masbuq's makeup is independent.

Key Terms
مسبوق (masbuq): A person who joins the congregational prayer late, missing one or more rak'ahs, and completes them after the imam's salam.
لاحق (lahiq): A person who started the prayer with the imam but missed some rak'ahs due to a nullifier, then rejoins and makes them up while still considered following the imam.
سجدہ سہو (sajdah al-sahw): Prostration of forgetfulness, two prostrations performed at the end of prayer to compensate for certain errors.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because his prayer is void due to the nullifier.
B) Because he is still considered to be following the imam, and the imam has no forgetfulness.
C) Because sajdah al-sahw is only for the imam.
D) Because his makeup rak'ahs are not part of the congregational prayer.

Key Takeaway
The distinction between masbuq and lahiq determines the requirement of sajdah al-sahw: only the masbuq performs it because his makeup is independent of the imam.

Imam Does Not Perform Sajdah al-Sahw in Jumu'ah and Eid
Ruling that imam skips prostration of forgetfulness due to crowd

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that the imam does not perform sajdah al-sahw in Jumu'ah and Eid prayers and explain that the prayer is valid without it due to the large crowd.

Core Idea
In large congregations, the imam's sajdah al-sahw is waived to avoid disturbance — the prayer is valid without it.

You already know that forgetfulness in prayer normally requires sajdah al-sahw (prostration of forgetfulness). But this rule is not absolute. The Hanafi school makes an exception for the imam in Jumu'ah and Eid prayers due to the large crowd. This lesson examines that exceptional ruling, which prioritizes congregational harmony over the usual obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is forgetfulness (sahw) during Jumu'ah or Eid prayer. The ruling is that the imam does not perform sajdah al-sahw.
2
Understand the normal obligation
Normally, unintentional omission of a wajib element in prayer requires sajdah al-sahw. This is wajib in the Hanafi school.
Sajdah al-sahw is a wajib compensation.
3
Recognize the exception
For Jumu'ah and Eid, the imam is exempted from performing sajdah al-sahw. The prayer is valid without it.
The exception is specific to these two prayers, not all large gatherings.
4
Identify the reason
The reason given is the huge crowd (bheed) – performing sajdah al-sahw would cause confusion and disturbance in the back rows.
The 'illah (effective cause) is preventing disorder.
5
Apply the ruling
In practice, if the imam forgets a wajib element in Jumu'ah or Eid, he does not perform sajdah al-sahw and continues; the prayer is valid.
This applies only to the imam; followers follow his lead.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۷۳۸) ولا يأتى الامام بسجود السهو في الجمعة والعيدين .
ترجمه : (۷۳۸ ) اور نماز جمعہ اور عیدین میں سہو ہونے سے امام سجدہ سہو نہ کرے۔
تشریح : نماز جمعہ اور عیدین میں بھیڑ بہت ہوتی ہے اس لئے سجدہ سہو کرنے سے پچھلی صف میں انتشار ہوگا اس لئے جمعہ اور عیدین میں سہو ہو جائے تو سجدہ سہو نہیں ہے، بغیر سجدہ کے نماز ہو جائے گی۔
(738) And the imam does not perform prostration of forgetfulness in Jumu'ah and the two Eids. Translation: (738) And in Jumu'ah and Eid prayers, when forgetfulness occurs, the imam does not perform sajdah al-sahw. Explanation: In Jumu'ah and Eid prayers, there is a great crowd, so performing sajdah al-sahw would cause disturbance in the back rows. Therefore, if forgetfulness occurs in Jumu'ah and Eid, there is no sajdah al-sahw; the prayer will be valid without prostration.
Source pages p. 40

Commentary
This is a ruling statement. The matn says: The imam does not perform sajdah al-sahw in Friday and Eid prayers. The commentary explains the reason: because of the large crowd, performing the extra prostrations would cause confusion and disturbance in the rear rows. Therefore, the prayer is valid without them. This is a concession (rukhsah) specific to these large gatherings. Note that this applies only to the imam; the followers do not perform sajdah al-sahw individually either, as they are following the imam.

Key Terms
الجمعة (al-Jumu'ah): The Friday congregational prayer, obligatory for men.
العيدين (al-'idayn): The two Eid prayers: Eid al-Fitr and Eid al-Adha.
سجود السهو (sajdah al-sahw): Prostration of forgetfulness, performed to compensate for unintentional omissions in prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is sajdah al-sahw not performed by the imam in Jumu'ah prayer?
A) Because forgetfulness never occurs in Jumu'ah.
B) Because it would cause disturbance in the crowded congregation.
C) Because the prayer is completed without it.
D) Because Jumu'ah is a short prayer.

Key Takeaway
In Jumu'ah and Eid prayers, the imam's obligation to perform sajdah al-sahw is waived to prevent disturbance; the prayer is valid without it.

Forgetting the First Sitting: When to Return in Obligatory Prayer
Ruling on when to return if one forgets the first tashahhud

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on returning to the first sitting when forgotten, apply the threshold of 'fully standing' (istawa qa'iman), and identify when sajdah al-sahw is required.

Core Idea
Return to the first sitting is wajib before fully standing; after, do not return but perform sajdah al-sahw.

Forgetting the first tashahhud is common. The Hanafi school gives a precise ruling based on how far one has stood. This lesson walks through the three scenarios and the evidence from hadith and athar, so you can apply the correct ruling in your prayer or when advising others.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The first sitting (al-qa'dah al-ula) is wajib in prayers of three or more rak'ah. Forgetting it triggers a need to return or compensate.
The ruling differs based on the degree of standing.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The hadith of Mughirah ibn Shu'bah in Sunan Abi Dawud: the Prophet (s) said that if the imam remembers before straightening up fully, he should sit; if he has straightened, he should not sit and must perform sajdah al-sahw.
This hadith is the core evidence for the threshold.
3
Apply the threshold: istawa qa'iman
The key phrase is 'istawa qa'iman' – fully upright. The ruling hinges on whether one has reached this state or not.
The text distinguishes three levels: closer to sitting, closer to standing, and fully standing.
4
Analyze the three scenarios
Scenario 1: Closer to sitting – return, no sajdah. Scenario 2: Closer to standing – return, sajdah wajib. Scenario 3: Fully standing – do not return, but if one mistakenly returns, prayer is valid with sajdah.
The 'al-sahih' view is that returning after fully standing does not invalidate the prayer.
5
Determine the consequence
Sajdah al-sahw becomes wajib when one returns after having moved substantially toward the next pillar (closer to standing). No sajdah if one was still close to sitting.
The athar of al-Zuhri and Anas support this distinction.

وجه : (۱) اسکی وجہ یہ ہے کہ چونکہ کھڑا نہیں ہوا تو ابھی کوئی زیادہ فرق نہیں پڑا ہے، اور ایسا سمجھو کہ وہ تھوڑ اسا بھی کھڑا نہیں ہوا۔
(۲) اس اثر میں اسکا ثبوت ہے۔ عن الزهري في الرجل يسهو في الصلوة ان استوى قائما فعليه السجدتان ، و ان ذكر قبل أن يعتدل قائما فلا سهو عليه - ( مصنف ابن ابی هیپه ۲۴۹ من کان یقول: اذالم يستقم قائما فلیس علیہ سکھو، ج اول ، ص ۱۳۹۰، نمبر ( ۴۴۹)
