(739) And whoever forgets the first sitting in obligatory prayer returns as long as he has not fully become upright, according to the apparent narration, and it is the most correct. Translation: (739) And whoever in obligatory prayer forgets the first sitting, then as long as he has not stood upright, he returns to it; the apparent narration is this and it is the most correct. Explanation: For example, he is praying a four-rak'ah obligatory prayer and forgot the first sitting, which is wajib. The apparent narration is that as long as he has not stood completely upright, he returns and sits. Reason (1) Because when he is close to sitting, its ruling is applied to him. (2) There is a hadith: From Mughirah ibn Shu'bah that the Messenger of Allah (s) said: 'When the imam stands after two rak'ahs, if he remembers before standing straight, let him sit; if he stands straight, let him not sit and perform two prostrations of forgetfulness.' (Abu Dawud, Chapter on One Who Forgets the Tashahhud While Sitting, p. 255, no. 1036) from this hadith it is understood that if he has not completely stood, he should sit, and if he has completely stood, he should not sit but perform sajdah al-sahw. (740) And the follower is like one praying nafl: he returns even if he has fully stood. (1 74) Then if he returns while he is closer to standing, he prostrates for forgetfulness; and if he is closer to sitting, there is no prostration upon him in the most correct view; and if he returns after fully standing, there is disagreement (the correct view is that the prayer is not invalid). Explanation: There are three situations: [1] He was close to sitting and remembered the sitting and sat, then no sajdah al-sahw is necessary because he sat before moving to another pillar. [2] He was close to standing but had not fully stood, then he sat, so sajdah al-sahw is necessary because he sat after moving to another pillar. [3] He fully stood, then he should complete the next rak'ah; if instead he sat, there is disagreement whether the prayer becomes invalid, but the correct narration is that it does not become invalid, only sajdah al-sahw is obligatory. The hadith of Abu Dawud above says not to return if fully standing, but if he does return, the prayer is not invalid because he did it to correct his prayer. Reason: (1) Because he did not actually stand much, as if he did not stand at all. (2) This athar supports it: From al-Zuhri concerning a man who forgets in prayer: if he stands straight, two prostrations are due; if he remembers before becoming straight standing, there is no forgetfulness upon him. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, no. 449) From this athar it is understood that if he is close to sitting, he does not make sajdah al-sahw, and if he has stood, he does. (3) There is another narration that he prostrates. Its proof is the athar of Anas ibn Malik that he moved to stand after two rak'ahs of 'Asr, so they glorified him, and he sat and performed two prostrations of forgetfulness while sitting. (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Chapter on One Who Forgets and Stands After Two Then Remembers Before...)
Source pages p. 40

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It addresses forgetting the first tashahhud (al-qa'dah al-ula) in obligatory prayers, a wajib act. The matn (739) states: if one forgets the first sitting and stands for the third rak'ah, one should return to sit as long as one has not fully straightened up (istawa qa'iman). This is the position of Zahir al-Riwayah and the most correct. The commentary explains that the first sitting is wajib, so if one forgets, one must return if still near sitting. The proof is the hadith of Mughirah from Abu Dawud: the Prophet (s) instructed that if the imam stands after two rak'ah and remembers before straightening up, he should sit; if he has already straightened, he should not sit but perform sajdah al-sahw. The next part (740) says the follower (muqtadi) is like one praying nafl: he should return even if fully standing. This is because the follower must follow the imam; even if he has fully stood, if the imam sits for sajdah al-sahw, the follower must sit to follow. The commentary clarifies this using the analogy of nafl where each two rak'ah is a separate unit, so returning is required. Then (741) discusses three scenarios: (1) If one is closer to sitting (i.e., not yet far from the ground) and returns, no sajdah al-sahw is needed because he had not fully committed to the next pillar. (2) If one is closer to standing (i.e., more than halfway up) and returns, sajdah al-sahw is wajib because he had already moved to the next pillar. (3) If one fully stands and then returns, there is ikhtilaf: the correct view is the prayer is not invalid, but sajdah al-sahw is wajib because he unnecessarily moved from the standing pillar. Additional proofs from athar of Zuhri and Anas are cited. The passage clarifies the nuanced ruling based on the degree of standing.

Key Terms
القعود الأول (al-qa'dah al-ula): The first sitting after two rak'ah in a prayer of three or more rak'ah, where tashahhud is recited. It is wajib.
استوى قائما (istawa qa'iman): Fully upright, standing straight after rising from bowing or prostration.
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwayah): The apparent or well-known narration from the founding imams, considered the primary source for rulings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the first sitting forgetting, when does sajdah al-sahw become wajib upon returning to sit?
A) When one returns before fully standing.
B) When one was closer to standing (more than halfway up) when returning.
C) When one was closer to sitting (less than halfway up) when returning.
D) When one fully stands and then returns.

Key Takeaway
Forgetting the first tashahhud is compensated by returning before fully standing (no sajdah) or by sajdah al-sahw if after fully standing; the prayer remains valid in both cases.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

Ruling on Muqtadi Returning to Sitting Due to Sajda al-Sahw
Ruling for muqtadi returning from standing due to sajda al-sahw

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a muqtadi who fully stands while the imam performs sajda al-sahw, explain the proof from qiyas and hadith, and identify the Shafi'i difference.

Core Idea
The follower must return to sitting even if fully stood – following the imam in sajda al-sahw is wajib.

This passage from Thamaratun Najah addresses a specific scenario in congregational prayer: the follower (muqtadi) forgets and stands up while the imam sits for the prostration of forgetfulness (sajda al-sahw). The Hanafi school, based on the zahir al-riwayah and analogy with voluntary prayer, rules that the follower must return to sitting even if he has fully completed standing. This ruling underscores the principle that following the imam is obligatory, and the follower's prayer is tied to the imam's actions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is the muqtadi standing up while the imam sits for sajda al-sahw. The ruling is that he must return to sitting even if fully stood.
This is the mufta bihi position from zahir al-riwayah.
2
Recognize the analogy with nafl prayer
The text compares the muqtadi to one performing nafl prayer where each two rak'ahs form an independent unit (shaf'). If one stands for the third rak'ah, he must return for tashahhud. Similarly, the follower must return to sit with the imam.
In nafl, sitting after every two is necessary.
3
Locate the hadith proof
The hadith from Abu Dawud (Bab al-ruju' ila al-qu'ud) states: if one has not fully stood, he sits; if fully stood, he does not sit but performs sajda al-sahw. The ruling for the muqtadi is analogized from this.
The hadith is ahad, so thubut and dalala are zanni.
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the follower should not return if fully stood but should continue and perform sajda al-sahw at the end.
The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) is that Hanafis return, Shafi'is do not.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب سجود السهو
قائما في ظاهر الرواية وهو الاصح (۷۴۰) والمقتدى كالمتنفل يعود ولو استتم قائما
باب الرجوع الى القعود قبل استمام القيام، ج اول ص ۱۳۶۷، نمبر ۱۴۰۳) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ بالکل کھڑا نہ ہوا تو بیٹھ جائے ۔ اور بالکل کھڑا ہو گیا ہوتو نہ بیٹھے بلکہ سجدہ سہو کر لے۔
ترجمه : ( ۷۴۰ ) اور مقتدی نفل پڑھنے والے کی طرح ہے کہ پورا کھڑا ہو گیا ہو تب بھی واپس لوٹے۔ تشریح : اس عبارت میں پریشانی ہے۔ نفل میں چار رکعت کی نیت کی ہو تب بھی ہر دور کعت الگ الگ شفع ہے اس لئے ہر قعدہ پر بیٹھنا ضروری ہے ، اس لئے اگر تیسری رکعت کے لئے بالکل کھڑا بھی ہو چکا ہے تب بھی قعدہ کے لئے بیٹھ جانا چاہئے ، اسی طرح سجدہ سہو کے لئے امام بیٹھ چکا ہے تو مقتدی کھڑا بھی ہو چکا ہے تو اس کو قعدہ کے لئے بیٹھ جانا چاہئے ، کیونکہ امام کی اقتداء ضروری ہے لغت : استم تم سے مشتق ہے، پورا کھڑا ہونا۔ یعود: واپس ہو جانا۔
Chapter of Prostration of Forgetfulness. Standing in the apparent narration and it is the most correct (740) and the follower is like one performing supererogatory prayer: he returns even if he has fully stood. (Reference: Chapter of returning to sitting before completing standing, volume 1 page 1367, number 1403) From this hadith it is understood that if he has not fully stood, he sits down, and if he has fully stood, he does not sit but performs the prostration of forgetfulness. Translation: (740) And the follower is like one performing nafl prayer: even if he has fully stood, he returns. Explanation: In this phrase there is confusion. In nafl, even if he intended four rak'ahs, every two rak'ahs are separate as shaf' (pair), so sitting after every two rak'ahs is necessary. Therefore, even if he has fully stood for the third rak'ah, he should sit down for the sitting. Similarly, if the imam sat for sajda al-sahw and the follower has stood, he should sit for the sitting because following the imam is obligatory. Lexicon: 'istamma' is derived from 'tamm': fully standing. 'ya'udu': he returns.
Source pages p. 41

Commentary
This passage from Thamaratun Najah presents the ruling on a follower (muqtadi) who forgets and stands up while the imam performs sajda al-sahw. The text states the relied-upon view (zahir al-riwayah) that the follower must return to sitting even if he has fully stood. The reasoning uses analogy (qiyas) with a voluntary (nafl) prayer: in nafl, even if one intends four rak'ahs, each pair is independent, so if one stands for the third rak'ah, he must return for the tashahhud after two. Similarly, the follower must return to sit with the imam. The hadith from Abu Dawud is cited as proof: if one has not fully stood, he sits; if fully stood, he does not sit but performs sajda al-sahw. The commentary clarifies that 'fully standing' means having completely risen to the standing posture. The follower follows the imam's action in sajda al-sahw, so he returns even if he stood. This is the correct view in the school.

Key Terms
سجود السهو (sujūd al-sahw): Prostration of forgetfulness performed to compensate for errors in prayer.
مقتدی (muqtadī): Follower in congregational prayer who follows the imam.
نفل (nafl): Voluntary supererogatory prayer.
استتمام (istimām): The act of completely rising to a standing posture.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi zahir al-riwayah, what should a muqtadi do if he forgets and fully stands while the imam is sitting for sajda al-sahw?
A) Continue standing and perform sajda al-sahw at the end alone.
B) Return to sitting regardless of having fully stood.
C) Return to sitting only if he had not fully stood; otherwise continue.
D) Remain standing and wait for the imam to finish.

Key Takeaway
The muqtadi must return to sitting even if fully stood because following the imam in sajda al-sahw is wajib.

Ruling on Returning to Sitting in Prayer: The Threshold for Sajda al-Sahw
Ruling with proof on sajda al-sahw

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi criterion for returning to sitting in prayer and determine whether sajda al-sahw is required based on whether the worshipper was closer to standing or sitting.

Core Idea
Sajda al-sahw is wajib only if the worshipper returns after having partially moved toward the next pillar; if still closer to the previous posture, no sajda is needed.

In this lesson, we examine the precise ruling regarding a common scenario: a worshipper forgets and begins to stand from the first tashahhud but then remembers and returns to sitting. When is sajda al-sahw required? The Hanafi school provides a nuanced criterion based on how far the transition to standing has progressed. We will walk through the three possible states, the primary proof from al-Zuhri, and a secondary narration from Anas, culminating in the mufta bihi position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three scenarios
The passage outlines three states: (1) closer to sitting, (2) closer to standing but not fully upright, (3) fully stood. For each, the ruling differs.
Memorize these three cases; they form the basis of the discussion.
2
Apply the threshold rule
Determine the hukm for each: no sajda when closer to sitting; wajib sajda when closer to standing; and for fully standing, there is ikhtilaf but the correct Hanafi view is that the prayer is not invalidated and sajda is still required.
The key criterion is 'closeness to standing' (qurb al-qiyam).
3
Examine the primary proof
Analyze the athar of al-Zuhri: 'If he comes fully to a standing posture (istawā qāiman), then two prostrations are due; if he remembers before becoming straight in standing (iʿtadala qāiman), then no sajda.' This establishes the threshold.
The terms istawā and iʿtadala are synonymous here.
4
Evaluate the secondary narration
The narration from Anas reports that even slight movement toward standing triggered sajda al-sahw. However, the correct view (al-aṣaḥḥ) is the first, as indicated by 'في الاصح' in the text.
This shows an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf resolved in favor of the al-Zuhri athar.
5
Understand the rationale
If the worshipper has not fully stood, the transition is incomplete; returning to sitting does not constitute a major disturbance requiring compensation beyond what the primary proof prescribes.
The rationale helps in analogical extension to similar cases.

Translation: (741) Then if he returns when he was closer to standing, he performs sajda al-sahw; and if he was closer to sitting, in the most correct narration, there is no sajda al-sahw upon him. And if he returns after having fully stood, there is a difference regarding the invalidity of the prayer (the correct view is that it does not become invalid). Explanation: Here there are three states. [1] He was close to sitting and the thought of sitting came and he sat down, then sajda al-sahw is not necessary because he sat before moving to another pillar. [2] He was close to standing but had not fully stood, and he sat down, then sajda al-sahw is necessary because he sat after having moved towards another pillar. [3] He fully stood, then he should complete the next rak'ah; if instead he sat, there is a difference as to whether the prayer is invalidated, but the correct narration is that it does not become invalid, only sajda al-sahw is required. The hadith of Abu Dawud above states that if fully stood, do not return; but if he returns, the prayer is not invalid because he did it to correct his prayer. Reason (1): Because since he did not stand, there is no big difference, and consider that he did not stand at all. (2) There is proof in this athar: from al-Zuhri concerning a man who forgets in prayer: if he comes fully to a standing posture, then two prostrations are due; but if he remembers before he becomes straight in standing, then no sajda upon him. (Mussanaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, 249, from those who said: if he does not become fully standing, there is no sajda upon him, volume 1, page 1390, number 449). From this athar it is understood that when closer to sitting, do not perform sajda al-sahw, and if he stood, he performs sajda al-sahw. (3) There is also another narration that he does perform sajda. Its proof is this athar: from Anas ibn Malik that he moved to stand in the two rak'ahs of 'Asr, so they subbaha (said Subhanallah) to him, so he sat, then performed two prostrations of forgetfulness while sitting. (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, chapter: who forgets and stands from two then remembers before... After he completed standing, the correction differed regarding invalidity of his prayer (742) And if he forgets the final sitting, he returns as long as he has not prostrated, and he prostrates for delaying the obligatory sitting. (743) And if he prostrates, his obligatory prayer becomes supererogatory, and he adds a sixth if he wishes, even in 'Asr, and a fourth in Fajr, and there is no dislike in adding in both according to the correct view. And he does not perform sajda al-sahw in the most correct view. ... (Urdu continuation)

Commentary
This passage clarifies the detailed ruling on returning to sitting after forgetting in prayer. The text presents three scenarios: (1) If one is closer to sitting and returns, no sajda al-sahw is needed because he did not actually move to the next pillar. (2) If he is closer to standing but not fully upright, and returns, sajda al-sahw is required because he partially shifted to the next action. (3) If he fully stands and then returns, there is ikhtilaf: according to the correct Hanafi view, the prayer is not invalidated because he intended to correct it, but sajda al-sahw becomes wajib even though the hadith suggests not returning. The proof includes an athar from al-Zuhri that distinguishes between fully standing and not. A second opinion from Anas suggests sajda al-sahw even upon slight movement, but the first view is preferred as the most correct narration. The commentary explains the rationale: not fully standing means no significant change.

Key Terms
استوى قائما (istawā qāiman): To become fully erect in the standing posture, indicating the completion of the transition from sitting to standing.
اعتدل قائما (i'tadala qāiman): To be straight in standing, synonymous with istawā qāiman.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) When one returns after having fully stood.
B) When one returns after being closer to standing but not fully upright.
C) When one returns after being closer to sitting.
D) Sajda al-sahw is never required when returning to sitting.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes three levels of transition in standing for sajda al-sahw: no sajda when closer to sitting, wajib when closer to standing, and wajib but prayer valid when fully stood.

Forgetting the Final Sitting and Standing Up
Ruling on forgetfully omitting the final tashahhud and standing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling when the final sitting is forgotten and the worshiper stands for an additional rak'ah, and explain the proof from hadith.

Core Idea
Forgetting the final sitting: return before the extra rak'ah's sajda; delay compensated by sajda al-sahw.

This passage deals with a common forgetfulness scenario in salah: omitting the final tashahhud and standing for the next rak'ah. The Hanafi school provides a precise rule on when to return and how to compensate. Understanding this rule depends on recognizing that the final sitting is fard and that an extra rak'ah before completing the fard's obligation is treated as nafl only after its sajda.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The worshiper forgets the final sitting and stands for the next rak'ah. The ruling: he must return as long as he has not prostrated the extra rak'ah, then perform sajda al-sahw for the delay.
2
Understand the basis
The final sitting is fard (obligatory). Omitting it means the fard obligation is unfulfilled; the extra rak'ah is considered nafl only after its sajda, so before that point the worshiper can abandon it.
Hanafi position: final sitting is fard (see issue 257).
3
Analyze the consequence
If he returns before sajda, the extra rak'ah is invalidated; he must sit, recite tashahhud, salam, and then perform sajda al-sahw. This corrects the prayer.
If sajda already performed, the extra rak'ah becomes a separate nafl and he must complete it with additional rakahs? (not covered here).
4
Note the proof from hadith
The hadith of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud: the Prophet (ﷺ) prayed five rak'ahs for Zuhr and performed sajda al-sahw after salam. This shows that an extra rak'ah added forgetfully does not invalidate the prayer but requires compensation.
The Hanafi school uses this to argue that the extra rak'ah is nafl and the fard remains incomplete; returning before sajda is preferred.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان سها عن القعود الاخير عاد مالم يسجد و سجد لتاخيره فرض القعود (۷۴۳)
ترجمه : (۷۴۲) اور اگر قعدہ اخیرہ کو بھول کر کھڑا ہو جائے تو جب تک سجدہ نہ کیا ہو بیٹھ جائے ، اور فرض قعدہ اخیرہ کی تاخیر کی وجہ سے سجدہ سہو کرے۔
تشریح : مثلا چار رکعت ظہر کا فرض پڑھ رہا تھا کہ قعدہ آخیرہ بھول گیا ، اس میں بالکل بیٹھا ہی نہیں اور پانچویں رکعت کے لئے کھڑا ہو گیا تو جب تک کہ پانچویں رکعت کا سجدہ نہ کیا ہو تو اسکے لئے یہ ہے کہ یہ واپس آکر بیٹھ جائے اور سجدہ سہو کرے۔ اسی طرح فجر کی نماز میں تیسری رکعت کے لئے کھڑا ہو گیا، اور مغرب کی نماز میں چوتھی رکعت کے لئے کھڑا ہو گیا اور قعدہ آخیرہ چھوڑ دیا، تو اسکے لئے یہ ہے کہ واپس آکر قعدہ آخیرہ میں بیٹھ جائے ۔ کیونکہ یہ قعدہ فرض ہے۔ وجه : (۱) باب صفۃ الصلوۃ کے مسئلہ نمبر۲۵۷ میں گزر گیا ہے کہ قعدہ اخیرہ فرض ہے اب اس کو چھوڑ کر پانچویں رکعت کی طرف گیا جو گویا کہ نفل ہوگی تو فرض کو چھوڑ کر نفل میں شامل ہوا ہے اس لئے جب تک پانچویں رکعت کا سجدہ نہ کیا ہو اور اس کو مضبوط نہ کیا ہواس کو چھوڑ کر قعدہ اخیرہ کی طرف لوٹ آئے اور قعدہ اخیرہ کر کے سلام پھیرے اور سجدہ سہو کرے (۲) اس حدیث میں اسکا ثبوت ہے عن عبد الله قال ان رسول الله لعل الله صلى الظهر خمسا فقيل له ازيد في الصلوة؟ قال وما ذاك ؟قال صليت خمسا فسجد سجدتين بعد ما سلم (بخاری شریف ، باب اذ اصلی خمسا ص ۱۹۶، نمبر ۱۲۲۶ مسلم شریف ، باب من صلی خمسا اونحوه، ص۲۱۲، نمبر ۱۲۸۳٫۵۷۲) اس حدیث میں پانچ رکعت پڑھنے پر آپ نے سجدہ سہو کیا ہے۔ اور پانچویں رکعت بریکار گئی
And if he forgets the final sitting, he returns as long as he has not prostrated, and he prostrates for delaying the obligatory sitting (743). Translation: (742) And if he forgets the final sitting and stands up, he sits down as long as he has not prostrated, and he performs sajda al-sahw due to delaying the obligatory final sitting. Explanation: For example, he was performing the four-rak'ah fard of Zuhr and forgot the final sitting, not sitting at all, and stood for the fifth rak'ah. As long as he has not prostrated the fifth rak'ah, he should return and sit and perform sajda al-sahw. Similarly, in Fajr prayer if he stands for the third rak'ah, and in Maghrib if he stands for the fourth rak'ah and omits the final sitting, he should return and sit for the final sitting because this sitting is fard. Reason (1): It has passed in the chapter on the description of prayer, issue number 257, that the final sitting is fard. Now, having left it and gone to the fifth rak'ah, which would become nafl, he has left the fard and entered into nafl. Therefore, as long as he has not prostrated the fifth rak'ah and strengthened it, he should leave it and return to the final sitting, then perform the final sitting, say salam, and perform sajda al-sahw. (2) There is proof in this hadith: from Abdullah (Ibn Mas'ud) that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) prayed Zuhr five rak'ahs. It was said to him: 'Has the prayer been increased?' He said: 'Why do you ask?' They said: 'You prayed five.' So he performed two prostrations after salam. (Bukhari, chapter: if one prays five, page 196, number 1226; Muslim, chapter: who prayed five or similar, page 212, number 1283/572). In this hadith, he performed sajda al-sahw upon praying five rak'ahs, and the fifth rak'ah was considered invalid.
Source pages p. 42

Commentary
This passage addresses the case of forgetting the final sitting (q'ada akhira) and standing up for the next rak'ah. The ruling is clear: if you realize before prostrating that extra rak'ah, you must return to the sitting position. This is because the final sitting is fard (obligatory) per the Hanafi school. By standing, you have begun a nafl rak'ah (since adding to a fard prayer turns the extra into nafl). But since the fard obligation remains unfulfilled, you must abandon the extra rak'ah before its sajda and return to complete the fard sitting. After completing the prayer with salam, you perform sajda al-sahw for the delay. The proof is the hadith of the Prophet (ﷺ) praying five rak'ahs for Zuhr; he performed sajda al-sahw after salam. This hadith shows that adding a rak'ah due to forgetfulness is compensated by sajda al-sahw, and the extra rak'ah is not counted. The commentary also notes the parallel in Fajr and Maghrib when exceeding the required number of rak'ahs.

Key Terms
قعدہ اخیرہ (q'adat al-akhīrah): The final sitting in prayer after the last rak'ah in which the tashahhud is recited.
فرض القعود (fard al-qu'ūd): The obligatory sitting (i.e., the final sitting).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case of forgetting the final sitting and standing for the next rak'ah, when must one return to the sitting?
A) Only if he has not yet fully stood.
B) Only if he has not yet performed the sajda of the extra rak'ah.
C) Anytime before salam.
D) He should not return but complete the extra rak'ah.

Key Takeaway
Forgetting the final sitting and standing up requires immediate return before the extra rak'ah's sajda, and then sajda al-sahw for the delay.

Transformation of Fard to Nafl Due to Extra Rakah
Ruling on transformation of fard to nafl after extra prostration

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when one prostrates an extra rak'ah after forgetting the final sitting, and apply it correctly to Zuhr, Asr, and Fajr prayers.

Core Idea
If you prostrate an extra rak'ah by mistake, the fard becomes nafl — add a rak'ah to make an even pair.

In this passage, we learn what happens when a worshipper, having forgotten the final sitting (tashahhud), stands up and prostrates an extra rak'ah. The ruling is a classic example of how Hanafi fiqh handles errors in prayer through transformation (inqilab) rather than invalidation. The fard prayer is converted into a nafl, and the worshipper must complete it as a valid voluntary prayer. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its justification, and the exceptional permission to pray nafl after Fajr and Asr in this scenario.

Guided Path
1
Identify the error and its consequence
The error is prostrating an extra rak'ah after forgetting the final sitting. The consequence is that the fard intention is overridden; the prayer becomes nafl.
2
Determine the corrective action
The worshipper must add another rak'ah to make an even number (e.g., 5 becomes 6, 3 becomes 4) so that the nafl is prayed in pairs (shaf').
The text says 'if he wishes' but it is necessary to avoid an odd number.
3
Understand the exceptional permission
This addition is allowed even after Fajr and Asr, when nafl is normally prohibited, due to necessity (darurah).
4
Confirm absence of extra prostrations
No sajda al-sahw is required for the added rak'ah; the prayer is valid as is.
The most correct view is no sajda.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فان سجد صار فرضه نفلا وضم سادسة ان شاء ولو في العصر ورابعة في الفجر ولا كراهة فى الضم فيهما على الصحيح. ولا يسجد للسهو في الاصح
ترجمه : : (۷۴۳ ) اور اگر سجدہ کر لیا ہوتو وہ فرض نماز نفل ہو جائے گی۔ اب اگر چاہے تو عصر وغیرہ میں چھٹی رکعت اور فجر میں چوتھی رکعت ملالے۔ اور صحیح روایت میں فجر اور عصر میں یہ ملانا مکروہ نہیں ہے، اور ا صبح روایت میں سجدہ سہو نہ کرے۔
تشریح : مثلا ظہر اور عصر میں پانچویں کا سجدہ کر لیا تو فرض کے ساتھ نفل ملالیا، اور قعدہ آخیرہ جو فرض ہے اس کو چھوڑ دیا ، اس لئے فرض نماز نفل بن جائے گی ، اس لئے ظہر میں چھٹی رکعت ملالے، اور فجر میں چوتھی رکعت ملالے تا کہ یہ شفع بن کر نماز مکمل ہو جائے ، اور ایک رکعت نماز باقی نہ رہے ۔ اس صورت میں اشکال یہ ہو گا کہ فجر کے بعد نفل نہیں ہے ، اسی طرح عصر کے بعد نفل نہیں ہے تو مزید رکعت ملا کر نفل کیسے بنائے ؟ تو مصنف فرما رہے ہیں کہ یہاں مجبوری کی صورت ہے اس لئے عصر کے بعد اور فجر کے بعد نفل
And if he prostrates, his fard becomes nafl, and he adds a sixth rak'ah if he wishes, even in 'Asr, and a fourth in Fajr, and there is no dislike in adding in both according to the correct view. And he does not perform sajda al-sahw in the most correct view. Translation: (743) And if he has performed the prostration, then his fard prayer becomes nafl. Now, if he wishes, he may add a sixth rak'ah in 'Asr etc., and a fourth in Fajr. And in the correct narration, this adding in Fajr and 'Asr is not disliked, and in another narration he does not perform sajda al-sahw. Explanation: For example, in Zuhr and 'Asr, if he prostrated the fifth, then he has mixed nafl with fard, and he has left the final sitting which is fard. Therefore the fard prayer becomes nafl. So in Zuhr he should add a sixth rak'ah, and in Fajr a fourth, so that it becomes a pair (shaf') and the prayer is completed, and no single rak'ah remains. In this case there is an issue: after Fajr there is no nafl, and similarly after 'Asr there is no nafl. So how can one add a rak'ah to make it nafl? The author says that here it is a situation of necessity, so nafl after Fajr and 'Asr is allowed in this case.
Source pages p. 42

Commentary
This passage deals with the consequence if one prostrates the extra rak'ah after forgetting the final sitting. The ruling: the fard prayer is transformed into a nafl (supererogatory) prayer because the fard obligation (the final sitting) was omitted, and the extra rak'ah became part of the prayer. To avoid having an odd number of rak'ahs (e.g., 5 in Zuhr), one adds another rak'ah to make it an even number (6), completing the nafl as two units (shaf'). In Fajr, from 3 rak'ahs one adds a fourth to make 2 pairs. This is a dispensation (rukhsah) due to necessity, even though nafl is normally not prayed after Fajr or 'Asr. The correct view (al-sahih) is that there is no dislike (karahah) in this situation, and no sajda al-sahw is required for the added rak'ah. The reasoning: the original intention was fard, but due to an error, the prayer now must be completed as nafl. The Hanafi school allows this to avoid wasting the performed rak'ahs.

Key Terms
ضم (ḍamm): Adding an extra rak'ah to the prayer to make an even number.
شفع (shaf'): A pair of rak'ahs; voluntary prayers are in pairs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on adding a sixth rak'ah in Zuhr after one has prostrated an extra fifth rak'ah due to forgetting the final sitting?
A) It is makruh and should be avoided.
B) It is permissible and recommended to form a complete pair.
C) It is invalid and the prayer must be repeated.
D) One should not add, but instead perform sajda al-sahw.

Key Takeaway
When an extra rak'ah is prostrated after forgetting the final sitting, the fard prayer becomes nafl, and one should add a rak'ah to complete a pair; this is permissible even after Fajr and Asr due to necessity.

Forgetting the Final Sitting: Return Before Prostration
Ruling on standing up after forgetting final sitting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when one forgets the final sitting and stands, and apply the condition of 'before prostration' to determine the correct action.

Core Idea
Forgetting the final sitting: return before the extra prostration; the fard must be performed before the supererogatory.

Prayer is a structured act, and every part has its place. Forgetting the final sitting (qa'dah akhirah) and standing for an additional rak'ah is a common human error. The Hanafi school provides a clear rule: as long as you have not yet prostrated the extra rak'ah, you must return to the sitting. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its evidence, and a minor difference within the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the forgetfulness
Recognize that the final sitting (qa'dah akhirah) was missed and the worshipper stood for an extra rak'ah. This can happen in any fard prayer.
The final sitting is fard (obligatory).
2
Determine the condition
Check whether the worshipper has prostrated the extra rak'ah. The ruling depends on this condition: if not prostrated, he must return; if already prostrated, he cannot return.
The condition is 'malam yasjud' (as long as he has not prostrated).
3
State the ruling
If he has not prostrated the extra rak'ah, he must return to the sitting, complete the final sitting (tashahhud), say salam, and then perform sajdah al-sahw.
Returning is wajib; sajdah al-sahw is also wajib for the delay.
4
Examine the evidence
The proof is from the hadith where the Prophet (ﷺ) prayed five rak'ah and performed sajdah al-sahw after salam. This shows that additional rak'ah can be compensated.
The final sitting is fard, so leaving it for a supererogatory action is not allowed before the extra prostration.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi difference
There is a narration that if he stood only slightly, sajdah al-sahw alone suffices. However, the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is to return.
The correct narration is the first as per the author.

Source Text

(۷۴۲) وان سها عن القعود الاخير عاد مالم يسجد و سجد لتاخيره فرض القعود
ان بیستم قائما عاد مجلس وسجد للسهو ، ج ثانی ص ۴۸۴ نمبر ۳۸۴۵) اس اثر میں ہے کہ تھوڑا سا اٹھے تو سجدہ سہوفر مایا، اس سے ثابت کرتے ہیں کہ سجدہ سہو کرے لیکن صحیح روایت پہلی ہے۔ ترجمه : (۷۴۲) اور اگر قعدہ اخیرہ کو بھول کر کھڑا ہو جائے تو جب تک سجدہ نہ کیا ہو بیٹھ جائے ، اور فرض قعدہ اخیرہ کی تاخیر کی وجہ سے سجدہ سہو کرے۔
تشریح : مثلا چار رکعت ظہر کا فرض پڑھ رہا تھا کہ قعدہ آخیرہ بھول گیا ، اس میں بالکل بیٹھا ہی نہیں اور پانچویں رکعت کے لئے کھڑا ہو گیا تو جب تک کہ پانچویں رکعت کا سجدہ نہ کیا ہو تو اسکے لئے یہ ہے کہ یہ واپس آکر بیٹھ جائے اور سجدہ سہو کرے۔ اسی طرح فجر کی نماز میں تیسری رکعت کے لئے کھڑا ہو گیا، اور مغرب کی نماز میں چوتھی رکعت کے لئے کھڑا ہو گیا اور قعدہ آخیرہ چھوڑ دیا، تو اسکے لئے یہ ہے کہ واپس آکر قعدہ آخیرہ میں بیٹھ جائے ۔ کیونکہ یہ قعدہ فرض ہے۔ وجه : (۱) باب صفۃ الصلوۃ کے مسئلہ نمبر۲۵۷ میں گزر گیا ہے کہ قعدہ اخیرہ فرض ہے اب اس کو چھوڑ کر پانچویں رکعت کی طرف گیا جو گویا کہ نفل ہوگی تو فرض کو چھوڑ کر نفل میں شامل ہوا ہے اس لئے جب تک پانچویں رکعت کا سجدہ نہ کیا ہو اور اس کو مضبوط نہ کیا ہواس کو چھوڑ کر قعدہ اخیرہ کی طرف لوٹ آئے اور قعدہ اخیرہ کر کے سلام پھیرے اور سجدہ سہو کرے (۲) اس حدیث میں اسکا ثبوت ہے عن عبد الله قال ان رسول الله [؟] صلى الظهر خمسا فقيل له ازيد في الصلوة؟ قال وما ذاك ؟قال صليت خمسا فسجد سجدتين بعد ما سلم (بخاری شریف ، باب اذ اصلی خمسا ص ۱۹۶، نمبر ۱۲۲۶ مسلم شریف ، باب من صلی خمسا اونحوه، ص۲۱۲، نمبر ۱۲۸۳٫۵۷۲) اس حدیث میں پانچ رکعت پڑھنے پر آپ نے سجدہ سہو کیا ہے۔
(742) And if he forgets the final sitting, he returns as long as he has not prostrated, and he prostrates for the delay of the obligatory sitting. There is an effect that if he stood a little, he should perform sajdah al-sahw, from this they prove that he does sajdah al-sahw, but the correct narration is the first. Translation: (742) And if he forgets the final sitting and stands, then as long as he has not prostrated, he sits, and he performs sajdah al-sahw due to the delay of the obligatory final sitting. Explanation: For example, he was performing the fard of Zuhr of four rak'ahs, then he forgot the final sitting, he did not sit at all, and stood for the fifth rak'ah, then as long as he has not prostrated the fifth rak'ah, it is for him that he should return and sit and perform sajdah al-sahw. Similarly for Fajr if he stood for the third rak'ah, and for Maghrib if he stood for the fourth rak'ah and left the final sitting, it is for him to return and sit in the final sitting. Because this sitting is obligatory. Reason: (1) In the chapter on description of prayer, issue no. 257, it has passed that the final sitting is obligatory; now when he left it and went to the fifth rak'ah, which becomes supererogatory, so he left the obligatory and entered the supererogatory; therefore, as long as he has not prostrated the fifth rak'ah and strengthened it, he should leave it and return to the final sitting, perform the final sitting, say salam, and perform sajdah al-sahw. (2) There is proof in this hadith: from Abdullah that the Messenger of Allah [؟] prayed Zuhr five rak'ahs, so it was said to him: 'Has the prayer been increased?' He said: 'What is that?' He said: 'You prayed five.' So he prostrated two prostrations after salam. (Bukhari, chapter on praying five, p. 196, no. 1226; Muslim, chapter on whoever prays five or similar, p. 212, no. 1283 [572]) In this hadith, upon praying five rak'ahs, he performed sajdah al-sahw.
Source pages p. 42

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling concerning a person who forgets the final sitting (qa'dah akhirah) in prayer and stands up. The ruling is from the chapter on Sajdah al-Sahw. The author states that if one stands after forgetting the final sitting, he must return to the sitting position as long as he has not prostrated the extra rak'ah. He then performs sajdah al-sahw for the delay of the obligatory sitting. The commentary explains the scenario with examples: for a four-rak'ah fard like Zuhr, if one stands for the fifth rak'ah without having sat for the final sitting, he must return before the prostration of the fifth rak'ah. Similarly for Fajr (three rak'ah) and Maghrib (four rak'ah). The reason given is that the final sitting is fard (obligatory), and by standing for an extra rak'ah, one is leaving a fard and engaging in a supererogatory act. The evidence is from the hadith where the Prophet (peace be upon him) prayed five rak'ah and performed sajdah al-sahw after salam. The text also mentions a difference in transmission: one effect says if he stood only slightly, he still performs sajdah al-sahw, but the correct narration is the first (that he returns). The relied upon position (mufta bihi) is that he returns before the additional rak'ah's prostration.

Key Terms
سجود السهو (sajdah al-sahw): Prostration performed to compensate for forgetfulness in prayer, either for omission of a wajib or for addition/error.
القعود الأخير (al-qu'ud al-akhir): The final sitting in prayer, which is a fard (obligatory) according to the Hanafi school.
فرض (fard): An obligatory act in prayer, omission of which invalidates the prayer unless compensated by sajdah al-sahw (if not deliberate).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person forgets the final sitting in Zuhr prayer and stands for the fifth rak'ah, but has not yet prostrated the fifth rak'ah, what should he do?
A) Continue the fifth rak'ah and perform sajdah al-sahw at the end.
B) Return to the sitting, perform the final sitting, say salam, and perform sajdah al-sahw.
C) Perform sajdah al-sahw immediately while standing.
D) Cancel the prayer and start over.

Key Takeaway
Forgetfulness of the final sitting requires immediate return before the extra rak'ah's prostration, followed by sajdah al-sahw.

Adding Supererogatory Rak'ahs When Prostration Already Performed
Ruling when one has already prostrated the extra rak'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a person prostrates an extra rak'ah in fard prayer and explain the corrective steps, citing the evidence from the Tabi'in.

Core Idea
Adding an extra rak'ah to fard converts it to nafl; you must complete a pair and repeat the fard.

This passage addresses a common forgetfulness error in prayer: standing for a fifth (or third) rak'ah and prostrating it. The Hanafi school provides a clear remedy: the fard transforms into nafl, and you must add another rak'ah to create an even number, then repeat the fard. The author also clarifies that there is no dislike in doing so during prohibited times, and no sajdah al-sahw is required. We will examine the ruling and its evidence from the sayings of the Tabi'in.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
When one prostrates an extra rak'ah (e.g., a fifth in Zuhr), the fard prayer becomes nafl. This is the core transformation.
The transformation occurs because the final sitting (fard) is omitted.
2
Determine the corrective actions
The person must add another rak'ah to make the total even (e.g., sixth in Zuhr, fourth in Fajr) to form pairs (shaf'), then repeat the fard prayer later.
Adding the extra rak'ah is wajib to avoid an incomplete nafl prayer.
3
Note the special exceptions
No sajdah al-sahw is performed according to the most correct view. Adding rak'ahs after Fajr and Asr is not makruh due to necessity.
The text uses 'على الصحيح' and 'في الاصح' to indicate the preferred positions.
4
Examine the evidence (dalil)
Two narrations from Hammad and Qatada (Tabi'in) in the Musannaf of Abd al-Razzaq support the ruling: add a sixth rak'ah and repeat the prayer.
Al-Hasan's narration mentions sajdah al-sahw, but the correct view omits it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۷۴۳) فان سجد صار فرضه نفلا وضم سادسة ان شاء ولو في العصر ورابعة في الفجر ولا كراهة فى الضم فيهما على الصحيح. ولا يسجد للسهو في الاصح
ترجمه : (۷۴۳) اور اگر سجدہ کر لیا ہوتو وہ فرض نماز نفل ہو جائے گی۔ اب اگر چاہے تو عصر وغیرہ میں چھٹی رکعت اور فجر میں چوتھی رکعت ملالے۔ اور صحیح روایت میں فجر اور عصر میں یہ ملانا مکروہ نہیں ہے، اور اصح روایت میں سجدہ سہو نہ کرے۔
تشریح : مثلا ظہر اور عصر میں پانچویں کا سجدہ کر لیا تو فرض کے ساتھ نفل ملالیا، اور قعدہ آخیرہ جو فرض ہے اس کو چھوڑ دیا ، اس لئے فرض نماز نفل بن جائے گی ، اس لئے ظہر میں چھٹی رکعت ملالے، اور فجر میں چوتھی رکعت ملالے تا کہ یہ شفع بن کر نماز مکمل ہو جائے ، اور ایک رکعت نماز باقی نہ رہے ۔ اس صورت میں اشکال یہ ہو گا کہ فجر کے بعد نفل نہیں ہے ، اسی طرح عصر کے بعد نفل نہیں ہے تو مزید رکعت ملا کر نفل کیسے بنائے ؟ تو مصنف فرما رہے ہیں کہ یہاں مجبوری کی صورت ہے اس لئے عصر کے بعد اور فجر کے بعد نفل بنانے میں کراہیت نہیں ہوگی، یہاں فرض نماز نفل بن گئی اس لئے فرض دوبارہ پڑھے۔
وجه : (ا) عن الثورى عن حماد قال اذا صلى الرجل خمسا و لم يجلس في الرابعة ، فانه يزيد السادسة ثم يسلم ثم يستأنف صلاته - (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب الرجل يصلي الظهر او العصر خمسا ، ج ثانی، ص۱۹۷، نمبر ۳۴۷۰) اس قول تابعی میں ہے کہ چھٹی رکعت ملائے اور نماز دوبارہ پڑھے۔ (۲) عن قتادة في رجل صلى الظهر خمسا قال يزيد اليها ركعة فتكون صلاة الظهر و رکعتین بعدها .... و کذالک ان صلی المغرب اربعا صلى اليها ركعة خامسة فتكون ركعتان تطوعا . قال معمر و اخبرنى من سمع الحسن يقول في هذا كله يسجد سجدتي السهو الى وهمه ـ (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب الرجل یصلی الظهر او العصر خمسا ، ج ثانی ، ص ۱۹۶، نمبر ۳۴۶۹) اس قول تابعی میں ہے کہ ایک رکعت اور ملالے تا کہ وہ نفل ہو جائے۔
(743) And if he prostrated, his fard becomes nafl, and he adds a sixth (rak'ah) if he wishes, even in Asr, and a fourth in Fajr, and there is no dislike in adding in these two according to the correct view. And he does not perform sajdah al-sahw according to the most correct view. Translation: (743) And if he has already prostrated, then that fard prayer becomes nafl. Now if he wishes, he may add a sixth rak'ah in Asr and similar, and a fourth rak'ah in Fajr. And according to the correct narration, there is no dislike in adding in Fajr and Asr, and according to the most correct narration, he does not perform sajdah al-sahw. Explanation: For example, in Zuhr and Asr, he prostrated the fifth, so he added a nafl to the fard, and he left the final sitting, which is fard, so the fard prayer becomes nafl. Therefore, he should add a sixth rak'ah in Zuhr, and a fourth rak'ah in Fajr, so that these become a pair (shaf') and the prayer is completed, and no single rak'ah remains. In this case, there is an issue: there are no nafl after Fajr and Asr, so how can he make it nafl by adding rak'ahs? The author says that this is a case of necessity, so there is no dislike in making it nafl after Asr and Fajr; here the fard has become nafl, so he should repeat the fard. Evidence: (1) From al-Thawri from Hammad: 'If a man prays five and does not sit in the fourth, then he adds a sixth, then says salam, then he repeats his prayer.' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, chapter on the man who prays Zuhr or Asr five, vol. 2, p. 197, no. 3470) In this saying of a Tabi'i, he adds a sixth rak'ah and repeats the prayer. (2) From Qatada concerning a man who prayed Zuhr five: 'He adds a rak'ah to it, then it becomes the prayer of Zuhr and two rak'ahs after it... Similarly, if he prayed Maghrib four, he adds a fifth rak'ah, then it becomes two rak'ahs of tatawwu'.' Ma'mar said: 'Someone informed me that he heard al-Hasan say in all this: he prostrates two prostrations of sahw due to his doubt.' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, chapter on the man who prays Zuhr or Asr five, vol. 2, p. 196, no. 3469) In this saying of a Tabi'i, he adds a rak'ah so that it becomes nafl.
Source pages p. 42

Commentary
This passage discusses the scenario where a person forgets the final sitting and stands for an extra rak'ah, but goes ahead and prostrates that extra rak'ah. In this case, the original fard prayer becomes supererogatory (nafl). To avoid having an odd number of rak'ahs, the person should add another rak'ah to complete a pair: for a four-rak'ah fard like Zuhr or Asr, he adds a sixth rak'ah (making three pairs); for Fajr, he adds a fourth rak'ah (making two pairs). The author states that there is no dislike (karahah) in adding these extra rak'ahs even during times when nafl is usually discouraged (after Fajr and Asr) because it is a case of necessity. Furthermore, according to the most correct narration, he does not perform sajdah al-sahw because the prayer has been transformed. The evidence comes from two sayings of the Tabi'in (Hammad and Qatada) recorded in the Musannaf of Abd al-Razzaq, which support the action of adding a sixth rak'ah and then repeating the fard, as well as the opinion of al-Hasan about performing sajdah al-sahw due to doubt.

Key Terms
نفل (nafl): Supererogatory prayer, voluntary. In this context, the original fard prayer is transformed into nafl due to the addition of an extra rak'ah.
شفع (shaf'): A pair of rak'ahs. The recommended unit for supererogatory prayers. In this ruling, the extra rak'ahs are added to make even pairs.
مکروہ (makruh): Disliked. The passage clarifies that adding extra rak'ahs after Fajr and Asr in this situation is not makruh due to necessity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

When Final Sitting Is Performed Before Standing
Ruling for standing after final sitting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two scenarios when one stands after the final sitting and apply the correct remedy: returning without repeating tashahhud, or adding an extra rak'ah and performing sajdah al-sahw.

Core Idea
Standing after final sitting does not invalidate the fard; the remedy depends on whether the extra rak'ah was prostrated.

In this lesson, we examine the ruling when a person performs the final sitting (qa'da akhir) but then stands up, mistakenly thinking the prayer is longer. The Hanafi school provides a clear remedy that preserves the validity of the fard prayer. The key distinction is whether the extra rak'ah's prostration has occurred, which determines whether the worshipper simply returns to sitting or adds another rak'ah to complete a supererogatory pair.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
The worshipper has performed the final sitting (a fard pillar) and then stands up, intending to add an extra rak'ah.
The final sitting is already completed, so the fard is effectively finished.
2
Determine if the extra rak'ah's prostration occurred
Check whether the worshipper has prostrated in the fifth rak'ah. This is the decisive factor.
If no prostration, the extra rak'ah is incomplete.
3
Apply the remedy for no prostration
If no prostration, the worshipper returns to sitting, says salam, and performs sajdah al-sahw. He does not repeat the tashahhud because it was already recited.
Returning is wajib, and sajdah al-sahw compensates the standing error.
4
Apply the remedy for prostration occurred
If prostration occurred, the worshipper adds a sixth rak'ah to make the two extra rak'ahs a supererogatory pair (nafl), then performs sajdah al-sahw. The original fard remains valid because the final sitting was performed.
Adding a sixth rak'ah is necessary to complete the nafl pair; the sajdah al-sahw corrects the unintended addition.
5
Note the evidence
This ruling is based on the statement of a Tabi'i (Hammad or Qatada), not a direct hadith. It is accepted in the Hanafi school as a sound basis.
Other schools may have different rulings due to differing views on the status of the final sitting.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۷۴۴) وان قعد الاخير ثم قام عاد و سلّم من غير اعادة التشهد فان سجد لم يبطل فرضه وضم اليها اخرى لتـصـيـر الزائدتان له نافلة وسجد للسهو
ترجمه : ( ۷۴۴ ) اور اگر قعدہ آخیرہ کیا پھر کھڑا ہوا ہوتو واپس لوٹے اور سلام پھیرے بغیر تشھد لوٹائے ، پس اگر سجدہ کیا ہوتو اس تو کا فرض باطل نہیں ہوگا ، اور اس کی طرف دوسری رکعت ملالے تا کہ یہ زائد رکعتیں نفل بن جائے اور سجدہ سہو کرے۔ تشریح : قعدہ آخیرہ میں بیٹھ چکا ہے، اب دو صورتیں ہیں [1] ایک یہ کہ پانچویں رکعت کا سجدہ نہیں کیا ہے تو واپس لوٹ جائے اور بیٹھ کر سلام کرے، اور سجدہ سہو کر لے، اور پہلی تشہد کو لوٹانے کی ضرورت نہیں ہے، کیونکہ ایک مرتبہ پڑھ چکا ہے ۔ [۲] دوسری صورت یہ ہے کہ پانچویں رکعت کا سجدہ کر لیا تو چھٹی رکعت ملالے، یہ دونوں رکعتیں نفل بن جائیں گیں ، اور پہلی چار رکعت کے بعد قعدہ آخیرہ کیا ہے اس لئے فرض بھی پورا ہو گیا، اب سجدہ سہو کر لے نماز ہو جائے گی ۔ دلیل پہلے قول تابعی گزر چکا ہے۔
(744) And if he performed the final sitting then stood, he returns and says salam without repeating the tashahhud; then if he prostrated, his fard is not invalidated, and he adds another rak'ah to it so that the two extra become nafl for him, and he performs sajdah al-sahw. Translation: (744) And if he performed the final sitting and then stood, he should return and say salam without repeating the tashahhud. Then if he has prostrated, his fard is not invalidated, and he adds another rak'ah to it so that the extra two rak'ahs become nafl, and he performs sajdah al-sahw. Explanation: He has already sat in the final sitting; now there are two scenarios: [1] If he has not prostrated the fifth rak'ah, he should return and sit and say salam, and perform sajdah al-sahw; he does not need to repeat the tashahhud because he already recited it once. [2] The second scenario: if he prostrated the fifth rak'ah, then he adds a sixth rak'ah; these two rak'ahs become nafl; and since he performed the final sitting after the first four rak'ahs, the fard is complete; now he performs sajdah al-sahw and the prayer is valid. The evidence is the previously mentioned saying of the Tabi'i.
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This passage handles the situation where a person remembers the final sitting and actually sits for it, but then stands up again. The ruling differentiates based on whether the extra rak'ah's prostration has occurred. If he has not prostrated, he simply returns to sitting and says salam, with no need to repeat tashahhud. If he has prostrated, it means he performed an additional rak'ah after the final sitting; in that case, he adds another rak'ah to make a pair, so the extra two become supererogatory, and the original fard remains valid because the final sitting was already performed. He then performs sajdah al-sahw. The evidence cited is the same as before from the Tabi'i statements (from lesson 743).

Key Terms
قعد أخير (qa'da akhir): Final sitting, which is fard. Here it means he actually performed it before standing up again.
تشهد (tashahhud): The testimony of faith recited during sitting. In this scenario, it does not need to be repeated when returning.

Sajdah al-Sahw in Supererogatory Pairs: Validity and Repetition
Ruling on building upon a nafl pair after sajdah al-sahw

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on building upon a nafl pair after sajdah al-sahw, and apply the rule that sajdah must be repeated at the end of the extended prayer.

Core Idea
Sajdah al-sahw signals the end of a prayer unit; attaching more rak'ahs after it is makruh but valid, requiring repeated sajdah.

In supererogatory (nafl) prayer, each pair of two rak'ahs is an independent unit. Performing sajdah al-sahw on the first pair effectively ends that prayer. This lesson examines the ruling if one then attaches another pair: is the prayer valid? Must sajdah be repeated? The Hanafi school provides a nuanced answer balancing validity and the sunnah placement of sajdah at the end.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
Determine the specific act: building upon a nafl pair after performing sajdah al-sahw on that pair. Identify the ruling: makruh tanzih (disliked) but valid if done, with the requirement to repeat sajdah al-sahw at the end.
2
Locate the Dalil
The author cites a hadith from Ata ibn Yasar showing that sajdah al-sahw should come at the end of the prayer. Identify the source as a hadith and note its zanni al-thubut status.
3
Trace the Wajh al-Dalalah
Explain how the hadith implies that sajdah al-sahw is a terminal action; performing it before the actual end of the prayer (when more rak'ahs are to come) contradicts its sunnah position, hence the dislike.
4
Note the Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf
The text mentions 'according to the chosen doctrine' indicating there were variant views among Hanafi authorities. Identify the mufta bihi position: repeat sajdah al-sahw after the fourth rak'ah.
Some earlier views may have considered the attachment invalid, but the preferred view maintains validity.
5
Evaluate the Tarjih
The tarjih authority is the 'chosen doctrine' (mukhtar). The ruling balances the general principle that prayer is not easily invalidated with the sunnah of sajdah placement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۷۴۵) ولو سجد للسهو في شفع التطوع لم يبن
ترجمه : (۷۴۵) اور نفل کی دورکعت پر اگر سجدہ سہو کیا ہوتو اس کے ساتھ دوسرا شفع ملانا اچھا نہیں مگر ملالیوے تو مختار مذہب کے موافق سجدہ سہو کا اعادہ کر لیوے۔
تشریح : نفل کی ہر دور کعت الگ الگ شفع ہے، یعنی دو رکعت پر ہی نفل پوری ہوگئی، اب کسی نے دورکعت پر سجدہ سہوکر لیا تو گویا کہ نماز ختم کر دی، اس لئے اگلی دورکعت کی بنا اس پر نہیں کرنی چاہئے لیکن اگر کر دیا نماز درست رہے گی ، البتہ چونکہ سجدہ سہو آخیر میں ہوتا ہے اس لئے چار رکعت کے بعد دوبارہ سجدہ سہو کر لے۔
وجه : (۱) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ سجدہ سہو آخیر میں ہونا چاہئے ۔ عن عطاء بن یسار .... قال ان النبي الله قال اذا شك أحدکم فی صلاته فان استيقن أن قد صلى ثلاثا فليقم فليتم ركعة بسجودها ثم يجلس فيتشهد
(745) And if he performed sajdah al-sahw in a pair of supererogatory prayer, he should not build upon it. Translation: (745) And if he performed sajdah al-sahw on a pair (two rak'ahs) of nafl, then it is not good to attach another pair to it; but if he attaches it, then according to the chosen doctrine, he should repeat the sajdah al-sahw. Explanation: Every two rak'ahs of nafl are a separate pair, meaning that nafl is completed with two rak'ahs. Now if someone performs sajdah al-sahw on two rak'ahs, it is as if he ended the prayer. Therefore, one should not attach the next two rak'ahs to it. But if he does attach, the prayer is still valid; however, since sajdah al-sahw should come at the end, after four rak'ahs he should perform sajdah al-sahw again. Evidence: (1) From this hadith it is learned that sajdah al-sahw should be at the end. From Ata ibn Yasar: ... that the Prophet said: 'If one of you has doubt in his prayer, and he is certain that he has prayed three, then he should stand and complete a rak'ah with its prostrations, then sit and recite tashahhud...'
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This passage addresses the specific case of supererogatory (nafl) prayer performed in pairs (shaf'). The default is that each pair of two rak'ahs is an independent unit. If one performs sajdah al-sahw at the end of the first pair, it indicates the completion of that prayer. Therefore, it is not recommended to attach another pair onto it. However, if someone does attach another pair, the prayer remains valid due to the overriding principle of validity. But because sajdah al-sahw should be performed at the very end of the prayer, one must repeat the sajdah al-sahw after the fourth rak'ah. The evidence is a hadith from Ata ibn Yasar suggesting that sajdah al-sahw is performed after the final sitting.

Key Terms
شفع التطوع (shaf' al-tatawwu'): A pair of supererogatory rak'ahs. Each pair is a complete unit of nafl prayer.
بنی (bana): To build upon; to attach the next pair of rak'ahs to the previous one, as if continuing the prayer.

Key Takeaway
Sajdah al-sahw indicates prayer completion, but if a second nafl pair is attached, the prayer remains valid and sajdah must be repeated at the end.

Standing After Final Tashahhud: Two Scenarios
Explains the ruling for one who stands after final tashahhud in obligatory prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling when a person stands after the final tashahhud and identify the correct action based on whether sajdah of the extra rak'ah was performed.

Core Idea
If you stand after final tashahhud, your prayer remains valid—add a sixth rak'ah if you already did sajdah, or return if you have not.

Have you ever forgotten whether you finished your prayer and stood up for an extra rak'ah? The classical Hanafi texts address this precise situation. This lesson unpacks the ruling from a concise passage that provides a practical remedy, showing that the prayer is not invalidated but requires a specific correction depending on how far you went into the extra rak'ah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that the act is standing after the final tashahhud in an obligatory prayer. The ruling provides two scenarios based on whether the sajdah of the extra rak'ah was performed.
The final tashahhud (qa'dah akhir) is wajib in the Hanafi school.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is from the sayings of the tabi'un (Hammad and Qatada) recorded in Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq. In the Hanafi school, such statements (qawl sahabi) are considered a valid evidence (dalil) for deriving rulings.
The text cites two narrations: one from Hammad about adding a sixth rak'ah, and another from Qatada about adjusting the prayer to make extra rak'ahs nafl.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The narrations directly prescribe specific actions: if one prays five without sitting in the fourth, add a sixth; if one prays five and sits in the fourth, the five become four obligatory plus one extra? Actually the text says for Maghrib, add a fifth to make a supererogatory pair. The Hanafi jurists derive from these that the prayer remains valid and the extra rak'ahs can be converted to nafl by pairing them.
The key point: the prayer is not nullified; it is corrected by adding a matching rak'ah.
4
Apply the ruling to the two scenarios
Scenario 1: If the person has not yet performed the sajdah of the extra rak'ah, he should immediately sit back, say salam, and perform sajdah al-sahw. Scenario 2: If he has performed the sajdah, he must add another rak'ah to make a pair of extra rak'ahs (nafl), then complete the prayer with sajdah al-sahw.
The tashahhud is not repeated because it was already recited in the final sitting.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
This ruling is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in the Hanafi school. Other schools may have different remedies, but the Hanafi view preserves the prayer's validity and recommends a practical correction.
The authority_weight is zahir_riwayah, as it appears in the core texts.

وجه : (ا) عن الثورى عن حماد قال اذا صلى الرجل خمسا و لم يجلس في الرابعة ، فانه يزيد السادسة ثم يسلم ثم يستأنف صلاته - (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب الرجل يصلي الظهر او العصر خمسا ، ج ثانی، ص۱۹۷، نمبر ۳۴۷۰) اس قول تابعی میں ہے کہ چھٹی رکعت ملائے اور نماز دوبارہ پڑھے۔ (۲) عن قتادة في رجل صلى الظهر خمسا قال يزيد اليها ركعة فتكون صلاة الظهر و رکعتین بعدها .... و کذالک ان صلی المغرب اربعا صلى اليها ركعة خامسة فتكون ركعتان تطوعا . قال معمر و اخبرنى من سمع الحسن يقول في هذا كله يسجد سجدتي السهو الى وهمه ـ ( مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب الرجل یصلی الظهر او العصر خمسا ، ج ثانی ، ص ۱۹۶، نمبر ۳۴۶۹) اس قول تابعی میں ہے کہ ایک رکعت اور ملالے تا کہ وہ فل ہو جائے۔ ترجمه : ( ۷۴۴ ) اور اگر قعدہ آخیرہ کیا پھر کھڑا ہوا ہوتو واپس لوٹے اور سلام پھیرے بغیر تشھد لوٹائے ، پس اگر سجدہ کیا ہوتو اس تو کا فرض باطل نہیں ہوگا ، اور اس کی طرف دوسری رکعت ملالے تا کہ یہ زائد رکعتیں نفل بن جائے اور سجدہ سہو کرے۔ تشریح : قعدہ آخیرہ میں بیٹھ چکا ہے، اب دو صورتیں ہیں [1] ایک یہ کہ پانچویں رکعت کا سجدہ نہیں کیا ہے تو واپس لوٹ جائے اور بیٹھ کر سلام کرے، اور سجدہ سہو کر لے، اور پہلی تشہد کو لوٹانے کی ضرورت نہیں ہے، کیونکہ ایک مرتبہ پڑھ چکا ہے ۔ [۲] دوسری صورت یہ ہے کہ پانچویں رکعت کا سجدہ کر لیا تو چھٹی رکعت ملالے، یہ دونوں رکعتیں نفل بن جائیں گیں ، اور پہلی چار رکعت کے بعد قعدہ آخیرہ کیا ہے اس لئے فرض بھی پورا ہو گیا، اب سجدہ سہو کر لے نماز ہو جائے گی ۔ دلیل پہلے قول تابعی گزر چکا ہے۔
(744) And if he performed the final sitting then stood up, he should return and perform salam without repeating the tashahhud. If he performed sajdah (of the extra rak'ah), his obligatory prayer is not invalidated, and he should add another rak'ah to it so that the two extra rak'ahs become nafl for him, and he performs sajdah al-sahw. Proof: (1) From al-Thawri from Hammad: 'If a man prays five (rak'ahs) and does not sit in the fourth, he should add a sixth, then say salam, then start his prayer anew.' (2) From Qatada regarding a man who prayed Zuhr as five rak'ahs: 'He adds a rak'ah to it, making it Zuhr and two rak'ahs after it... Similarly, if he prayed Maghrib as four, he adds a fifth rak'ah, making it a supererogatory pair.' And Ma'mar said: 'Al-Hasan said in all this: He performs two prostrations of forgetfulness.' Translation: (744) And if he performed the final sitting then stood up, he should return and perform salam without repeating the tashahhud. So if he did sajdah, his obligatory prayer is not invalidated, and he should add another rak'ah to it so that these extra rak'ahs become nafl for him, and he performs sajdah al-sahw. Explanation: ...
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It addresses the case of a person who, after performing the final tashahhud (qa'dah akhir) in an obligatory prayer, stands up for an additional rak'ah. The ruling provides two scenarios based on whether he has performed the sajdah of the extra rak'ah. If he has not performed sajdah, he returns to sitting and says salam without repeating tashahhud, and performs sajdah al-sahw. If he has performed sajdah, he adds another rak'ah to make a total of six (if originally four) or five (if originally three) so that the two extra rak'ahs become nafl (supererogatory). He then performs sajdah al-sahw. The proof is from the sayings of tabi'un (followers) Hammad and Qatada, as recorded in Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, supporting the practice of adding a sixth rak'ah when five are prayed without sitting in the fourth. The explanation clarifies that if sajdah is done after standing, the prayer is not invalidated; the extra rak'ahs become nafl, and sajdah al-sahw is performed at the end.

Key Terms
قعد الأخير (qa'dah akhir): The final sitting in prayer, including tashahhud and salawat, after which the prayer ends with salam.
سجود السهو (sujud al-sahw): Two prostrations performed to compensate for forgetfulness in prayer, before salam after completing the tashahhud.
تشهد (tashahhud): The recitation 'al-tahiyyatu lillah...' in the final sitting.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Sajdah al-Sahw in Nafl and Adding Another Pair
Ruling with proof about sajdah al-sahw in nafl prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when sajdah al-sahw is performed in nafl prayer and explain the consequence of adding another pair, citing the Hanafi proof.

Core Idea
Sajdah al-sahw ends the current pair in nafl; adding another pair requires repeating sajdah at the end.

Prayers in Islam have detailed rulings regarding forgetfulness (sahw). This lesson examines a specific scenario in nafl (supererogatory) prayers: what happens if someone performs sajdah al-sahw after the first two rak'ahs and then wishes to add another two rak'ahs? The Hanafi school provides a clear ruling based on the principle that sajdah al-sahw should be performed at the very end of the prayer. You will learn the legal classification and the practical steps to follow.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine the act being discussed: performing sajdah al-sahw in a pair (shaf') of nafl prayer, and then the issue of adding another pair. The ruling is that it is disliked (makruh tanzihi) to add another pair, but if done, the prayer remains valid.
Note: The ruling is specific to nafl prayer where each pair is independent.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is from the hadith of Imran bin Husain (RA) where the Prophet (SAW) performed sujud al-sahw after salam, indicating that sajdah should be at the end.
The hadith is found in Muslim, Bukhari, Abu Dawood, etc.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
From the hadith, the wajh al-dalalah (point of evidence) is that sujud al-sahw is performed after the final salam, not in the middle. Therefore, if sajdah is done in the middle of nafl (after two rak'ahs), it must be repeated at the end if the prayer is extended.
This demonstrates the Hanafi principle that sajdah al-sahw is a concluding act.
4
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Consider a person praying four rak'ahs of nafl. After two rak'ahs, he performs sajdah al-sahw. He then stands up and prays two more rak'ahs. According to the ruling, he must repeat sajdah al-sahw after the four rak'ahs.
The prayer is valid, but repeating sajdah is necessary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۷۴۵) ولو سجد للسهو في شفع التطوع لم يبن بنانے میں کراہیت نہیں ہوگی، یہاں فرض نماز نفل بن گئی اس لئے فرض دوبارہ پڑھے۔ 
ترجمه : (۷۴۵) اور نفل کی دورکعت پر اگر سجدہ سہو کیا ہوتو اس کے ساتھ دوسرا شفع ملانا اچھا نہیں مگر ملالیوے تو مختار مذہب کے موافق سجدہ سہو کا اعادہ کر لیوے۔ تشریح : نفل کی ہر دور کعت الگ الگ شفع ہے، یعنی دو رکعت پر ہی نفل پوری ہوگئی، اب کسی نے دورکعت پر سجدہ سہوکر لیا تو گویا کہ نماز ختم کر دی، اس لئے اگلی دورکعت کی بنا اس پر نہیں کرنی چاہئے لیکن اگر کر دیا نماز درست رہے گی ، البتہ چونکہ سجدہ سہو آخیر میں ہوتا ہے اس لئے چار رکعت کے بعد دوبارہ سجدہ سہو کر لے۔ وجه : (۱) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ سجدہ سہو آخیر میں ہونا چاہئے ۔ 
شفعا آخر عـلـيـه استحبابا فان بنی اعاد سجود السهو في المختار (۷۴) ولو سلم من عليه سهو ،فاذا فرغ فلم يبق الا ان يسلم فليسجد سجدتين و هو جالس ثم يسلم ۔ (ابوداود شریف، باب اذ اشک فی النین و الثلاث من قال بلقی الشک ،ص ۱۵۶، نمبر ۱۰۲۷) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ سلام کے علاوہ کوئی چیز باقی نہ رہے تو سجدہ سہو کرے۔(۲) حدیث یہ ہے عن عمران بن حصين قال سلم رسول الله عله فى ثلاث ركعات من العصر ثم قام فدخل الحجرة فقام رجل بسيط اليدين فقال اقصرت الصلوة يا رسول الله فخرج مغضبا فصلى الركعة التي كان ترك ثم سلم ثم سجد سجدتي السهو ثم سلم (مسلم شریف، باب فصل من ترک الرکعتین اونحوها فليتم مابقی د یسجد سجدتین بعد التسلیم، ص ۲۱۴ نمبر ۱۲۹۴٫۵۷۴ر بخاری شریف ، باب صل یا خذ الامام اذا شک بقول الناس ،ص ۱۹، نمبر ۷۱۴ ترندی شریف ، باب ماجاء فی الامام تنبض فی الرکعتین ناسیا ص ۸۳ نمبر ۱۳۶۴ ابوداؤد شریف ، باب السهو فی السجدتین، ص ۱۵۳ نمبر ۱۰۱۸ اس باب کی آخری حدیث ہے ) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ سلام کیا پھر سجدہ سہو کیا پھر سلام کیا۔ جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ سجدہ نماز کے آخیر میں ہو۔ لغت شفع : کا معنی ہے جوڑواں ، دورکعت کے مجموعے کو شفع ، کہتے ہیں۔ بنی بنا کرے۔
(745) And if he performed sajdah al-sahw in a pair of supererogatory prayer, he should not build upon it in terms of [؟] there is no dislike, here the obligatory prayer became nafl so he should repeat the obligatory prayer. Translation: (745) And if one performed sajdah al-sahw on a pair of nafl, it is not good to add another pair to it, but if he adds, according to the preferred school, he should repeat sajdah al-sahw. Explanation: Each pair of nafl is separate, meaning the nafl is completed with two rak'ahs. If someone performed sajdah al-sahw after two rak'ahs, it is as if he ended the prayer, so he should not build the next pair upon it. But if he does, the prayer is valid; however, since sajdah al-sahw should be at the end, after four rak'ahs he should repeat sajdah al-sahw. Proof: This hadith shows that sajdah al-sahw should be at the end. [Hadith text: 'If you are in doubt...'], and the hadith of Imran bin Husain: The Prophet (SAW) performed salam after three rak'ahs of Asr... then he performed the missed rak'ah, then salam, then sujud al-sahw, then salam. This shows that sajdah is at the end of the prayer. Lexicon: shaf' means pair; a set of two rak'ahs is called shaf'. Bana means he built.
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling regarding sajdah al-sahw in nafl prayer. The text states that if one performs sajdah al-sahw in the first two rak'ahs (shaf') of a nafl prayer, it is disliked (makruh) to add another pair (shaf') because the nafl is complete with the first pair. However, if one does add another pair, the prayer is valid but the sajdah al-sahw must be repeated at the end of the prayer (after the four rak'ahs) because sajdah al-sahw should be at the very end of the prayer. The proof is taken from the hadith of the Prophet (SAW) where he corrected his forgetfulness after salam by performing sujud al-sahw, indicating that sujud al-sahw is performed at the conclusion of the prayer. The explanation clarifies that each two-rak'ah unit in nafl is independent, and sajdah al-sahw effectively ends that unit. Therefore, joining another unit after sajdah al-sahw requires repeating the sajdah at the end of the entire prayer.

Key Terms
شفع (shaf'): A pair, specifically a set of two rak'ahs in prayer.
بنى (bana): To build upon; i.e., to join another pair (shaf') to the one that already had sajdah al-sahw performed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If someone performs sajdah al-sahw after the first two rak'ahs of a nafl prayer and then adds another two rak'ahs, what should he do?
A) The prayer becomes invalid and must be repeated.
B) It is valid, but he must perform sajdah al-sahw again at the end of the four rak'ahs.
C) He should not add another pair; it is forbidden.
D) He must repeat the first pair.

Key Takeaway
In nafl prayer, sajdah al-sahw performed after a pair ends that unit; adding another pair is valid but requires repeating sajdah at the end.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
6 min
Joining an Imam After Salam Due to Forgetfulness
Ruling on iqtida after salam due to sajdah al-sahw

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition under which joining (iqtida) an imam who has performed salam due to sajdah al-sahw is valid and apply the hadith proof to explain why.

Core Idea
A salam due to forgetfulness is not final until sajdah al-sahw is performed — joining during that interval is valid.

This lesson examines a specific scenario in congregational prayer: an imam who has forgetfulness (sajdah al-sahw due) says salam to the right as a prelude to performing sajdah al-sahw. At that moment, a person joins the congregation. Is his prayer valid? The answer depends on whether the imam actually performs the sajdah. This ruling illustrates the Hanafi principle that the salam that releases prayer is not always the first salam; an intermediate salam can be superseded by subsequent sajdah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is iqtida (joining) behind an imam who has performed a salam due to sajdah al-sahw. The ruling is that the iqtida is valid only if the imam performs the sajdah al-sahw after that salam. If he does not, the iqtida is invalid (batil).
2
Locate the dalil
The proof cited is the hadith of Abu Sa'id: 'The key to prayer is purification, its prohibition is takbir, and its release is salam.' This establishes that salam ends the prayer.
The hadith is from Tirmidhi and Abu Dawood.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith states that salam is the 'tahlil' (release) of prayer. Therefore, a salam generally ends the prayer. However, a salam uttered for the purpose of sajdah al-sahw is not the final release if the sajdah follows; it is an intermediate salam. If the sajdah is omitted, that salam becomes final.
This is a Hanafi interpretation based on the sunnah practice of the Prophet.
4
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah)
If the imam performs sajdah al-sahw after the first salam, the prayer continues, so the joining is valid. If no sajdah, the prayer ended with that salam, so the follower's prayer is invalid.
The follower must ensure he joined while the imam is still in prayer.
5
State the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is that iqtida is sahih if the imam performs sajdah al-sahw, and batil otherwise.
This is from Zahir al-Riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۷۴۶) ولو سلم من عليه سهو فاذا فرغ فلم يبق الا ان يسلم فليسجد سجدتين و هو جالس ثم يسلم 
ترجمه : (۷۴۶) اور اگر امام سہو والے نے سلام پھیرا پھر اس کے ساتھ دوسرے نے اقتدا کی تو اگر امام سجدہ سہو کرے تو اقتدا صحیح ہے، اور اگر سجدہ نہ کرے تو صحیح نہیں۔ 
تشریح : یہ مسئلہ اس اصول پر ہے کہ سجدہ سہو سے پہلے جو دائیں جانب سلام پھیرتے ہیں، اگر اس کے بعد سجدہ کرلیا تو یہ سلام انقطاع کا نہیں ہوگا بلکہ بعد والاسلام انقطاع کا ہوگا ، اور اگر سجدہ سہونہیں کیا تو یہ سلام انقطاع کا ہوگا اور اسی پر نماز ختم ہو جائے گی ۔ صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ امام پر سجدہ سہو تھا اس لئے اس نے سجدہ سہو کے لئے سلام پھیرا، اور اس وقت کسی نے اس کی اقتداء کی۔ پس اگر اس کے بعد امام نے سجدہ سہو کیا تو اس کی اقتداء درست ہوگی ، اور سجدہ سہو نہیں کیا تو اس کی اقتداء درست نہیں ہوگی۔ وجه : (۱) کیونکہ اس سلام کے بعد سجدہ نہیں کیا تو گویا کہ نماز ختم ہو گئی تب آدمی نے اس کی اقتداء کی ہے اس لئے اس کی اقتداء درست نہیں ہوئی ، اور اگر سجدہ سہو کیا تو یہ سلام درمیان میں ہو گیا اور گویا کہ ابھی نماز باقی ہے اس لئے آنے والے کی اقتداء درست ہے۔ (۲) حدیث میں ہے کہ سلام نماز ختم کر دیتا ہے ۔ عن ابی سعید قال قال رسول الله مفتاح الصلوة الطهور وتـحـريـمـهـا الـتـكـبـيـر وتحليلها التسليم ولاصلوة لمن لم يقرأ بالحمد وسورة في فريضة او غيرها. (ترندی شریف، باب ماجاء فی تحریم الصلوۃ و تحلیلها ص ۵۵ نمبر ۲۳۸ رابو داؤد شریف، باب الامام يحدث بعد ما يرفع رأسه من آخر ركعته ص ۹۸ نمبر ۶۱۸) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ سلام نماز کو حلال کر دیتا ہے، یعنی نماز کو ختم کر دیتا ہے۔
(746) And if one who has forgetfulness (due to sajdah al-sahw) performs salam, and when he finishes and nothing remains except to say salam, he should perform two prostrations while sitting, then say salam. Translation: (746) And if the imam who has sajdah al-sahw performs salam, and then someone joins him in iqtida, then if the imam performs sajdah al-sahw, the iqtida is valid; if he does not perform sajdah, it is not valid. Explanation: This ruling is based on the principle that the first salam (to the right) before sajdah al-sahw is not the final closing salam if sajdah is performed afterward; the final closing is the salam after sajdah. If sajdah is not performed, the first salam is the final closing and ends the prayer. So, if the imam had sajdah al-sahw due, he performed salam for the purpose of sajdah. If someone joins after that salam and the imam subsequently performs sajdah al-sahw, the iqtida is valid because the prayer is still ongoing. If the imam does not perform sajdah, the prayer ended with that first salam, so iqtida is invalid. Proof: (1) Because if no sajdah after that salam, the prayer is ended; if sajdah is performed, the salam was intermediate. (2) The hadith: 'The key to prayer is purification, its prohibition is takbir, and its release is salam.'
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage provides a ruling on the validity of joining (iqtida) an imam who, due to forgetfulness, has performed an intermediate salam intending to perform sajdah al-sahw. The ruling hinges on whether the imam actually performs the sajdah al-sahw after that salam. If he does, the iqtida is valid because the prayer is not yet complete; the intermediate salam does not sever the prayer. If he does not perform sajdah, that salam becomes the final closing salam, thus the prayer ended and any attempt to join is invalid. The proof includes a hadith from Abu Sa'id stating that the salam (takbir) is what makes the prayer permissible (i.e., ends it). Therefore, the first salam without sajdah ends the prayer, while the first salam followed by sajdah is not the final release.

Key Terms
اقتداء (iqtida'): Following an imam in congregational prayer; joining the prayer behind the imam.
تحليلها التسليم (tahliluha al-taslim): The release of prayer is the salam; meaning the salam ends the state of prayer and makes lawful what was forbidden during prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
An imam who has sajdah al-sahw due says salam to the right, and someone joins the congregation at that moment. The imam then performs sajdah al-sahw. What is the ruling on the follower's prayer according to the Hanafi school?
A) It is invalid because the first salam ended the prayer.
B) It is valid because the sajdah al-sahw continues the prayer.
C) It is valid only if the follower intended to pray nafl.
D) It is invalid because joining after salam is never allowed.

Key Takeaway
The validity of iqtida after an imam's salam due to forgetfulness depends on whether the imam performs sajdah al-sahw; if yes, the prayer continues and joining is valid; if not, the prayer ended and joining is invalid.
